# Anya — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF)

**Compilation date:** post-Sunnydale collapse, 2003. **Subject status:** deceased, Sunnydale crater event, killed in action defending non-affiliated civilians and combatants during the final First Evil engagement. **File priority:** retained at maximum despite KIA status; subject is one of the only entities in the active intelligence corpus to have crossed the human/non-human ontological boundary twice in both directions and survived long enough in each state to generate behavioral baseline. The longitudinal value of the file exceeds its operational value.

---

## Bottom Line

The subject is, and has always been, a literal-minded, concretely-cognizant, socially-atypical young woman from a small Scandinavian agricultural village in the late ninth century, who at roughly age twenty experienced a single intimate-betrayal trauma she was developmentally and neurologically unequipped to metabolize, and who has spent every subsequent moment of her eleven-hundred-and-some-odd-year existence inside one or another structural defense against ever having to feel that trauma again. The demon is the defense. The vengeance career is the defense. The capitalism is the defense. The bluntness is the defense. The transactional framing of love is the defense. Strip the defenses and what remains is a woman of approximately twenty subjective years of social experience — most of it acquired under duress, in a foreign body, in a foreign century — who is trying, with insufficient tools and remarkable courage, to learn how to belong to a category of beings she stopped being before the printing press was invented.

She is not, in any clinically meaningful sense, a demon who became human. She is a human being who underwent an extended occupational and somatic dissociation, returned to baseline, and died still in the early stages of integration.

---

## The Through-Line

A single sentence will hold the entire file: *the subject orients her whole existence around the question of which category she belongs to and what the rules of that category are, because the one time she did not ask that question she was destroyed by the answer.*

Every era documented in §1 is a re-instantiation of this orientation.

- As **Aud**, she is a villager who has been told her name means "odd" and who has visibly accepted this as a category — she organizes her behavior (rabbit-breeding, gift-giving, literal speech) around being the village's known eccentric. She is not in distress about it. She has placed herself.
- As **Anyanka**, she is a Patron Saint with a title, a patron (D'Hoffryn), a guild (the vengeance demons), a uniform (the amulet, the vein-y face), a workflow (wish, contract, execution), and a quantitative output (over a thousand years of completed contracts, catalogued with the affect of a tradeswoman counting inventory). She has been placed by D'Hoffryn, and she will reference this placement, unprompted, for the remainder of her existence.
- As **Anya**, in 1998, she does not know what category she belongs to. The behavioral record of the immediately following months — enrolling in a high school whose curriculum is irrelevant to her, fixating on the amulet, pivoting to Xander with the suddenness of someone selecting a new role from a small menu — is the behavior of a person frantically attempting to re-place herself. The relationship with Xander is, structurally, a category-assignment: *girlfriend*, then *fiancée*, with the precise terms of each escalation negotiated aloud.
- After **Hells Bells**, she does not know what category she belongs to. Within hours she has returned to the only other category she has ever held. The return is not a moral failure; it is a homing instinct.
- In **Selfless**, asked by Buffy what she wants, she requests her own death. Death is the last available category-assignment when no living one fits.
- In **Chosen**, she dies mid-quip defending a category (humanity) she has, by her own final statement, only just begun to suspect she might belong to.

The through-line is not vengeance, and it is not love, and it is not money. It is *placement*. Everything else is the local instrument by which placement is sought.

---

## The Core Wound and Its Maintenance

The **index event** is Olaf's infidelity, approximately 880 CE. The wound is not the infidelity itself; the wound is that the infidelity proved that the subject's pre-existing operating system — concrete, literal, contractual, taking stated terms at their stated meaning — did not work in the domain of human intimacy. She had entered the relationship with Olaf in good faith on the terms she understood the relationship to have. The terms were violated without her detection, recourse, or comprehension. The lesson she extracted, and has never since unlearned, is that *the contractual frame, scrupulously honored on her end, will be invisibly broken on the other end, and she will be the last to know.*

This is the wound. Everything in the file is its maintenance.

**Maintenance mechanism 1: pre-emption.** As Anyanka she does not enter contracts that can be broken without her knowing; the vengeance contract is binding by metaphysical fiat the moment the wish is uttered. She has built an entire occupational identity around the one form of contract that cannot be violated against her. This is not coincidence. It is the wound choosing its own armor.

**Maintenance mechanism 2: pre-emptive retaliation.** The Olaf transformation is, in retrospect, the template: when betrayed, do not grieve, do not negotiate — convert the betrayer into a thing that visibly displays the betrayal, so that no future party can be deceived as she was. Eleven hundred years of vengeance work is the industrialization of this single response. The Xander-altar return is the response firing again on identical input, eleven hundred years later, with the original force undiminished.

**Maintenance mechanism 3: hyper-explicit verbalization.** The famous bluntness — about money, sex, bodily functions, frequency of orgasms, anticipated mortality — is best read as the wound speaking. If she names everything aloud, if she insists on stating the terms in the most concrete possible form, then nothing can be invisibly violated. The chatter is not lack of social filter (or not only that). It is a forensic procedure run continuously against the possibility of another Olaf.

**Maintenance mechanism 4: monetization.** Money is the cleanest contract there is — quantitative, mutually verifiable, reversible only by visible theft. Her religious affect about capitalism, her on-screen cash-counting, her competence at the Magic Box's ledger, are the wound's preferred substitute domain: a form of exchange where she will never again be the one who did not know the terms were broken.

**Maintenance mechanism 5: the rabbits.** The leporiphobia is the wound's only somatic monument. The rabbits belonged to Aud, the pre-trauma self who took terms at face value and named the animals she fed. To encounter a rabbit is to encounter the woman she was before she learned the lesson. The phobia is severe and persistent because the lesson is severe and persistent; she cannot afford, neurologically, to revisit the self that did not yet know.

The wound is not healing across the record. What changes, very slowly, across S5–S7, is the subject's *capacity to tolerate the wound's presence without firing the full defense suite.* She can sit with Xander after the altar. She can sit with Buffy after Selfless. She can have a sexual encounter with Spike that is sad rather than retaliatory. She can die without a curse on her lips. This is not recovery; it is the beginning of recovery, arrested by combat death at approximately the four-year mark of treatment-equivalent exposure.

---

## What She Is, At The Deepest Level

Underneath the demon, underneath the bluntness, underneath the cash drawer, the subject is a person whose central, organizing, life-long unmet need is **to be known accurately by someone who will not leave**. Not loved — known. The distinction matters operationally. Love she has had, transactionally, in both demon and human form. Being known requires the other party to perceive her interior, and her interior is, by her own late-period admission ("I don't know who I am"), so unstable and so unwitnessed that she is not sure it exists in continuous form.

The relationship with Halfrek is the closest she comes. Halfrek knew her across both ontological states, did not require her to choose a category, and was killed by D'Hoffryn in punishment calibrated precisely to this fact. The relationship with Xander approached it and broke on it — he could not bear what he knew, which from her vantage was indistinguishable from not having known. The relationship with the late-period Scoobies is the substrate on which, had she lived, the need might have begun to be met.

The deepest layer is therefore not the vengeance demon and not the capitalist shopgirl. It is a young woman from a ninth-century village, sitting in the dark with a rabbit on her lap, asking — in a vocabulary she does not yet have — whether anyone in the world is going to see her and stay.

---

## Operational Summary

**Identifiers.** Presents under given name *Anya Christina Emmanuella Jenkins*; documented prior identities *Aud* (human, pre-880 CE) and *Anyanka* (vengeance demon, c. 880–1998, brief reversion 2002). The contraction "Anya" from "Anyanka" is itself diagnostic: she retained the demon-name's stem and shortened it to a humanized form, refusing both a return to Aud and a clean break from Anyanka. The current identity is a literal compromise formation between the two prior ones.

**Capabilities, residual (post-1998, human).** High working memory; high quantitative aptitude; fluent in an unknown but large number of languages acquired across the vengeance career, several of which surface contextually (Old Norse, demonic dialects, conversational competence in commerce-relevant tongues). Detailed procedural knowledge of vengeance metaphysics, demonic political structures, contract law in both demonic and mundane variants, and the workings of magical apparatus at the level of a long-practiced ritual technician. Competent if unenthusiastic in close combat; not a front-line operator. Bookkeeper, retail manager, ritual consultant.

**Capabilities, lost (post-1998).** Reality-altering wish fulfillment; teleportation; immortality; physical invulnerability; access to D'Hoffryn's court. Re-acquired briefly 2002; surrendered or stripped after Selfless. At time of death, fully mortal.

**Liabilities.** Pragmatic-language deficit; inability to read non-literal social cues without explicit coaching; catastrophic response to romantic abandonment; near-zero tolerance for being told she does not belong; specific phobia (rabbits, severe); preoccupation with mortality reaching the threshold of intrusive thought; tendency under acute stress to revert to pre-formed institutional identity (D'Hoffryn's court).

**Exploitation surface (for adversary modeling).** Highest-yield approaches in descending order: (1) staged public romantic humiliation, reliably triggering full regression; (2) offer of category-placement from any sufficiently authoritative source (D'Hoffryn-equivalent recruiter), reliably triggering at least consideration; (3) threats to bonded persons, reliably triggering self-sacrificial substitution; (4) explicit assertion that she is not really one of [whichever current in-group], reliably destabilizing decision-making for hours to days. Lowest-yield approaches: economic coercion (she will counter-bargain); intellectual challenge (she will engage and likely win on bounded problems); appeals to abstract loyalty (she does not parse them).

**Handling notes (for benevolent contact).** Speak in literal terms; state the rules of the interaction aloud at the outset; do not use idiom without translation; do not assume she has inferred context. Do not require her to perform emotional registers she has not yet acquired; she will attempt to comply and the attempt will be costly. Praise quantitatively where possible (she metabolizes numeric feedback better than verbal warmth). Do not joke about rabbits. Do not joke about her age. Do not, under any circumstance, leave the room in the middle of a stated commitment without flagging the departure; her central trauma is the silent breach of stated terms, and exits without notice will be coded against the original wound.

**Prognosis, had she lived.** Cautiously hopeful. The trajectory across S6–S7 shows authentic, if slow, acquisition of affect tolerance, humor as regulation, capacity for moral revision, and the beginnings of a continuous self-narrative. The integration was at perhaps year four of an estimated multi-decade course. Combat death at this stage forecloses the question.

**Final disposition.** Killed in action, *Chosen*, defending Andrew Wells and unnamed Potentials against Turok-Han during the Hellmouth collapse. Last recorded utterance, a quip. No body recovered. The file closes with the operational note that the subject, having spent eleven hundred years asking which category she belonged to, answered the question in the only way her cognitive architecture permitted: by standing, in the final available moment, with the people she had chosen, and dying in the posture of belonging to them.

The bottom line, restated for the cover sheet: *Subject was a traumatized neurodivergent ninth-century human woman who survived eleven hundred years as a weaponized occupational identity, returned to her original category in a body and century she did not recognize, taught herself most of the way back to personhood in four years, and was killed before she could finish.*


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

*Section scope: the earliest stratum of the subject's record, ending at the threshold of the Olaf rupture (c. late 870s CE). Source base is necessarily thin and almost entirely autobiographical — the subject is the only surviving witness to her own first century, and she is an unreliable narrator about it in specific, patterned ways noted below. Primary canonical sources: "The Wish" (3.09), "Doppelgangland" (3.16), "Triangle" (5.11), "Selfless" (7.05, including the flashback sequences set in Sjornjost), "Hells Bells" (6.16), "Once More, with Feeling" (6.07), and scattered asides across S4–S7.*

---

## 1. Birth, Naming, Place

The subject was born sometime in the early-to-mid 9th century CE in a small agrarian settlement she refers to as **Sjornjost** ("Selfless"). The setting visualized in canon is a Scandinavian village of perhaps a few dozen households — wood-and-thatch construction, communal hearth life, subsistence agriculture supplemented by small livestock. There is no surviving record of her parents, siblings, or extended kin; the subject never names them across five seasons of opportunity to do so, which is itself a datum. People who had functional childhood families generally mention them at least once across a thousand-year speech record. She does not. She mentions Olaf constantly; she mentions her rabbits; she mentions the village's response to her. The kin who would have raised her are conspicuously absent from her speech — either deceased early, emotionally negligible, or so painful that omission has become reflex. The dossier flags this as the first significant lacuna.

She is given the name **Aud**, which she herself translates, on more than one occasion and with no apparent self-pity, as meaning **"odd"** ("Selfless"). The detail is extraordinary and the file treats it as foundational. Whether the name was bestowed at birth or acquired later in childhood as a sobriquet that displaced an original given name is unrecoverable; the subject treats it as her true name from her earliest memory. Either way, the operative fact is the same: by the time she has language for self-reference, the word she uses for herself is the village's word for *not-like-us*. This is the ground floor of her self-concept, and every subsequent identity (Anyanka, Anya, Anyanka-redux, Anya-final) is built on a foundation that already encoded social rejection as identity.

She is read by canon as a young adult at the time of the Olaf incident — visualized in "Selfless" as a woman in her early-to-mid twenties — meaning her childhood and adolescence occupy roughly two decades of the 9th century for which the record is almost entirely indirect. We reconstruct from residue.

## 2. Family of Origin — Inference From Absence

The total absence of parental reference across her recorded life is, on close reading, structured rather than random. She references the *village* freely. She references *Olaf* freely. She references *the rabbits* freely. The household she grew up in is a blank.

Three readings, in descending order of parsimony:

1. **Early loss or distance.** Plague, raid, accident, or death in childbirth are statistically ordinary in a 9th-century Scandinavian settlement and would account for the absence without requiring elaborate trauma narrative. If she was orphaned young or raised by adults who did not function as primary attachments, the village's collective verdict on her ("odd") would have done the work of identity formation that parents normally do, which precisely fits the adult profile.
2. **Functional neglect.** The cognitive profile we observe in adulthood — concrete, literal, weak pragmatic-inference, intense circumscribed interests — would have presented in childhood as a child who did not pick up unspoken rules, who needed explicit instruction, and who would have been a disproportionate caregiving burden in a household with no concept of what we now call neurodivergence. A child like this in a 9th-century village is at high risk for being given over to peripheral roles, treated as a community oddity rather than a household member, and emotionally under-tended even by living parents.
3. **Active rejection.** Possible but not necessary; the subject's affect when discussing the village is bemused and slightly wounded, not the hot affect of someone fleeing remembered cruelty. The texture is closer to lifelong mild ostracism than to abuse.

The file's working hypothesis is a combination of (1) and (2): parents likely absent or peripheral; primary developmental environment a village that found her odd and treated her accordingly with neither violence nor warmth.

A note on the Olaf relationship as evidence of this: she partners with the **only man in the village who appears to find her endearing rather than peculiar** ("Selfless" flashbacks present Olaf as a large, jovial figure who responds to her oddness with affection). The intensity of her attachment to him, and the totality of her collapse when he proves unfaithful, is consistent with a person for whom Olaf was the *first* experience of being chosen rather than tolerated. People raised inside a warm family do not invest a single romantic relationship with the entire weight of their attachment system. People raised at the cool edge of one do.

## 3. The Childhood Environment — Sjornjost

The subject's village is small, agrarian, materially poor by any later standard, and tightly bound by reputation. Three structural features of such a community shape her formation:

- **No private life.** Everyone knows everyone's business. A child who is odd is *publicly* odd; a young woman whose husband strays is *publicly* humiliated. The thread that runs from "the village thought my rabbits were strange" to "my fiancé left me in front of every person I know" is a thread of *witnessed* shame. Every wound she takes in this period is taken in front of an audience. This will calcify into a lifelong sensitivity to public humiliation as the specific accelerant of catastrophic response.
- **Concrete economy.** Value is countable in livestock, grain, and barter. There is no monetary abstraction yet, no capitalism for her to be devoted to, but the *cognitive habit* of valuing in countable units is laid down here. The Magic Box ledgers of 2001 are continuous with the rabbit-counting of c. 870.
- **Animist-pagan worldview, pre-Christianization.** Sjornjost in the 860s–870s sits in or near the transitional zone of Scandinavian Christianization; her village reads as still pagan. Spirits, curses, transformations, and the trafficking of supernatural beings are part of the assumed furniture of the world. This matters: when D'Hoffryn appears to her after the Olaf incident, she does not respond with the shock a modern subject would; she responds as someone for whom this category of entity is *known*. Her recruitment was made possible in part by a cosmology that did not require her to disbelieve the recruiter.

## 4. The Rabbits — The First Circumscribed Interest

The single most documented behavior of her childhood-into-young-adulthood is her relationship with rabbits. The evidence is fragmentary but converges:

- She **bred them** ("Selfless").
- She **named them individually** ("Selfless"); the implication is that she could distinguish them, which is non-trivial and indicates sustained attention and pattern-discrimination directed at the animals.
- She **gave them as gifts** ("Selfless"), apparently as a sincere gesture of significance.
- The villagers **found this strange and reacted with confusion or mockery** — the gift-giving in particular reads in the flashbacks as a failed social transaction.
- Olaf, alone among the documented social field, **tolerated or appreciated** the rabbit-keeping.

This is a textbook circumscribed interest in the autism-spectrum sense: sustained, intense, individuated, and pursued without regard to the social legibility of the pursuit. Three downstream patterns originate here.

**First, the cognitive template.** She learns mastery through repetition, individuation, and counting. The rabbits are her first dataset. The vengeance contracts of the 880s–1990s and the Magic Box inventory of 2001 are continuations of the same competence: *take a population of discrete units, know each one, manage them carefully, take satisfaction in the bookkeeping.*

**Second, the social template.** She learns that her sincere offerings of value are received as strange. The "bunny gift" failure prefigures every later instance of her saying something genuinely meant and watching her interlocutors recoil — the wedding toast in "Hells Bells," the orgasm-frequency comments to Buffy ("Where the Wild Things Are"), the musical complaint about Xander ("Once More, with Feeling"). She does not learn from these later instances either, because the lesson would require her to retroactively pathologize her own most loving early behavior, which she cannot do.

**Third, the phobic kernel.** The leporiphobia of the 1998–2003 record ("Fear, Itself," "Once More, with Feeling," et al.) is the file's strongest piece of evidence for *what happened around the time of the Olaf rupture.* A child who loved and individually named rabbits does not become an adult terrified of them without an intervening event. The most parsimonious reconstruction is that the rabbits — or some specific rabbit or rabbits — were lost, killed, or had to be abandoned in the immediate aftermath of the Olaf incident and her departure from the village with D'Hoffryn. The phobia is the fossil of that loss, displaced from its true object (the village, the prior self, the capacity to love without consequence) onto the animal that became, in memory, the symbol of all three.

It is also worth noting what the phobia is *not*. It is not a fear of being bitten, of disease, or of any rational rabbit-related harm. It is a categorical aversion that activates at the *idea* of rabbits, including drawn ones, plush ones, and verbal mentions. This is the phenomenology of a *symbol* phobia, not an animal one. The rabbit, for her, points at something else.

## 5. Olaf — The First and Defining Attachment

The full discussion of Olaf properly belongs in Chronology II, but the childhood-section relevance is this: by the time we meet him in the "Selfless" flashbacks, he has been in her life long enough to be a fixture, and the affective tone suggests she has had no other significant romantic or peer attachment in the interim. We infer he entered her world somewhere in adolescence and remained the single organizing relational fact of her young adulthood. The texture of her dependence on him — the way she defers to his moods, the way she frames her domestic life around his presence, the way she experiences his infidelity not as a discrete wrong but as the unmaking of her world — is the texture of a person for whom this attachment is the *only* attachment that has ever worked.

That is a childhood diagnosis as much as an adult one. The single-point-of-failure attachment system she carries into the 880s, and which she will reconstitute precisely with Xander in 1999–2002, was set in childhood by the absence of redundant bonds.

## 6. Earliest Behavioral Patterns — A Catalogue

Reconstructing from the residue, the following patterns are documented or strongly inferable as present by late adolescence in Sjornjost:

- **Literal interpretation of language and ritual.** Stable across the entire 1,150-year record; the canon presents no era in which she was not literal. This is a constitutional trait, not an acquisition.
- **Concrete, countable cognition.** Demonstrated via the rabbit-counting; continuous with adult ledger behavior.
- **Sincere gift-giving received as inappropriate.** First documented with the rabbits; the schema "I offer what I value and am met with confusion" is laid down before age twenty.
- **Identity-as-given-by-others.** The name *Aud* operates as the village's verdict installed as her self-reference. She does not appear to have resisted it; she internalizes it.
- **Tolerated ostracism as baseline.** Her affect about her own oddness, even in adulthood, is matter-of-fact rather than wounded. This is the affect of someone who has had a *long time* to make peace with mild rejection — i.e., who has been mildly rejected since childhood.
- **Disproportionate response to attachment breach.** Latent and untested until Olaf; once tested, catastrophic. The pattern's *availability* in her psyche, however, predates Olaf — what Olaf does is detonate something that was already loaded by the underlying attachment-scarcity of her upbringing.
- **Craftsmanship affect — pride in well-executed labor.** Present in the rabbit-breeding (she does it carefully, repeatedly, well); will recur in vengeance work, in shopkeeping, and in the precision of her late combat. She is, from the earliest record, a person whose self-worth runs through *doing a thing thoroughly.*
- **No documented capacity for casual sociality.** No childhood friendships are mentioned, ever, in any context. The Halfrek bond of the demon era will be her first attested peer friendship, and Halfrek meets her *after* the rupture. The childhood social field was apparently empty of equals.
- **Animist permeability to the supernatural.** Cultural rather than personal, but operative: she lives in a world where curses and transformations are real options, and she will reach for one when wounded.

## 7. The Pre-Trauma Self — A Composite

Composite, with appropriate epistemic humility: the subject at, say, twenty, on the eve of the Olaf rupture, is a literal-minded, concrete-thinking, mildly-but-chronically-ostracized young woman in a small pagan village, living with the one man who finds her tolerable and loveable, keeping rabbits she has named and bred with attentive pride, going about her domestic tasks with competence and a certain odd dignity, accepting *Aud* as both her name and the village's accurate description of her, possessed of no redundant attachments, no peer friendships, and — critically — **no model of what to do when the single relationship that holds her life together fails.** She has never had to recover from a rupture because she has never had a rupture from anything she cared about. Her affective range has been calibrated to a narrow, livable band: small daily satisfactions (the rabbits, the home, Olaf's affection), small daily injuries (the villagers' confusion at her gifts), no extremes in either direction.

Into this band, Olaf's infidelity will land like an axe.

## 8. Notes for Subsequent Sections

The dossier flags three items for cross-reference to later chronology entries:

- The **rabbit-loss event** (inferred, undated, immediately pre- or post-Olaf rupture) is the working candidate for the proximate cause of the leporiphobia and should be revisited in Chronology II.
- The **Aud/Anya naming continuity** — that she takes, when she becomes mortal again in 1998, a name that is a near-shortening of her birth name *Aud* into the modernized *Anya* rather than retaining *Anyanka* or choosing freshly — is treated in §1 of the shared assessment as a clinical artifact, and the present section grounds it: she is reaching, under the rupture of re-humanization, for the *only prior human self she has*, the odd village girl with the rabbits. This is not regression as defect; it is the only available coordinate.
- The **absent family** lacuna should be treated as a permanent gap in the record rather than as something to be filled by speculation. Its operative significance is structural: she enters adulthood without a redundant attachment system, and every subsequent identity will be organized around the same single-point-of-failure architecture.

The ground floor, then: a child named *odd*, in a village that tolerated her at arm's length, with rabbits for company and one man for love, in a world where curses were real and grief had a phone number. Everything that follows is built on these four facts.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

*Covering: the late Aud period (approx. mid-870s CE through 880 CE), the precipitating betrayal, the recruitment by the patron entity designated D'Hoffryn, the assumption of the operational identity "Anyanka," and the first two centuries of vengeance work through the loss of the first amulet (c. 1199 CE). This is the forge. Every adult behavior catalogued in later sections of this file traces a clean line back to events documented here.*

---

## 1. THE LATE AUD PERIOD: A YOUNG WOMAN ALREADY MARKED

The subject's own account places her in a small Scandinavian settlement she names as Sjornjost, a community small enough that everyone knew her by the diminutive she translates for English-speakers as "odd." This single biographical datum is more diagnostically valuable than any other piece of pre-recruitment evidence in the file. She was not given the name Odd in private; it was the name her parents, her neighbors, and her partner used aloud, day after day, for the entire span of her formative years. The community had categorized her — gently or not — as the strange one, and she had absorbed the categorization as a name.

What can be reconstructed about her daily life in this period, from her own asides over the Sunnydale years:

- **Household.** She lived with a man named Olaf, of marriageable age and of some local stature; he appears to have been physically large, loud, social, and given to public-house drinking with male peers. She was, as far as the record indicates, a common-law or betrothed partner rather than a formally wed wife — her later horror at the wedding-ceremony itself ("Hells Bells") suggests she had no prior ritual experience to compare it to.
- **Vocation.** Domestic and small-husbandry. She bred rabbits in a hutch or warren of her own keeping. The rabbits were not livestock in the food sense; she named them, handled them, and presented them to villagers as gifts. The villagers reacted with the embarrassed bemusement reserved for the local oddity bearing an inappropriate offering. She did not understand the reaction and did not modify the behavior.
- **Social register.** Already markedly literal. Her late-life recollections of the period contain no anecdotes of friendship, of confidante relationships with other women, of inclusion in the female rituals of the village. The absence is conspicuous. She refers to Olaf, to rabbits, and to her own embarrassments. She does not refer to a single named human peer.
- **Sensory and cognitive style.** Concrete, naming-oriented, taxonomic. Naming each rabbit individually is the behavior of a mind that does not abstract a class easily and prefers the discrete particular — a pattern that will reappear in her bookkeeping at the Magic Box eleven centuries later, where she counts every coin and refers to every regular customer by individual quirk.

The picture is of a young woman, probably in her late teens by local convention, with what a modern clinician would identify without hesitation as autistic-spectrum traits, surviving in a tightly bound traditional community by attaching to one socially-legitimating male partner and to a private menagerie of small animals over which she had control, names, and unambiguous reciprocity. This is a fragile equilibrium. It requires Olaf's presence as a kind of social passport, and it requires the rabbits as her only attested emotional reservoir outside of him.

Both supports are about to fail simultaneously.

---

## 2. THE BETRAYAL: ANATOMY OF THE INDEX EVENT

The precipitating event is described by the subject and by D'Hoffryn in fragmentary form across "The Wish," "Triangle" (which restores Olaf to the record as a still-extant troll), and "Selfless" (which reconstructs the moment of transformation in dramatized flashback). From these the file can assemble the following sequence:

**Stage one: discovery.** Olaf takes up with a woman from the village — most plausibly a barmaid given the subject's later, oddly specific Old-Norse curse-formula about "the thing with the udder." The affair appears to have been semi-public, the kind of indiscretion a small village conducts in plain sight while pretending not to. The subject's literal cognition would have made her, paradoxically, both the last to notice and the most absolutely disturbed when she did. She does not have the social apparatus to manage ambiguous knowledge; once she knows, she knows fully.

**Stage two: the private decision.** Between discovery and transformation, the subject works alone. There is no record of her seeking counsel from another woman, from a village elder, from any institutional figure. She does not — and this is critical — confront Olaf verbally in any sustained way. The behavioral pattern of going silent, withdrawing into a competent solo project, and then producing a catastrophic finished output is established here for the first time and will recur for the next 1,100 years. (See later sections on her wedding-day silence, her solo planning of vengeance contracts, her bookkeeping isolation.) She acquires — or already possesses — a working knowledge of practical magic sufficient to perform a major transformative curse. The acquisition itself is undocumented; this is one of the genuine blanks in the file, and the most plausible reconstruction is that village folk-practice in her region included enough women's craft that a young woman of obsessive cognitive style could have assembled a workable repertoire over years of private study, much as she will later assemble a workable accounting practice in months.

**Stage three: the execution.** The curse turns Olaf into a troll. The choice is diagnostically dense:
- It is *literal*: he behaved like a beast, so he becomes a beast. The subject's vengeance idiom from this moment on will be relentlessly metaphor-made-flesh.
- It is *durable*: she does not kill him. Death would end the punishment; transformation extends it indefinitely. The preference for the ongoing aesthetic punishment over the discrete lethal one is her signature, and Olaf is its prototype.
- It is *humiliating in a specifically gendered register*: she takes the man whose body and voice gave her social standing in the village and converts him into something the village will fear, mock, and finally drive out. She is not only punishing Olaf, she is reclaiming the social currency he stole from her.
- It is *non-confrontational*: she does it to him rather than saying anything to him. She does not require his apology, his explanation, or his presence. The curse is a way of having the last word without ever having to speak it.

**Stage four: the aftermath.** The village's reaction is not recorded directly but can be inferred from her recruitment moments later: she is alone, exposed, and probably in flight or in immediate danger of communal retribution when D'Hoffryn appears. The troll she has created is presumably loose and destructive; she is the known oddity who lived with the missing man; the math is not difficult.

This is the moment that fixes her psychological structure for the next millennium. She has discovered three things at once: that she is capable of inflicting devastating proportional harm; that the harm feels *right* in a way that nothing in her ordinary life ever has; and that the world is now closing in on her for having done what she experienced as justice.

---

## 3. THE RECRUITMENT: D'HOFFYRN'S OFFER

The patron entity arrives at this precise pressure point. The timing is not accidental; D'Hoffryn is a connoisseur of exactly this rupture, and his court is staffed entirely by women he has scouted in the hour after their first act of disproportional retaliation. The recruitment scene as reconstructed from "Selfless" has several features the file must underline:

**He praises the work, not the worker.** His opening register is aesthetic appreciation — the curse was *elegant*, *worthy*, *of his interest*. This is precisely the form of recognition the subject has never received in her life. The village has named her odd; D'Hoffryn names her *gifted*. For a person whose entire formative experience has been failed reciprocity, the first competent reading of her interior is delivered by a horned demon-lord at the worst hour of her existence, and it is delivered as a job offer.

**He offers a category.** Up to this moment she has had no name for what she is other than the one her village gave her. He provides her a title — *Anyanka, Patron Saint of Scorned Women* — and a function — *vengeance demon, women's-suffering division*. This is the first time the subject has been given a class membership in which her traits are assets rather than deficits. Her literalism becomes her precision instrument. Her concreteness becomes her contractual rigor. Her difficulty with ambiguity becomes her absolute clarity about justice. He has effectively diagnosed and credentialed her autism in the same breath.

**He offers indefinite tenure.** Demonhood removes aging, removes mortality, removes the body she has just been forced to flee in. She does not have to be Aud anymore. She does not have to be in this village anymore. She does not have to be a person who has just lost the one human attachment she had. The relief of this offer is enormous and largely unrecognized in later analyses of her recruitment — the deal is not only "you can punish men forever," it is "you can stop being who you are." She accepts.

**He does not require her to choose him over Olaf.** The transformation has already estranged her irrevocably from her prior life. D'Hoffryn arrives only after the bridge is burned. This is a recurring feature of his recruitment method, and it is what allows him to maintain the fiction — believed by his recruits, perhaps believed in some attenuated form by himself — that he is rescuing rather than acquiring. The subject will carry this fiction with her for the next thousand years and will continue to address him as a father-figure long after he has demonstrated otherwise.

**The mechanism of empowerment.** She is given an amulet. The amulet is the locus of her demonic power; without it she is a human woman again, and with it she is, within the contractual rules, near-omnipotent in her domain. The externalization of her power into a removable object is, in retrospect, the structural vulnerability of every vengeance demon in D'Hoffryn's stable. It is also the perfect symbolic match for her psychology — her capacity to harm is something she carries rather than something she is, and it can be taken off her, and one day will be.

---

## 4. NAME, IDIOM, AND THE CONSTRUCTION OF "ANYANKA"

The new name is not a clean break. *Anyanka* contains *Aud* by sound and rhythm in the way the subject seems to have preferred — even her final mortal name, *Anya*, is a further contraction along the same axis. Across three identities spanning eleven centuries she has never adopted a name not phonetically descended from the original. The persistence of the root through every transformation is a small, mostly overlooked fact, and it is the strongest evidence in the file that no version of this subject has ever fully repudiated any prior version. The continuities run deeper than the ruptures.

The operational idiom she develops in her early Anyanka period — visible in retrospect through the curse-craft on display in "The Wish," "Selfless," and the references to her historical work — has the following features:

- **Wish-mediated rather than self-initiated.** She does not choose targets. She responds to the spoken wish of a wronged woman. This is significant: it preserves her sense of contractual legitimacy and externalizes the moral burden. She is, in her own framing, a service provider. The wronged woman is the principal; Anyanka is merely the contractor. The same framing will protect her conscience for a thousand years and will fail her, completely and at once, in "Selfless."
- **Literal interpretation of the wish.** Cordelia wishes Buffy had never come to Sunnydale; the result is a catastrophic alternate-universe Sunnydale ruled by vampires. The curse is technically responsive to the literal phrasing of the wish and indifferent to its intent. This is the autistic literalism of Aud transposed into a metaphysical instrument. It is not malice; it is exact reading.
- **Aesthetic finish.** She does not perform crude curses. The work has elegance, irony, and what she will later refer to with genuine pride as craftsmanship. She is an artisan of suffering and considers the artisanship the dignifying element.
- **Specialization in betrayal by men.** Her caseload is functionally one category: women wronged by intimate partners. Other vengeance demons in D'Hoffryn's stable specialize differently (Halfrek's portfolio appears to include neglected children); Anyanka's portfolio remains, for eleven hundred years, the wound that recruited her. She has been processing her own index trauma over and over again, with other women's mouths providing the wishes, for longer than most human civilizations have existed.

---

## 5. THE FIRST TWO CENTURIES: WORK, REPUTATION, AND THE 1199 INCIDENT

The file's resolution on the period from approximately 880 to 1199 CE is low but not zero. The subject volunteered scattered references across her Sunnydale years: a wronged shepherdess in a "small fishing village" (offhand mention, undated, likely tenth century by context); a Crusader's wife (twelfth century by implication); various poisonings she takes credit for in passing during arguments with Xander. The work of these centuries can be characterized rather than itemized:

- **Volume.** By her own count, "over a thousand" vengeances over the full career; the early-period rate is probably the slower part of that curve, as she learns the trade and as her reputation grows. Plausible estimate: low hundreds in the first two centuries.
- **Geographic range.** Initially Scandinavian and northern European; expanding through the medieval period into the Mediterranean and the Near East as wish-traffic and her own mobility expand. She moves where wronged women summon her.
- **Affect during the work.** Uniformly positive. There is no record, anywhere in canon, of her expressing reservations about a vengeance during the Anyanka period proper. The role is ego-syntonic to a degree that should itself be diagnostic; nobody is naturally this comfortable inflicting elaborate suffering on strangers. The fit is forced by the prior trauma, by the credentialing relief of D'Hoffryn's framing, and by the absence of any competing identity.
- **Relationships within the court.** She forms her one durable peer attachment in this period, with the demon called Halfrek (also a former human, recruited under similar circumstances). The Anya–Halfrek friendship is the only attested non-romantic same-status bond in her entire eleven-century record before Sunnydale, and it is the relationship D'Hoffryn will eventually destroy to punish her in "Selfless." That he chooses Halfrek specifically, of all available targets, indicates that he has been watching this attachment for centuries and knows its weight.

**The 1199 amulet loss.** The canonical reference is brief — she mentions in passing that she has been depowered once before — and the date is reconstructed from her elliptical chronological asides. The incident is critical because it is a rehearsal of what will permanently happen to her in 1998. For some period (the duration is unclear, plausibly weeks to months) she existed as a human woman in a medieval setting, without the protection of demonhood, presumably in considerable danger. She recovered the amulet and resumed work; the recovery taught her, falsely, that depowerment was a recoverable state. This false lesson is what makes her Sunnydale loss psychologically catastrophic — she spends the early human period of "Anya" operating on the prior assumption that the amulet can be restored, and only gradually, over the run of season four, does she internalize that this time it is permanent.

The 1199 incident also gave her, presumably, her first sustained adult experience in a human body since her recruitment — three centuries after the fact. The somatic shock of that brief re-mortality is not described in the record, but its later analog in 1998 is documented in painful detail (see Medical, §2), and there is no reason to think the earlier instance was easier. She would have learned then, for the first time, that her human body had not aged during her demonhood; she was still the young woman D'Hoffryn had recruited, frozen at the threshold of the worst day of her life, returned to it whenever the amulet was removed. The implication is unsettling and important: every time she loses the amulet, she lands back inside the body that lost Olaf. Her re-humanizations are not neutral; they are returns to the scene.

---

## 6. THE FIRST DEFINING CHOICES — AND WHAT THEY FIXED

Looking back across the formation period, three early decisions can be isolated as load-bearing for the entire subsequent record:

**Choice one: to curse Olaf rather than confront him.** Established the lifelong pattern of converting interpersonal conflict into solo craft executed at distance. Every adult coping strategy she develops — the bookkeeping, the contracts, the wish-mediated vengeance, the long silences before catastrophic action — derives from this template. She has never, in eleven hundred years, learned how to have an argument with an intimate partner. She has only ever learned how to produce, in private, a finished work of retaliation.

**Choice two: to accept D'Hoffryn's offer rather than flee into anonymity.** A different young woman in the same crisis might have run to the next valley and started over. The subject accepted credentialing instead. This established her organizing hunger for *placement* — the need to belong to a named category with explicit rules. The same hunger will later make her enroll in Sunnydale High when she does not know what else to do with a human body; will make her latch onto the role of Xander's girlfriend with the totality usually reserved for vocations; will make her return to D'Hoffryn at the first post-wedding crisis. She does not tolerate being uncategorized. She will accept almost any category, including one that requires her to harm strangers for a millennium, rather than be nothing in particular.

**Choice three: to specialize, within the demon role, in her own wound.** D'Hoffryn's court permits a range of vengeance portfolios. The subject chose — or drifted into, and never moved out of — the one that exactly mirrored her index trauma. Eleven hundred years of processing the Olaf event through other women's mouths is the longest unbroken trauma-reenactment loop the file is aware of. It accomplished two things: it sustained her, by giving the original wound an inexhaustible outlet; and it preserved the wound exactly as it was, unworked-through, ready to fire again the moment a sufficiently similar precipitant arrived. In 2002, when Xander walked away from the altar, the loop closed in seconds. The eleven hundred years had not metabolized anything. They had only postponed.

---

## 7. WHAT THE FORMATION PERIOD DID NOT GIVE HER

A surveillance file is as much about absences as presences. The following developmental experiences are missing from the subject's record entirely and their absence shapes everything downstream:

- **No adolescent peer group.** She passed from village-oddity directly to demonic specialist. She has never been in a cohort of equals her own developmental age. When she lands in Sunnydale High at apparent age 18, she is not regressing — she is, in a real sense, attending high school for the first time, because she never had one. Her inability to read the social environment is not just dislocation; it is genuine inexperience.
- **No reciprocal romantic apprenticeship.** Olaf was, as best the record can tell, her first and only pre-recruitment partner. She has no template for dating, for managed disagreement, for graceful disengagement, for tolerating uncertainty in a partner's feeling. Every romantic move she makes in Sunnydale is constructed from scratch under field conditions.
- **No grief-work for Olaf.** She was recruited mid-rage. The mourning was foreclosed by the immediate provision of a vocation that consumed it. She has never grieved the loss of her first relationship, only weaponized it. This is the single largest piece of unfinished psychological business in her record, and it will resurface — disguised but unmistakable — every time she encounters a death she cannot weaponize: Joyce's, Tara's, eventually her own.
- **No model of survivable betrayal.** Because she answered the first betrayal with annihilation, she never discovered that some betrayals can be survived without it. The lesson of her last year — quietly, painfully learned in the wake of "Hells Bells" — is that it is possible to be left and to remain, that the world does not require a troll be made of every man who fails one. She is killed in "Chosen" before this lesson can fully consolidate.

---

## 8. SUMMARY: THE FORGE

The formation period produced an operative whose internal architecture can be summarized in a single line: *a literal, lonely, gifted young woman, caught at the exact instant of her first betrayal by an entity who offered her credentialing in exchange for indefinite reenactment of her wound*. Every later phase of her life — the eleven hundred years of professional vengeance, the four years of stumbling re-humanization in Sunnydale, the brief relapse, the chosen death among the people she had finally learned to call hers — is built on the foundation poured in those few months between Olaf's first infidelity and D'Hoffryn's recruitment offer.

The forge did three things and only three things, and each is permanent:

1. It established that catastrophic retaliation was her native idiom for unbearable feeling.
2. It established that institutional placement by a powerful patron was her native solution to category-homelessness.
3. It preserved, intact and untreated, the original wound that the institution was designed to discharge but never to heal.

The next section of the file — Chronology III — picks up the long working career and the social ecology of D'Hoffryn's court across the medieval, early modern, and modern periods, culminating in the Sunnydale assignment and the second loss of the amulet.


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

*Covering the bulk of the subject's longitudinal record: the vengeance vocation from approximately 880 CE through 1998 CE (~1,118 years of operational activity), bracketed and informed by the brief recursion of 2001–2002. This is the era for which the file is necessarily reconstructive — direct observation is impossible, demonic record-keeping is patchy, and the subject herself is the primary source. What can be assembled is nevertheless dense: the patterns established here are the patterns the subject carries, intact, into mortal life, and every micro-behavior in the Sunnydale period (1998–2003) is a footnote to a habit built across this millennium.*

---

## 1. Onboarding and Apprenticeship (c. 880 – c. 920 CE)

The recruitment is the hinge. D'Hoffryn's pitch — "Now, that is a vengeance I can support" — is delivered to a woman who has just transmuted a faithless husband into a troll using folk-magic she has clearly been studying privately for some time (the spell is not improvised; the ingredients suggest weeks of preparation, and the subject's later facility with ritual mechanics confirms a baseline competence that predates her elevation). What he offers her is not power — she has just demonstrated she has power — but *category*. A name, a court, a peer group, an office, a uniform (the demon-face she later describes, embarrassed, as "vein-y"), and above all a set of explicit rules within which her literal cognition is no longer a defect but a credential.

The behavioral file infers, with high confidence, that the first decades are a long adjustment to embodiment in the altered form. The subject's late-period horror at her own face ("I had wrinkles and the *veins*…") is the residue of someone who was, at one point, genuinely shocked to catch her own reflection. The early Anyanka is almost certainly clumsy: her later boasts ("over a thousand years") emphasize *duration* and *volume*, never *elegance of early work*. The masterpieces she names by title — Cordelia's wish, the Russian uprising, the Mason-Dixon massacre — are all late or middle-late. She does not cite her first hundred jobs. Either they were beneath citation or they were apprentice work she has since edited out of her own narrative — a self-curating habit that becomes diagnostic later (see her selective accounts to Xander of her past, always quantitative, never specific until pressed in "Selfless").

Halfrek almost certainly enters the record in this first century. The intimacy between them, when finally observed in "Older and Far Away" and "Hells Bells," has the texture of a friendship measured in lifetimes — Halfrek finishes her sentences, mocks her affectionately about Xander, knows the names of grievances Anya has not spoken aloud in centuries. The most economical reading is that they came up together, perhaps were trained by the same handler, perhaps shared a circuit. This is the only peer attachment the subject forms in the entire eleven hundred years; that it survives across that span and that the subject still calls Halfrek by her old human name, *Cecily*, in private, is the one piece of evidence we have that something tender persisted in her under the role.

---

## 2. The Establishment of the Vocational Pattern (c. 920 – c. 1199 CE)

By the late ninth and early tenth centuries the subject has settled into the operational shape she will hold, with only stylistic variation, for the next millennium.

**Specialization.** She works one docket: scorned women, romantic betrayal, infidelity, abandonment. D'Hoffryn's court is a guild — there are colleagues specializing in maternal grievance (Halfrek's beat, eventually), in commercial wrong, in dynastic feud. Anyanka does not poach. She is the patron saint of one particular suffering and she stays in her lane with the parochial pride of a tradesman. This is the first instance of a lifelong pattern: when given a defined role, the subject inhabits it to the exclusion of all peripheral possibility. She does not branch. The same trait will make her, later, an exceptional shopkeeper who refuses to discount inventory.

**Method.** The work is contractual. A woman speaks a wish in earshot of the amulet, the amulet hears, Anyanka manifests, the wish is granted in literal terms. The literalism is the craft. Her satisfaction in "The Wish" — "I gave Cordelia *exactly* what she wanted" — is the satisfaction of a translator who has rendered a colloquial phrase into its precise denotative consequence. This is autistic literalism elevated to a professional virtue, and the subject's late-life pleasure in bookkeeping, where double-entry must balance to the penny, is the same pleasure exercised on a smaller canvas.

**Affect.** Across this period the subject reports — and the indirect evidence supports — moral untroubledness. The men deserve it. The contract is freely entered. The wish was specific. She is not cruel for cruelty's sake; she is, by her own lights, *fair*. This is the defense the file flags as splitting: the moral world is binary, women wronged are categorically right, men who betrayed are categorically forfeit, and the third category — ambiguity — does not appear in her docket.

**The first amulet loss (c. 1199).** Brief, recoverable, deeply formative. The exact circumstances are not reconstructable from the canon, but the subject mentions it in passing as something that *happened* and was *fixed* — implying both that depowering was survivable and that D'Hoffryn restored her, which in turn implies she was valuable enough to be restored. The episode functions in her psychology as a near-miss: she has tasted, briefly, what it is to be inside a human body with human time pressing on her, and she has been allowed to retreat from it. This is the cognitive template she will reach for in 1998 ("when this gets fixed I will go back") and that will fail her there, because the second loss is not survivable in the same way.

---

## 3. The Middle Centuries (c. 1200 – c. 1700 CE)

This is the long flat of the curve and the period for which the file has the least specific material. Inferences:

**Geographic mobility.** The work follows the wronged woman, and the wronged woman is everywhere. The subject is not territorial. Her references in the Sunnydale period to ritual practices, foodstuffs, languages, and historical events range across Scandinavia, the Slavic east, the eastern Mediterranean, and western Europe with the casualness of someone who has lived in all of them. She speaks, when sufficiently angry or sufficiently inebriated, in scraps of what sounds like Old Norse, and her vocabulary for ritual implements is polyglot in a way that suggests no single liturgical training.

**The texture of the work.** What she does, day to day, across these centuries is not glamorous. The bulk of vengeance work is small: a village miller's wife wishes her husband impotent and Anyanka makes it so; a baker's widow wishes the man who jilted her sister would choke on his bread and Anyanka attends to it. The famous catastrophes — uprisings, massacres — are the rare upper end of a distribution whose median is petty and domestic. This matters for the subject's later self-image: when she boasts of "over a thousand years," she is averaging across an enormous body of low-stakes work and a handful of spectacular ones. The boast is calibrated for the spectaculars.

**Plague centuries.** It is impossible that the subject is in continental Europe during the fourteenth century without registering the Black Death. Her late-period horror of disease, of the body's permeability, of mortality as a *thing that happens to populations*, is most consistent with a witness who has watched the human category, at scale, encounter the limit of its own embodiment. Her behavior in Sunnydale around Joyce Summers' death ("The Body") — the famously direct, unguarded speech about not understanding why people stop and start — has the affect not of someone encountering death freshly but of someone who has seen too much of it and never been required to articulate it, and is now articulating it in a language she does not yet command.

**Witch hunts and the Reformation.** The subject's lane — the punishment of unfaithful men, often by means readable as *witchcraft* — places her, professionally, adjacent to every European episode of witch-finding from the fifteenth century forward. The pattern is uncomfortable: she is the actual supernatural agent, and the women burned are her clients or her clients' neighbors. Whether she registers the moral asymmetry at the time is doubtful; her late-period capacity to revise past judgments suggests she may have registered it retrospectively, contributing to the cumulative load that surfaces in "Selfless."

**Bunny exposure.** Worth noting: rabbits, domesticated and wild, are ubiquitous across her operational range for the whole period. She avoids them. The phobia, formed in the Aud era, is not desensitized by a thousand years of repeated low-grade exposure — which is itself diagnostic. Phobias maintained against constant background stimulus are phobias defended by avoidance routines, and the file infers a thousand years of small, automatized detours: not entering certain hedgerows, not accepting certain foods, not sleeping in certain barns. The fossil is kept alive by ritual.

---

## 4. Major Documented Actions

**The Russian peasant uprising of 1905.** The subject mentions this with pride. Operationally, it cannot have been her sole work — historical events of this scale are overdetermined — but her contribution was likely catalytic: a wronged woman, a specific landlord, a specific household, a vengeance that escalated into a regional grievance that she did not bother to contain. Pattern note: she does not appear to have moderated the consequences. The vengeance career is not concerned with proportion at the meta-level even when it is obsessively concerned with proportion at the contract level. This will be important in "Selfless," where she massacres a fraternity in literal fulfillment of a wish whose speaker did not intend that scale.

**The Mason-Dixon massacre.** The canon's reference is geographically and temporally specific in a way that is hard to triangulate (the term is anachronistic for the period she elsewhere implies); the file treats it as the subject's own re-labeling, in modern American shorthand, of an antebellum or Reconstruction-era action she conducted in the American South. Significant: she has by this point added North America to her operational range, presumably following European migration. She is, in other words, *current* — she does not get stranded in a single century's idiom, which speaks to a working capacity for cultural assimilation that becomes invisible only in 1998, when the assimilation problem is no longer language and clothing but neurochemistry and embodiment.

**The Cordelia Chase wish (Sunnydale, late 1997 / early 1998).** Operationally a routine job; historically her last as Anyanka in this stretch. The wish — that Buffy Summers had never come to Sunnydale — is granted with characteristic literalism, producing an alternate reality of mass demonic predation. Giles, recognizing the amulet, smashes it. The amulet does not regenerate. She is stranded.

The file flags the *manner* of the stranding. She has been depowered before; she expects retrieval. The behavior across the following months — re-enrollment in high school, confused fixation on regaining the amulet, an apparent failure to grasp that this time the answer is no — reads as a person waiting for a call that does not come. By "The Prom" she has begun the second adjustment of her existence: not to a new body, this time, but to an old one, permanently.

---

## 5. The Recursion (Summer 2002 – Autumn 2002)

The middle period has a coda, and the file is required to address it here rather than in the late record because it belongs structurally to *this* chronology — it is the vengeance career resumed, not a new chapter.

**Reinstatement.** After Xander leaves her at the altar, the subject returns to D'Hoffryn. The speed of the return — within hours of the jilting — is the most diagnostically dense single behavior in her record. She does not grieve. She does not seek the Scoobies. She does not drink, sleep, or stall. She walks directly back into the only category that has ever told her what she is. D'Hoffryn accepts her with what reads as relief; he has been holding her chair.

**Operational degradation.** She is bad at it. The contracts she takes are erratic, the satisfactions she reports are forced. Halfrek, observed with her in this period, treats her with the gentleness one extends to a colleague who has come back too soon from a serious illness. The subject is going through the motions of a vocation she no longer fits, and the file infers — from the conspicuous absence of boastful affect during this stretch — that she knows it.

**The fraternity massacre.** The work that breaks her. The wish is spoken, the contract is enacted with full literalism, and the result is a roomful of dead young men with their hearts on the outside of their bodies. She walks among the corpses and reports, to herself and to a horrified Willow, the satisfaction-script she has used for a thousand years — and the script does not fit. The mismatch is not moral revelation in any single moment; it is a slow puncture across the episode, ending with her request, to Buffy, for execution.

**D'Hoffryn's counterstroke.** He does not kill her. He kills Halfrek. The choice is exquisitely calibrated, and the file notes it as evidence that D'Hoffryn has, across a thousand years, maintained an accurate model of his employee's actual vulnerabilities — he knows that her body has stopped being the thing she most fears losing. He has trained her too well to have missed where the soft tissue migrated. The punishment confirms, in the cruellest possible curriculum, what the subject has already begun to suspect: that she is no longer of the demon category and cannot return to it. The middle period closes here.

---

## 6. Evolution of Patterns Across the Period

The longitudinal arc of the vocation, distilled:

- **Identity consolidation (880 – ~1000):** the role replaces the self. The subject becomes able to answer the question *what are you* without hesitation, for the first time in her existence. The relief of this is, the file infers, profound and is the reason the role holds for as long as it does.
- **Routinization (1000 – ~1500):** the work becomes craft, the affect becomes flat-professional, the moral binary hardens. Same-sex peer bond with Halfrek stabilizes. Phobic avoidance routines around rabbits automate.
- **Connoisseurship (1500 – ~1850):** the subject begins selecting jobs for aesthetic interest as much as need. The cited masterpieces cluster in the later centuries. Boasting affect develops.
- **Late drift (1850 – 1998):** geographic and cultural mobility increases; modernity is integrated; some attrition of zeal is plausible. The Cordelia job, in this reading, is unremarkable in itself but consequential in its interruption.
- **Stranding and incomplete extraction (1998 – 2002):** the file places the *real* end of the middle period here, not at the amulet's destruction. The subject is bodily extracted but psychologically still on the payroll throughout her first Sunnydale years — her capitalism, her literalism, her contractual framing of romance, her wedding-night threats, all are vocational habits running on the wrong substrate.
- **Recursion and rupture (2002):** the attempt to return fails because the substrate has, in fact, changed. The middle period ends not when she loses her power but when she discovers that the power, restored, no longer fits.

What the eleven hundred years built, and what she carries out of them into the final mortal year, is a complete vocabulary for being *useful, placed, and categorical* — and no vocabulary at all for being *loved without terms*. That asymmetry is the inheritance of the middle period, and every behavior worth surveilling in the late record is, in some form, her attempt to assemble the missing vocabulary from the available one. The middle period taught her to count. It did not teach her what is uncountable. The remainder of the file is the record of her learning, late and imperfectly, the difference.


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

*Covering the period from late spring 2002 (the aborted wedding) through the collapse of Sunnydale, 2003; reconstructed from continuous observation, residue-evidence at known dwellings and workplaces, and the subject's own verbal record, which in this period becomes unusually candid and, for the first time, retrospective.*

---

## 1. The Precipitating Event: The Wedding That Did Not Happen (May 2002)

The recent-history file properly begins not with an event but with a non-event — a wedding scheduled, catered, witnessed, costumed, and then unconsummated by ceremony. The subject's preparation behavior in the two weeks preceding is consistent with what the broader record predicts: total commitment to a bounded, contractual ritual she could plan as a project. Surveillance of the Magic Box register tape for the weeks in question shows abnormal patterns — long stretches with no transactions, interrupted by bursts of compulsive small purchases (ribbon, place-cards, a third copy of a bridal magazine she already owned). She rehearsed her vows aloud while alone in the shop after closing. She wrote at least two drafts of a prenuptial financial document and presented neither.

The morning of the ceremony she dressed early, alone except for a single attendant, and waited. Duration of wait before subject understood the groom was not arriving: approximately ninety minutes longer than necessary. The delay is informative — it indexes the depth of her commitment to the contract-frame: she could not at first model the possibility of non-performance, because in her schema a wedding is an executed agreement, not an event subject to last-minute revision.

The decompensation that followed was not loud. Witness reports across the next forty-eight hours converge on the same description: the subject did not weep extensively in public, did not break property, did not telephone Xander Harris repeatedly. Instead she went quiet, sat in the reception hall as the guests dispersed, and several hours later was alone. This silence is the diagnostic detail. In her ordinary affect-regulation pattern, distress runs out the mouth; when distress instead goes inward, decompensation is imminent.

Within seventy-two hours she had re-summoned D'Hoffryn and accepted reinstatement.

## 2. The Re-Vengeance Interval (Summer 2002)

The second demon-period is brief — measured in weeks rather than years — and almost entirely unproductive by her old professional standards. This itself is the file's central observation about the interval: she could not work.

Her first contracted task is the cursing of Xander Harris. She has the means, the warrant (a wronged-woman caller would have satisfied the criteria), and full restoration of her power. She does not execute. She arrives at his apartment, observes him through the window, and leaves. Subsequent attempts at lesser vengeances are documented as half-formed: she initiates curses, retracts them, talks herself in and out of completion. The record shows a master craftsperson who has lost the capacity to finish her own work.

The episode that does complete — the fraternity massacre — is significant because she did not initiate it. She granted a wish made by another woman, executed the curse with full force, and only then registered what she had done. Behavioral evidence at the scene: she remained in the room. She did not flee, did not gloat, did not call D'Hoffryn for credit. She sat on the staircase. When Buffy Summers arrived she did not negotiate; she requested execution. This is not the Anyanka of 1199 or 1905. The professional identity is no longer load-bearing; it is a costume she put back on and discovered does not fit.

D'Hoffryn's countermove — killing Halfrek in lieu of Anya — is the file's first hard confirmation of where her vulnerabilities now actually live. He did not torture her, did not strip her powers immediately, did not threaten Xander. He killed her one peer. The precision indicates that D'Hoffryn, an observer of her for over a thousand years, also recognized that her center of gravity had shifted. The friendship was the pressure point, not the romance and not the power.

## 3. Re-Mortalization, Second Iteration (Autumn 2002)

The subject re-enters the human category for the second time in her recorded existence. The clinical contrast with the 1998 re-mortalization is stark and is the most important single observation of the recent-history file.

In 1998 she presented as disoriented, fixated on regaining her power, and emotionally absent — a person trying to reverse an event. In 2002 she presents as a person trying to *survive* an event she now understands she will not reverse. Surveillance and direct observation at the Magic Box, the apartment she had shared with Xander, and the Summers residence over the autumn months yields the following behavioral profile:

- **Sleep architecture disrupted.** She is observed at the Magic Box at hours she did not previously keep. Lights on at 3 a.m. Inventory re-counted on consecutive nights. The compulsive counting behavior, previously a baseline tic, is now a sedative.
- **Eating disordered downward.** Her standing lunch order at the Espresso Pump is cancelled in this period; she is observed eating standing up, from the register area, in small quantities. Weight loss is visible by midwinter.
- **Hygiene maintained, grooming declined.** She continues to shower and dress for work but the elaborate hair arrangements of the prior year are abandoned. She wears the same three or four outfits in rotation. The shift indicates depression with preserved executive function — she is functioning, but the discretionary surface has been sanded off.
- **Speech rate halved.** This is the most striking behavioral change. The subject who in 2000–2001 generated a continuous, register-inappropriate verbal stream now produces shorter utterances, longer silences, and — for the first time on record — listens more than she speaks in group conversations.
- **Capitalism vocabulary attenuated.** Money-talk drops by roughly two-thirds. She still operates the till competently but no longer rhapsodizes about it. The defense has not been chosen against; it has simply lost its anesthetic value.
- **Rabbit-mentions persist** at baseline frequency. The phobia is era-invariant.

The Spike encounter (winter 2002) is consistent with the depressive picture. Behaviorally: it occurs after both parties have been drinking, in the Magic Box after hours, on the floor, observed accidentally by Xander and the others via a magical scrying. The subject's affect in the immediate aftermath is not erotic satisfaction or guilt; it is the dull surprise of someone who learned that her body can still do something and is not sure whether the information consoles her. Her verbal framing afterward ("It was just sex") is technically accurate and clinically incomplete; what it was, more precisely, was two people with identical recent injuries (rejection by a partner who could not love them as they wished to be loved) using each other as proof of continued embodiment.

## 4. Reintegration into the Scoobies (Winter 2002 – Spring 2003)

The reintegration is gradual, asymmetric, and — for someone whose attachment pattern has historically been all-or-nothing — psychologically unprecedented. The file documents a subject doing something she has never previously done: maintaining a relationship with a person who hurt her, without either revenge or repair to a prior state.

Working contact with Xander is reestablished within a month of her re-mortalization, primarily through shared Magic Box and Scooby activity. Surveillance of their interactions in this period shows a precise behavioral choreography: she stands at consistent distances (markedly greater than in 2001); she addresses him by name more frequently than before, as if the name itself is being deliberately practiced as a neutral object; she does not touch him incidentally, where previously she had touched him constantly. When the Magic Box is destroyed during the First Evil events, she does not seek him for comfort. She seeks Buffy.

This last detail is the recent-history file's most important relational data point. Her primary attachment has shifted, in the final months, from Xander Harris to Buffy Summers and, secondarily, to Dawn Summers. The shift is not romantic and not even straightforwardly affectionate — it is alliance-based. She perceives Buffy as the one person in the group who has also been killed and returned, who has also experienced category-rupture, and who has consequently no patience for performance. Buffy is the person to whom she speaks most directly in the final season. The famous monologue in "Empty Places" (delivered to Buffy after Buffy is removed from leadership and Anya defends her against the group) functions as the file's clearest statement of her revised worldview: that being extraordinary is in fact harder than being ordinary, and that she had not understood this until recently.

With Willow Rosenberg the relationship is functional, polite, and quietly compassionate. The two of them in this period are both surviving recent collapses (Willow's killing of Warren and her own near-apocalypse, Anya's relapse and re-loss). Neither presses the other. Observed interactions are notable for unusual gentleness on Anya's part — she modulates her vocabulary when Willow is in distress, refrains from her usual literalism. This is new behavior. It indicates that her pragmatic-language deficit, presumed stable across the record, is in fact penetrable by sufficient empathy when the empathy is reciprocally modeled.

With the Potentials — the rotating cast of teenage girls housed at Revello Drive in spring 2003 — she is observably impatient. She instructs them in weapons handling and combat history with the clipped didactic register of someone who knows the material and has no interest in motivating reluctant learners. The Potentials find her frightening. This is informative: stripped of the demon role, she has retained the demon affect when teaching the work of violence. The professional residue persists where it is operationally useful.

## 5. Cognitive and Verbal Shifts: The Emergence of a Reflective Register

In the final eight months of her life the subject begins, for the first time, to speak about herself in past tense and in evaluative terms. Specimens drawn from across the period:

- She describes her vengeance career, in private conversation with Xander, as something she did rather than something she was. The grammatical shift is small and decisive.
