- She uses the word *human* with self-application, slowly, and with what an observer would identify as effort. In 1999–2001 she had used the word almost taxonomically, as a category she was studying from outside. In 2003 she uses it possessively.
- She volunteers, unprompted, opinions about other characters' interior states — a pragmatic-inference move historically absent from her behavior. The inferences are often blunt, sometimes wrong, but they are *offered*, where previously she would have asked for the data outright or proceeded without it.
- Her humor stabilizes. The defensive quipping that began to emerge in late 2001 becomes, by spring 2003, a reliable affect-regulator. She is funny on purpose. She knows when she is funny. She uses humor to deflect questions she does not want to answer — a skill the earlier subject lacked entirely.

These shifts taken together do not constitute a personality change. They constitute the late, hard-won acquisition of a *middle register* — the absence of which was the principal psychological deficit of her entire prior record. She is not transformed; she is, for the first time, modulated.

## 6. The Final Weeks (Late Spring 2003)

The Sunnydale endgame compresses behavioral signal. In the final weeks the subject is housed continuously at the Summers residence with the rest of the Scoobies and the Potentials. The dwelling is overcrowded, sleep-deprived, and tactically tense. Her observed behavioral baseline in this environment is unexpectedly stable. She is one of the more reliably present and undecorated participants in planning meetings — speaks when she has information, does not speak when she does not.

Two micro-incidents in this period are file-worthy:

- During the brief expulsion of Buffy from the house, Anya is one of three people who initially vote against Buffy's leadership and then, within hours, articulates publicly the case for what Buffy has done and for the difficulty of what she has carried. The reversal is not contradiction; it is the visible operation of her newly-acquired reflective register, working in real time.
- Two nights before the final battle, she is observed alone in the kitchen of the Summers residence at approximately 2 a.m., counting something — possibly money, possibly weapons inventory, possibly nothing. The counting behavior is the oldest defense in her record. Its presence in the final 48 hours indicates that her core dysregulatory load remained high and that the late-acquired modulations were a surface, not a replacement.

She does not have a final conversation with Xander Harris. The file finds no evidence of one. Whether this is because she did not seek it or because the closing days were too compressed cannot be determined. The absence is consistent either way with her late pattern: she had recategorized him from primary attachment to ordinary comrade, and ordinary comrades do not require valedictory speeches.

## 7. Death and Current Status (Sunnydale Collapse, Spring 2003)

The subject was killed in combat in the Hellmouth assault, on or about the day of the collapse of Sunnydale, CA. Cause of death: a single bladed weapon through the torso, sustained while she was actively engaged in protecting another combatant (the long-haired man Andrew Wells, a peripheral and noncombatant member of the household). She was speaking at the moment of impact. Her final recorded utterance was a quip directed at the man she was defending. She did not fall in a position of prominence and was not immediately retrieved. The body was lost in the geological collapse that followed the battle and is unrecoverable; the town site is now a crater.

The death is not heroic in the narrative-formal sense — there is no farewell, no slow-motion choice, no name spoken over a body. It is also not accidental. It is *consonant*: she was in the front line by her own decision, defending a person to whom she owed nothing under any contract she had ever previously honored, and the final words out of her mouth were ordinary words for her — a joke, dryly delivered, with the timing she had spent four years acquiring.

**Current status:** Deceased. No remains. No grave. Memorialized only in the verbal record of the survivors, who appear to have spoken of her seldom and inconsistently in the months following — a fact that would have grieved the earlier subject and, the file estimates, would not have surprised the later one. She had, in her own framing, finally become *somebody*; the somebody she became was someone willing to die unwitnessed.

**Last known dwelling:** the Summers residence, 1630 Revello Drive, Sunnydale, CA, now nonexistent.
**Last known place of employment:** the Magic Box, Main Street, Sunnydale, CA, destroyed by combat damage approximately one month prior to her death.
**Last known financial assets:** undetermined; the Magic Box accounts, which she had managed personally and meticulously, were lost with the building. Personal effects at the Summers residence — modest, including the wedding dress, which she had retained — were lost in the collapse.
**Last known peer attachment, demon-side:** Halfrek (deceased, autumn 2002).
**Last known peer attachment, human-side:** Buffy Summers (extant, location post-collapse uncertain at time of filing).

---

## 8. Synthesis of the Recent Period

The chronologically recent file documents a single arc, executed in roughly twelve months: the subject relapsed to her pre-formed defensive identity under the exact precipitant that had organized that identity eleven hundred years earlier; discovered, within weeks, that the defense no longer worked; chose to be punished for what she had done in the brief interval of its use; was punished asymmetrically (by the killing of her friend rather than herself); re-entered the human category in a state of clinical depression; reintegrated slowly and incompletely into a peer group she now understood she had been provisionally rather than fully a member of; began for the first time to develop a reflective interior; and died in a manner congruent with that interior, defending a person of no particular importance to her, mid-sentence, without an audience.

Two observations close this section.

First: the recent period contains the only sustained evidence in the entire 1,143-year record that the subject was capable of change in the strong sense — not new behavior in service of an old structure, but a slow restructuring of what she used the behavior for. The earlier file documents a person who learned to perform humanity; the recent file documents a person beginning to inhabit it.

Second: the death terminates the developmental trajectory at exactly the point where, clinically, the work had become interesting. The file closes with the observation made in the workup synthesis and now substantiated by the final period's data: she nearly managed it. Had she lived, the prognosis was cautiously hopeful. She did not live. The dossier ends here because the subject does.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY

## SUBJECT: ANYA (AUD / ANYANKA / ANYA JENKINS)

*Compiled from observational record, subject's volunteered statements, third-party report (primarily X. Harris, R. Giles, W. Rosenberg), and inferential reconstruction across the three ontological phases of the subject's somatic life. The subject's medical file is necessarily fragmentary: she has no continuous physician of record, no insurance history prior to a single brief enrollment under the Magic Box's small-business policy (c. 2001), and no standardized intake examination at any point. What follows is reconstructed from the body she presented across 1998–2003 — a body that was, by her own report, approximately five years old in its current configuration and approximately 1,140 years old in continuous occupant-experience.*

---

## A. NOTE ON BASELINE: THERE IS NO BASELINE

The standard medical assumption — a continuous somatic record from which deviations can be measured — does not hold for this subject. She has occupied **three distinct bodies in two distinct ontological registers**, with no overlap of physiology:

1. **The Aud body** — human, female, Scandinavian, late 9th century, occupied from birth to approximately age 20–25 (her own statements vary). Lost at the moment of demonic apotheosis. Never recovered.
2. **The Anyanka body** — demonic, of the form D'Hoffryn's court grants its justice-class agents: bone-ridged face, altered dentition, altered vascularization (she gestures at her own face and uses the word *"vein-y"* when describing it). Occupied for approximately 1,100 years. Notable for absence — or radical reduction — of the standard human somatic load: no aging, no menstruation reported, no requirement of regular sleep, no documented illness, attenuated pain response, instantaneous tissue repair, mode of locomotion supplemented by translocation via amulet.
3. **The Anya body** — human, female, presenting as approximately age 18–22 in 1998 and aging at standard human rate thereafter. This body is *not* her Aud body recovered. It is, by all available indication, generated as an artifact of de-powering: when Giles destroyed her amulet, the demonic configuration could not sustain itself and resolved to its mortal substrate, but the substrate it resolved to was not eleven hundred years old. It was a fresh young human female of indeterminate biological provenance. She has the developmental neurology of a young adult and the experiential memory of a millennium.

This is the central somatic fact of the file, and every subsequent entry should be read against it.

---

## B. ERA I — THE AUD BODY (pre-880 CE)

Direct medical observation: none. Reconstruction relies on the subject's own asides, principally in "Selfless" and "Triangle."

**General constitution.** Subject describes herself in this period as functional, agriculturally competent, capable of caring for livestock (the rabbits) and managing a household. No reported chronic illness. Survived to reproductive adulthood in a 9th-century Scandinavian village, which selects for above-baseline immune robustness.

**Reproductive history.** No record of pregnancy. Cohabits with Olaf in what reads as a marriage or marriage-equivalent of some duration ("a thousand years ago" she had "a thing" with him). Sexual relationship presumed active; no offspring mentioned.

**Dental and nutritional.** Inferentially poor by modern standards, baseline by period standards. The subject in later eras shows no surviving dentition from this body, the Aud body having been entirely superseded.

**Injuries.** None documented. Olaf is described as physically large (becomes a troll of considerable mass), and there is no record of domestic violence; the betrayal that triggers her transformation is sexual infidelity, not abuse. Aud's pre-transformation injury risk is best characterized as the ambient mortality of her century — accidents, infection, childbirth (had she conceived) — none of which actualized in the recorded window.

**Psychological impact, retrospective.** The Aud body is the only body in which the subject experienced un-traumatized, ordinary human embodiment. It is also the body in which her social atypicality (concrete cognition, literal language, the rabbit-naming) made her an outsider in her own village. Her own translation of her name as *"odd"* indicates that bodily ordinariness did not protect her from social ostracism. The body she lost when she became Anyanka was therefore already, in her felt experience, a slightly defective social instrument. This may explain the *absence* of mourning for the Aud body in any later statement — she does not speak of it with longing. She speaks of the rabbits.

---

## C. ERA II — THE ANYANKA BODY (c. 880–1998 CE; brief return 2002)

**Acquisition.** Granted by D'Hoffryn at the moment of recruitment. The transformation is not described mechanically; she emerges with the standard vengeance-demon morphology of his court (cf. Halfrek; cf. the "Doppelgangland" alternate-universe vampire-Willow's bone structure, which is iconographically related).

**Morphology.**
- *Face:* ridged forehead, altered cheekbone topology, distended vascular pattern across temples and jaw ("vein-y").
- *Dentition:* enlarged and sharpened (visible in "Selfless" flashbacks and the 2002 reversion).
- *Eyes:* sclera and iris altered in color and luminosity in active vengeance state.
- *Skin:* tonally shifted; texture per third-party report rougher and denser.
- *Hands:* functional, no documented claws; capable of fine manipulation (she retains hand-tool dexterity, ritual gestures, sigil-tracing).

**Physiology.**
- *Aging:* arrested. Eleven hundred years without senescence.
- *Sleep:* presumed unnecessary or radically reduced; she shows no acclimation difficulty when later forced into a human sleep cycle, but she also shows no nostalgia for the freedom from it, suggesting the demon body simply did not register sleep as deprivation.
- *Nutrition:* unclear. She demonstrates appetite as Anyanka in flashback (drinking, eating), but no evidence of nutritional dependency.
- *Reproduction:* no record. Vengeance demons appear to be functionally non-reproductive in the standard sense — D'Hoffryn's court is recruited, not bred.
- *Menstruation:* absent across the eleven-hundred-year window, inferred from her later somatic confusion at menarche-analogue events in the human body.
- *Pain tolerance:* high; tissue repair rapid. She survived the loss of her amulet in 1199 in a depowered state (the "Mason-Dixon" reference, anachronistic on its face, indicates a prior temporary depowering — she has been a human briefly before, c. 1199, and recovered her status). The fact that this earlier depowering left no apparent psychological imprint suggests it was brief and not yet experienced as identity-threatening.

**Substances.** Anyanka drinks. The "Triangle" flashbacks show her drinking with Olaf-as-troll. Whether intoxication registered subjectively is unknown.

**Injuries.** Eleven hundred years of combat-adjacent work with no recorded incapacitation. She loses her amulet twice — once in 1199, once in 1998 (Sunnydale, "The Wish") — both functionally castrating events but neither leaving a wound in the surgical sense.

**The "second face."** Critical psychological note. When she reverts to demon morphology in 2002, she does not experience it as a return to her true self. She experiences it as a costume she has put back on and then can no longer comfortably wear. Her subsequent voluntary surrender of demon status — extracted through D'Hoffryn's killing of Halfrek — is the second irrevocable loss of this body. She does not mourn it either. The Anyanka body, like the Aud body, is something she leaves rather than loses.

---

## D. ERA III — THE ANYA BODY (1998–2003)

This is the body of clinical interest. Approximately five calendar years of continuous occupancy. The subject's primary documented physiology.

### D.1 General presentation

Female, presenting age 18 in 1998 and 22 at death in 2003. Caucasian, light-haired (color modified across the record — natural tone appears to be a medium blonde, occasionally lightened). Height approximately 5'5"–5'6". Build slender, musculature unremarkable until late record (some increase in functional strength after Scooby combat training in S5–S6). No tattoos. No piercings beyond standard ear. No surgical scars on intake. No birthmarks of record.

### D.2 The first eighteen months: a body without an operating manual

The subject lands in this body in spring 1998 with the experiential memory of a millennium and the somatic memory of nothing. Observable consequences across her first two years of human re-embodiment:

- **Interoceptive narration.** She speaks her bodily states out loud, constantly and inappropriately. "I have a brain full of square roots." "My breasts are highly sensitive to extremes in temperature." "Xander, your penis [musical complaint redacted for context]." This is not exhibitionism. It is the verbal externalization of sensory data she has not yet learned to filter into private experience. The pattern attenuates across the record — by S7 she narrates her body markedly less, suggesting she has finally internalized the filter.
- **Menarche-analogue and menstrual onboarding.** No direct record. Inferred from her early-period remarks about "bleeding" with what reads as genuine surprise. The hormonal cycle she is now subject to was, for her, novel after eleven centuries; affect lability in her first two human years is likely partly endocrinological.
- **Sleep.** Reports of insomnia early; she is repeatedly seen at Magic Box hours that suggest she does not yet know how much sleep her new body needs. By S6 she has settled into a roughly normal cycle.
- **Hunger and satiety.** Eats opportunistically and at irregular intervals in early seasons; develops more regular eating patterns once cohabiting with Xander. Her brief tenure at Doublemeat Palace (S6) produces no notable change in eating, suggesting food-aversion did not generalize from work exposure.
- **Pain.** Her response to minor injury early is disproportionate — small cuts produce loud distress. Read against the prior eleven hundred years of attenuated pain response, this is calibration, not weakness. By late S6 her response is roughly age-normative.
- **Sexual response.** First documented partnered sexual activity (with Harris, S4) is described by her in clinical, frequency-counting terms ("orgasms," numbered, scheduled). This is best read not as kink but as a person learning the vocabulary of a human nervous system in real time. Her later sexual encounter with Spike (S6, "Entropy") is markedly different in affect — quiet, sad, mutual — and represents the first occasion on which she appears to use sex in a recognizably adult-human emotional register.

### D.3 Aging

The subject experiences linear human aging for the first time since age ~22 (Aud). She is aware of this and disproportionately preoccupied with it. The preoccupation is not vanity but ontological terror: she has personal experiential knowledge of immortality and is now watching the meter run. Verbal markers across the record include:

- Remarks on Joyce Summers' death (S5) framed not as condolence but as encounter with the *concept* of death.
- Remarks on Buffy's resurrection (S6) similarly framed — *people stay dead, except when they don't, and this is unbearable*.
- Direct statement to Giles (paraphrased): she does not want to die.
- Wedding-anxiety speeches that center on aging-as-imprisonment rather than commitment-as-imprisonment.

The death-anxiety is best understood as a medical-adjacent phenomenon: it is the subjective experience of a nervous system that has been recently re-coupled to mortality after eleven centuries of decoupling. There is no human comparator. The closest analog in the clinical literature would be the existential reactions of long-term ICU survivors or near-death experiencers, scaled up by three orders of magnitude.

### D.4 Documented injuries, Anya body

- **Various minor abrasions, contusions, lacerations** sustained in Scooby operations across S4–S7. None requiring documented medical intervention. She is rarely the front-line combatant; her injury exposure is comparable to a competent civilian in a high-risk household.
- **Concussive exposures** plural, undocumented severity, from various demonic engagements. No reported persistent post-concussive symptoms.
- **Trolley/wedding-day acute stress reaction** ("Hells Bells," 2002): subject presents with symptoms consistent with acute distress — vasovagal-adjacent collapse-and-recovery, tearfulness, derealization. No physician seen. Self-medicates by reclaiming demon status (see §F).
- **Reversion to demon form** (2002): not an injury per se but a somatic event of the first magnitude. Tissue, bone, dentition, and vascularization all transform. The subject reports no pain from the transformation but the *un*-transformation, when D'Hoffryn revokes her status late in S7, leaves her affectively flattened for weeks — a withdrawal-like profile.
- **Terminal injury** ("Chosen," 2003): impalement by Bringer's blade, mid-combat, from behind. Death rapid. No agonal phase observed; she dies mid-quip, which is consistent with rapid exsanguination from a major vascular wound or with severance of upper cord. No body recovered (Sunnydale collapses into the Hellmouth).

### D.5 Surgical and procedural

None of record. She avoids medical settings; whether this is principled (distrust of human institutions she has not had time to learn) or pragmatic (no documentation, no fixed address until Xander) is unclear.

### D.6 Substances

- **Alcohol.** Social use across the record. One documented bender ("Triangle," S5) following a fight with Harris — she drinks aggressively, becomes loudly affectionate then loudly tearful, sleeps it off. The episode is the affect-curve of an inexperienced drinker self-medicating attachment-threat. No subsequent escalation of pattern; she does not become a problem drinker.
- **Caffeine.** Heavy and steady from S4 onward, primarily through the Magic Box's coffee. Functional, not problematic.
- **Tobacco.** No record.
- **Cannabis.** No record.
- **Other recreational substances.** No record. Notably, given Sunnydale's pharmacological ambient, she does not seek out altered states; she has spent eleven hundred years in one and is suspicious of the offer.
- **Pharmaceuticals.** No prescriptions of record. Given her death-anxiety and affect dysregulation, an attentive primary-care physician in 2002 would likely have offered an SSRI; none was offered, because no physician was seen.

### D.7 Phobia: leporiphobia

Severe, specific, persistent across the entire human record. Triggered by visual presentation of rabbits, mention of rabbits in song or speech, plush rabbits, Easter iconography. Symptoms include freezing, vocal distress, tachycardia (inferred from observation), and on at least one occasion (the wedding sequence) somatic complaint sufficient to disrupt function. The phobia meets DSM-5 criteria for Specific Phobia, animal type:

- excessive and unreasonable
- nearly invariably triggers immediate anxiety
- recognized by the subject as excessive (she sings about it self-consciously)
- causes clinically significant distress
- present for more than six months (in fact, present for a millennium)

**Etiology.** Best explanation: the rabbits of the Aud era. She bred them, named them, gave them as gifts, and was mocked for it. The phobia is the only fossil of her pre-trauma identity that survived into both the Anyanka and Anya bodies — it crossed two ontological transformations intact. This is diagnostically extraordinary. It suggests that the affective core of the original trauma (mockery, exposure, loss of innocent attachment) was somatically encoded at a level deeper than ontology, and that the rabbits stand in for the entire lost Aud-self. To fear them is, in a real sense, to fear *her own original self* and what was done to it.

### D.8 Sensory and neurological

- **Vision, hearing, vestibular:** unremarkable.
- **Sleep architecture:** normalized by S6.
- **Headaches:** occasional, self-reported, no pattern.
- **Seizure history:** none.
- **Cognitive profile:** see §3 of base workup. Notable for high working memory, strong numerical fluency, weak pragmatic inference. This profile is *stable across all three bodies* and predates her trauma — strongest single piece of evidence for the broad-autism-phenotype reading in the psychiatric section.

### D.9 Reproductive health, Anya body

- Menstruation: present, irregular early, regularizing.
- Contraception: discussed openly with Harris; method not specified.
- Pregnancy: none.
- STI history: none documented; brief partnered history with two partners (Harris, Spike).
- Gynecological care: no record.

### D.10 The penultimate body-event: re-humanization, late S7

When D'Hoffryn revokes her demon status in punishment-by-proxy for sparing Willow, she undergoes the inverse transformation. The body that remains is her late-Anya body, somewhat altered: she presents in the final episodes with subdued energy, reduced verbal output, weight roughly stable, but a flattened affect that has clear somatic correlates (reduced gesture, lowered vocal volume, slower gait). This is consistent with a depressive episode of moderate severity overlaid on a recent traumatic loss (Halfrek). No intervention sought.

---

## E. CROSS-ERA SOMATIC THEMES

**The body as costume.** Across three bodies and two ontological transitions, the subject does not display somatic identification with any of her bodies as *her*. She mourns no body she has lost. She does not seek to recover the Aud body when re-humanized, nor the Anyanka body when re-de-powered. The body is, for her, an instrument of the current contract. This is functionally a chronic mild dissociation from embodiment — clinically subthreshold, but a consistent feature.

**The single somatic continuity.** The phobia. Rabbits. Across eleven hundred years and three bodies, the only stable somatic-affective marker is leporiphobia. This is the medical signature of the file: everything else is replaceable, this is not.

**Pain as information she does not trust.** In the Anya body she repeatedly reports pain inappropriately — too loud for small injuries, too quiet for large ones. Her pain signal is uncalibrated because she spent a millennium with it attenuated. She is, in effect, a chronic pain-illiterate, and any future medical handler should weight her self-report accordingly.

**Mortality as novel pathology.** Her body's most distinctive medical condition, in the Anya years, is the simple fact of being mortal. She experiences senescence as illness. Any clinician treating her would need to understand that ordinary aging presents to her as a terminal diagnosis, because subjectively it is one.

---

## F. PSYCHOLOGICAL IMPACT, ITEM BY ITEM

- **The Aud body's loss:** unmourned, but the rabbit-phobia preserves its grief somatically.
- **The Anyanka body's acquisition:** experienced as elevation, not violation. She has never expressed distress at having been demonized.
- **The Anyanka body's first loss (1199):** brief, recoverable, no apparent imprint.
- **The Anyanka body's second loss (1998):** catastrophic at the time, generative in retrospect — it is the precondition of every relationship she ever forms.
- **The Anya body's onboarding:** chronic low-grade interoceptive distress for approximately eighteen months; substantially resolved by S6.
- **The Anyanka reversion (2002):** experienced as relief, then as wrongness. She cannot re-inhabit the demon body now that she has learned the human one. This is the somatic correlate of the moral revision documented in "Selfless."
- **The Anyanka body's third loss (late S7):** depressive flattening, somatic slowing, reduced verbal output. The most clinically depressive presentation of her record.
- **The Anya body's destruction (2003):** rapid, in defense of strangers, with a joke on her lips. This is the only body of the three whose ending she chose, and the choice is the medical record's last and most important data point.

---

*End of section. The file should be read with the understanding that this subject is the only known case in the available record of a being who has been continuously conscious across three discrete bodies and two ontological categories, and whose final body — the one in which she died — was the one she had occupied for the shortest time and inhabited the most fully.*


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT "ANYA"

*A body the subject did not grow into. Every entry below should be read against that fact: the musculature, the nervous system, the proprioceptive map all belong to a young woman in her late teens to early twenties; the operator inside them has roughly eleven hundred years of demonic embodiment, prior to which she had perhaps two decades of agrarian human life in tenth-century Scandinavia. The somatic record is the record of an experienced consciousness piloting an under-rehearsed vehicle. Almost every "tic" catalogued below is a seam where the operator and the vehicle do not quite fit.*

---

## 1. BUILD, FRAME, AND BASELINE CARRIAGE

The subject's frame is small-to-medium, narrow-shouldered, long-necked, with the unmarked musculature of a person who has never done sustained physical labor in this body. Resting posture is upright to the point of stiffness — shoulders drawn back, sternum slightly forward, chin level — a presentation more consistent with a person *holding* a posture than inhabiting one. The carriage is the first tell: she has clearly observed that human women of this era and locale stand a certain way, and she is producing that stand rather than defaulting into it. In unobserved moments (alone in the Magic Box stockroom; behind the register after closing) the shoulders drop forward two to three centimeters and the chin tucks; the held posture is not her own.

Weight distribution at rest is markedly even, almost flat-footed; she does not shift weight foot-to-foot the way a person who has grown up in a body shifts. She locks her knees more often than is healthy and has to be reminded, by her own micro-adjustments, to unlock them. Hips are square to whatever object she is addressing — register, counter, interlocutor — with very little of the casual rotational drift that characterizes neurotypical standing conversation. This squaring is one of the most reliable identifiers: across crowds, she can be picked out by the unusually exact perpendicularity of her stance to whoever holds her attention.

---

## 2. GAIT

Walking gait is brisk, short-strided, and *purposive* — every walk has a destination and the body knows it before the walker articulates it. Cadence is faster than the Sunnydale ambient pace by perhaps fifteen percent; she frequently arrives at doors a half-second before her companions and stops short, having to wait. Arm swing is reduced; arms tend to be occupied (ledger, money bag, weapon, Xander's hand) or held close to the torso. When unoccupied, the dominant (right) arm swings in a shortened, controlled arc; the non-dominant arm barely swings at all. This asymmetry is consistent with someone who learned to walk in skirts and has not unlearned it across the transition to trousers and denim.

Heel strike is firm; she does not glide. On hard floors her step is audible from twenty feet — heels in particular announce her. She is not light on her feet in combat either; her footwork in the few times she enters a melee ("Graduation Day," "Chosen") is competent but planted, not dancerly. Turns are executed as discrete pivots rather than continuous curves: she walks to a point, stops, rotates, walks again. This block-style locomotion suggests a movement schema organized around *positions* rather than *flows* — a vengeance demon's choreography of arrivals and departures, not a forager's continuous motion.

Under threat the gait compresses further: stride shortens, cadence increases, the body angles forward from the ankles. Under intimacy (with Xander, walking) the gait becomes uncharacteristically loose — she will lean a shoulder into his upper arm at intervals of roughly four to six paces, a deliberate-feeling re-contact that reads as a self-cued reminder that the attachment is still there.

---

## 3. HANDS

The hands are the most expressive part of the subject and the part most actively in conflict between operator and vehicle. At rest they are rarely actually at rest. Catalogued behaviors:

- **Counting.** Bills, coins, inventory, sometimes empty air. The thumb pad rolls against the pad of the index and middle fingers in a counting motion even when nothing is being counted; observers have noted this during conversations about money, mortality, and Xander's whereabouts. It is a self-soothing pattern, and it is the closest thing in the record to a true stim.
- **Smoothing.** She flattens fabric — her own skirt, the tablecloth, a stack of ledger pages — with a firm two-handed sweep from center outward. Frequency rises sharply in social-anxiety contexts (parties, group meetings where she is not the speaker).
- **Object cradling.** She handles ritual objects, cash drawers, and small breakables with a noticeably tender two-handed grip — fingers spread, thumbs underneath, the object held away from the torso. This is *demon* hand-work: the muscle memory of having handled an amulet that was her power source.
- **Pointing.** When making a verbal point she points with the whole hand, fingers slightly splayed, not the index finger. Her index-finger point is reserved for accusations and is delivered with the arm fully extended.
- **Grip on weapons.** White-knuckled, slightly too tight, with the thumb wrapped around in a closed grip rather than overlapping the fingers — a non-trained grip. Her axe-work in "End of Days" and "Chosen" is brute-force pendulum swings; she does not rotate the haft in the hand.

Nail-biting is absent. She keeps her nails short, square-cut, and unpainted across the entire record; the one episode where she presents painted nails ("The Replacement," at Xander's apartment) shows her flexing the fingers experimentally as if testing whether the coating changes their function. She does not wear rings except for the engagement ring during 2001–2002, which she rotates around the finger with the thumb of the same hand in a continuous quarter-turn — the highest-frequency repetitive movement in the record during that period, and one that ceases entirely after "Hells Bells."

In stress: the hands clutch each other at waist height, fingers interlaced, thumbs squeezing the opposite hand's metacarpals. In intimacy: she leads with the palm rather than the fingertips — she presses, she does not stroke. In threat: hands rise to chest height, palms outward, in a posture that is half de-escalation, half spell-casting muscle memory.

---

## 4. FACE

Resting face is unusually still. The Sunnydale ambient face — micro-smiles, eyebrow flickers, sympathetic frowns of the listener — is largely absent. She does not produce listening-face. Interlocutors often check whether she has heard them; she has heard them with high fidelity, but the receipt has not been somatically signed.

When she speaks, the face becomes mobile in distinct bursts: brows up at the start of a declarative, brows level through the middle, brows down sharply at the end. There is little of the continuous accompaniment-music that most speakers' faces provide their own sentences. Smiles are large, fast, symmetrical, and *brief* — they appear and depart on the order of half a second, with no residual softening. The eyes do not always participate; when they do (with Xander early in the relationship; with Tara; in the last episode, with Andrew), the effect is striking precisely because of its rarity.

Eye contact is sustained well past the local cultural comfort window. She is capable of looking at an interlocutor for the duration of a multi-sentence exchange without breaking. Under stress this lengthens further into a stare; under intimacy it occasionally breaks, downward and to the right, a learned behavior. She blinks slightly less often than average at baseline and considerably less often when computing a transaction (literal or social).

Specific facial signatures:

- **The "explanation face."** Brows drawn together, lips slightly parted, head tilted five to ten degrees. Appears whenever a human social convention has been invoked that she does not understand and is about to ask about.
- **The "vindication face."** Eyes wide, lips compressed into a line, single nod. Appears when an interaction confirms her contractual model of the world ("I told you so" without the words).
- **The phobic face.** Eyes wide and fixed, mouth slightly open, color draining from the cheeks, a small high gasp. Bunnies. Reliable, replicable, distressing to her and rapidly suppressed in front of others over time — by S6 she will turn her head away rather than display it.
- **The dissociative-competence face.** Flat. Mouth neutral, eyes focused middle-distance, no micro-expression. Appears in acute crisis: she becomes very still and very efficient.

She does not cry easily, but when she does it is full-body and unmodulated — a person who has not learned the social shape of crying. Tears arrive without the typical preparatory facial collapse; she will be speaking, then weeping, with no transition. She does not cover her face when crying. The first such instance in record (post-"Hells Bells") is silent and motionless except for the tears themselves.

---

## 5. VOICE AND ORAL HABITS

Pitch is mid-range with a notable tendency to *flatten* declaratives — statements end at the same pitch they begin. Questions sometimes do, too, which produces the characteristic flat-interrogative ("So we're having sex now") that her interlocutors initially mistake for a statement. Volume is reliably one notch above local norm: she is the loudest person in most rooms she occupies, and she does not modulate downward for content (sex, money, death) that her companions modulate for.

Speech rate accelerates under stress and especially under enthusiasm; the words do not become slurred, only packed. Articulation is precise — consonants fully voiced, vowels not reduced. She has lost essentially all trace of the Old Norse phonology of her first language; the English presentation is unaccented American with an occasional formality of vocabulary (full forms of verbs, no contractions in moments of emphasis) that reads as either antique or pedantic depending on context.

She has a small set of verbal tics: the inappropriate-disclosure opener ("Did you know..."), the pricing-out summary ("That's seven dollars even"), the bodily catalogue ("My uterus..."). These are not nervous fillers; they are the syntactic shapes she defaults to when she has not yet decided what to say.

Oral habits: she licks her lips before delivering an unfavorable truth. She bites the inside of her lower lip when listening to bad news. She breathes through her mouth slightly more than is typical, especially when concentrating. She does not whisper well — her whisper retains full vocal-fold engagement, audible across a room.

Laugh: short, surprised, slightly too loud, with a single descending vowel — a *ha* rather than a chain. Genuine laughter (with Xander, with Tara) is rarer and softer and accompanied by a small head-shake. She does not have a social laugh; either she finds it funny or she does not respond.

---

## 6. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Sleep is the body's domain and she does not own it. Reports across the record indicate a sleep onset latency that is short by human standards (she falls asleep quickly when she finally does) but a chronically delayed sleep phase — she stays up. The Magic Box ledger-work she conducts late into the night is partly avoidance of bed. Once asleep she sleeps heavily; Xander reports having to wake her with effort.

Sleeping position with Xander: on her side, facing him, knees slightly drawn up, one hand on his sternum or upper arm — a contact maintained through the night. Without him (post-jilting, S7), she reverts to supine, arms at sides, in a posture observers have noted resembles lying-in-state. She is a still sleeper; she does not toss. She talks in her sleep occasionally — the few reported instances ("Older and Far Away") are in languages other than English, with names not in her current rolodex.

Dreams, when reported, are vivid and unpleasant: recurrent themes of being chased by something faceless, of standing in a room she cannot leave, of trying to count something that keeps changing. She does not have nightmares about Olaf or about specific vengeance victims; the unconscious content has been preprocessed into abstract pursuit. She wakes early after such dreams and is functional within minutes — no grogginess, no extended re-orientation — which itself is unusual and points to a vigilance baseline that does not fully stand down even in sleep.

---

## 7. EATING AND DRINKING

Eating is *operational*. She fuels at scheduled intervals, finishes what is in front of her, and rarely lingers. She eats faster than her companions and notices when she has done so. Food preferences are unsentimental: high-calorie, easily portable, well-priced. She will favor whatever the establishment offers most cheaply and is genuinely offended by waste.

She chews with mouth closed but with audible swallow; she does not pace bites with conversation, which is to say she will speak with food in her mouth if a transactional opportunity arises. Utensil handling is competent but un-elegant — fork in the right hand, knife abandoned on the plate edge, food cut in batches at the start of the meal rather than continuously. This is the eating style of a person who learned utensils late and has optimized for throughput.

Coffee: she drinks it black, in volume, and is observed to be undisturbed by caffeine. Alcohol: she has limited tolerance and limited prior calibration. The "Triangle" bender shows the full progression — talkative, then aggressive, then weepy, then sleeping — with no apparent learning curve afterward; she does not appear to drink to excess again. Water intake is high. She is observed to bite the rim of plastic cups absentmindedly.

Bunnies as food (offered to her once in a market context, possibly imagined, possibly canonical) produce an immediate and total recoil. She does not eat rabbit. She also avoids food that resembles rabbit shape or color (small, soft, brown).

---

## 8. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE BODY

The intimate body is the domain in which the operator-vehicle gap is most narrowed, in part because the demon period included no functional human sexuality and so there is less acquired counter-pattern to override. With Xander she is reported (by her own narration, frequent and unsolicited) to be enthusiastic, frequent, and exploratory in a cataloguing way — she names what is happening as it happens, requests specific acts by name, and tracks frequency.

Touch behavior in non-sexual intimate contexts is *contact-seeking* but not *contact-melting*. She will hold a hand, lean a shoulder, sit thigh-to-thigh; she does not stroke, nuzzle, or trace. The touch she initiates has the quality of a docking maneuver — connection made, position held, no further movement. Receipt of touch is initially over-startled (she flinches at unexpected touch from anyone, including friends, through S4) and gradually normalizes; by S6 she can be hugged without bracing, by Tara especially. She does not initiate hugs except with Xander and, late, with Halfrek.

Kissing style: closed-mouth, firm, brief — opening into more only with explicit cue. She does not nuzzle the face or kiss the forehead. The scene with Spike in "Entropy" shows a different mode entirely: ungentle, mutual, instrumental, and notably silent — neither party narrates, neither softens, the body is being used as a tourniquet.

Post-coital behavior with Xander: she dresses promptly and resumes whatever activity preceded the encounter, but maintains hand or foot contact through the resumption. With Spike: she leaves the area.

Menstruation, hormonal cycling, and other bodily processes she discusses with the same flat catalogue voice she applies to weather. There is no shame register; there is also no privacy register. The absence of both is itself a tell — the social negotiation around the body has not been internalized, only observed.

---

## 9. MICRO-MOVEMENTS, TICS, AND POSTURAL TELLS BY STATE

**Calm baseline (Magic Box during business hours, no romantic disturbance, cash flow positive).** Upright stance, square hips, hands occupied with ledger or register, brisk gait, full eye contact, voice one notch loud, micro-smile in service of customer. Thumb-pad counting against fingertips at very low frequency. Breathing nasal, even, slightly shallow.

**Mild stress (Scooby meeting in which she is not the topic; a social event she has been required to attend).** Increased verbal output, particularly off-topic disclosure. Fabric-smoothing on her own clothing. Bouncing of the front foot when seated, frequency one to two cycles per second, suppressed if she notices it. Money or object counted in pocket. Speech rate up ten to twenty percent.

**Moderate stress (Xander absent or late; a customer dispute; an apocalypse being discussed in terms she finds imprecise).** Hands interlace at waist. Posture stiffens further. Eye contact lengthens into staring. Skin flushes at the throat and upper chest, not the face. Voice rises in volume; pitch holds. The "explanation face" appears repeatedly. Frequency of mortality-references in speech increases markedly.

**Acute stress (sudden threat, bunny sighting, news of death).** Body locks. A small high inhalation, audible. Hands rise to chest height. Color drains from cheeks. Pupils dilate. She does not vocalize for two to four seconds, then either flees the immediate space or recovers into dissociative-competence mode.

**Dissociative competence (combat, end-of-world logistics, packing for evacuation).** Flat face, economical movement, decisive object-handling, voice dropped to ordinary volume, no extraneous speech. She becomes briefly very capable and very absent. This is the state most resembling her demon-period operating mode.

**Intimacy (with Xander, late period; with Tara; with Halfrek).** Posture softens, shoulders drop, chin tucks slightly. Voice quiets — the only context in which it does. Touch initiation increases. Eye contact may break downward. She permits silence; in no other state does she.

**Threat to a bonded other.** Forward angle from ankles, weight on balls of feet, hands free and slightly forward of the hips, voice low and clipped, full pupillary dilation. She will step in front of the bonded other without verbal negotiation. This is the only state in which her body moves *before* her speech.

**Romantic-humiliation re-trigger (the index-trauma signature).** Total stillness, then a single deep inhalation, then a turn-and-walk that is faster than her normal gait and does not stop at the door. Voice cuts out entirely. She does not weep until she is alone. This is the somatic shape of the relapse, observable both in the Aud-Olaf account she gives and in the post-"Hells Bells" footage.

---

## 10. GROOMING, DRESS, AND THE PRESENTED SURFACE

Grooming is meticulous in a checklist sense. Hair is washed, brushed, and arranged into recognizable contemporary styles; the styling is competent but conservative, with little experimentation across the record — she has identified what works on this face and reproduces it. Makeup is similarly modest and reproducible: a defined lip, mascara, no contour-work. No tattoos, no piercings beyond standard earlobes. She wears earrings consistently; they are usually small studs, occasionally a small drop, never anything that swings dramatically.

Dress evolves visibly over the four-year record. Early Anya wears whatever appears age-appropriate and is acquirable cheaply — fitted tops, knee-length skirts, simple flats — chosen with an eye to fitting in rather than to self-expression. Mid-period she dresses to Xander's apparent preference and to Magic Box professional norms: skirt-and-blouse combinations, low heels, a single cardigan repeated. Engagement-period dress becomes brighter and more deliberate, with more red. Post-jilting and into S7 the palette darkens and the silhouettes become more covering — long sleeves, higher necklines. The wedding-dress moment is the only formal couture in the record and she wears it with poise that surprises her companions; she has, after all, attended a great many of other people's weddings and observed.

Scent: she does not appear to wear perfume; observers report no signature olfactory marker beyond clean fabric and a faint commercial soap. She is fastidious about hand-washing — she washes them after handling money, before eating, after physical contact with anything she classifies as unclean, which includes most demons and some Scoobies after fieldwork.

She owns very little. Across the record she is associated with no jewelry of sentimental provenance (the amulet is gone; the engagement ring is returned), no collection, no display of personal artifacts in any space she occupies. The Magic Box she treats as hers but stocks with stock. Her apartment, glimpsed only briefly, is sparsely furnished, organized, and reads as a hotel room she has been in for some months. This is the somatic-environmental signature of a person who has not lived long enough in any one self to accumulate the objects that selves accumulate.

---

## 11. THE FOSSILS — INVOLUNTARY HOLDOVERS FROM PRIOR EMBODIMENTS

A small set of behaviors persist that cannot be accounted for by her current life and must be read as residues:

- The two-handed object cradle (amulet-handling).
- The squared-perpendicular stance (a court demon addressing a petitioner).
- The flat-interrogative intonation (a language not English).
- A specific way of tilting the head before delivering a curse-shaped sentence — chin down, eyes up — observable when she is angry on someone else's behalf even when no curse is being delivered.
- The bunny-recoil (Aud, the village, the rabbits left behind).
- A tendency, when seated alone, to fold the hands in the lap with the right thumb pressed into the left palm — a posture of waiting that she does not produce in any active social context. It is, plausibly, the posture of a thousand-year courtier between assignments.

These fossils do not diminish across the record. They are not unlearned; they are simply less and less often triggered as her life thickens around her. The last episode shows her with most of them still present and one new behavior emerging — a small, involuntary touch to her own collarbone when reassured, a self-soothing gesture she did not have in any prior era. The body, given enough time and enough being-loved, was beginning to make its own.

---

*End of Somatic Atlas. Cross-reference with Section 7 (Speech & Discourse Patterns) for verbal-somatic synchrony, and Section 12 (Decompensation Ladder) for the full state-transition map.*


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# Attachment & Relational Patterns

## 1. Origin of the Template: The Aud-Olaf Dyad

Every relational behavior on record traces, at root, to a single dyad: Aud and Olaf, somewhere on the Scandinavian coast in the latter half of the ninth century. The file has only fragments — her own retellings in "Selfless" and scattered references across the human period — but the fragments are diagnostically sufficient because they form the entire experiential basis on which all subsequent attachments are constructed.

What the dyad contained, by her own report: cohabitation; explicit verbal contract ("husband" in the customary sense of her village); domestic labor undertaken with literal pride; a shared household economy oriented around the rabbits she bred; and, crucially, no apparent peer network outside Olaf. She is mocked by villagers; she does not appear to have had girlfriends, sisters, or a confidante. Olaf is not just her partner; he is her entire social aperture. When he betrays her with "that troll," the loss is not only romantic — it is the loss of the only person who functioned as her interface with the species.

Three properties of this dyad become the template that runs, with eerie fidelity, through every subsequent relationship across 1,140 years:

1. **One-person attachment economy.** She does not distribute relational load. Whoever the primary bond is, that person is also the social proxy, the validator, the audience, and the regulator. There is no relational bench depth.
2. **Explicit verbal contracting.** The terms of the bond are stated aloud, often in registers that other parties find startling. She negotiates intimacy the way her village would negotiate a betrothal: in plain words, in front of witnesses where possible.
3. **Catastrophic-and-craftsmanlike rupture response.** Betrayal is not metabolized as grief; it is converted, with calm pride of work, into a precisely fitted punishment. The troll-curse is a piece of artisanal vengeance. So is, a thousand years later, the boils and lesions she very nearly inflicts on Xander.

This is not romance gone wrong. This is the only relational module she ever installed, running through different hardware.

## 2. Attachment Classification

The cleanest read is **disorganized attachment with an anxious-preoccupied surface in the late human period**, overlaid on what was probably an **avoidant-by-default** baseline through the demon centuries.

The disorganization shows up structurally: she approaches and repels in the same gesture. The proposal to Xander at the dance ("The Prom") is delivered as a transactional ultimatum — bond with me on these terms or I will be alone — which is simultaneously approach (she has chosen him as the one) and pre-emptive defense (the transactional frame lets her treat his eventual departure as breach-of-contract rather than personal rejection). The wedding-toast sequence in "Hells Bells" carries the same dual signal: she narrates Xander's flaws aloud, in public, while declaring undying love, as if to test in real time whether the bond can survive full disclosure. The structural feature of disorganized attachment — *seeking the figure who is also feared* — is observable each time she escalates intimacy with Xander and immediately produces a stress-marker (a rabbit reference, a death reference, a money-counting episode).

The anxious-preoccupied surface emerges in the late record: the constant verbal monitoring of the relationship, the demand for explicit affirmation ("Do you love me, Xander?" in registers that strike her partner as needy because they are), the inability to be alone in the apartment without narrating the absence. The avoidant baseline of the demon centuries — eleven hundred years of contracted, non-bonded contact with clients — is the dissociative defense she built on top of the original disorganization, and the defense to which she reverts under "Selfless"-magnitude stress.

## 3. Bonding: How the Subject Initiates Attachment

Her initiation pattern is highly stereotyped and consistent across all observed instances.

**Phase 1 — Selection by salience.** She does not date; she designates. Someone becomes proximal during a high-affect event (Xander during the Ascension prep; Spike during a mutually destabilized post-Buffy-resurrection period; Halfrek as a colleague during her second demon term) and is thereby tagged as a candidate. There is no observed instance of gradual interest accreting over neutral contact.

**Phase 2 — Verbal contracting in inappropriate register.** Within remarkably short windows of selection she will articulate the proposed terms aloud. "I'm going to be your girlfriend." "We will have intercourse." "I think it should be you and me." The phrasing strikes Sunnydale-natives as comic; in her ninth-century-village frame it is correct procedure. The function is twofold: it converts an ambiguous social field into a contract she can read, and it externalizes the bond so that breach can be adjudicated rather than felt.

**Phase 3 — Totalization.** Once accepted, the bond becomes the organizing axis of her week. She moves in, co-mingles finances, learns the other's preferences with the same focused intensity she once gave to vengeance contracts. Xander becomes her single primary referent — she narrates to him, plans by him, measures days by his presence. The Magic Box period is in many ways a deliberate construction of a *shared* domain (workplace adjacent to home, professional partnership with his friends, ritualized lunches) that allows the bond to saturate every available channel.

**Phase 4 — Surveillance for breach.** Underneath the totalization, a continuous, low-level monitoring runs. She tracks Xander's eye-movements toward other women, parses his tone for deception, asks frequency-questions about his exes. This is not pathological jealousy in the ordinary sense; it is the contract-holder auditing performance. The eleven-hundred-year demon career was a job spent listening for exactly this signal — the moment a partner deviates from terms — and that listening apparatus does not turn off.

## 4. Distrust: How the Subject Withholds and Tests

Distrust is, paradoxically, less visible than trust in her record, because she does not modulate. She is either inside the contract or outside it. While outside, she is briskly transactional — see her early interactions with Buffy and Willow ("you have what I need, here are my terms") which read as cold but are simply un-bonded. The category between stranger and intimate — "friendly acquaintance," "colleague one likes," "person one is getting to know" — is functionally empty for most of the record.

When she does test a bond, the tests are blunt and on the record rather than subtle and behavioral. She asks. She asks Xander whether he finds Buffy more attractive. She asks Willow whether Willow likes her. She asks Tara whether she is being weird. The directness reads as endearing or socially awkward depending on the audience, but is in fact a coping mechanism: she cannot read indirect signals reliably, so she substitutes explicit interrogation. Other people's relationships are conducted in a language she cannot parse without subtitles, and so she demands subtitles.

The one form of indirect testing she does perform is the **rabbit-mention** and the **money-count** under relational stress. When she is uncertain of Xander's commitment, the bunny-references spike and the till-receipts get audited twice. These are not tests of the partner; they are self-soothing rituals that also serve, unconsciously, as visible distress flares to which the partner can either respond (passing the test) or ignore (failing).

## 5. Betrayal: How the Subject Experiences and Inflicts It

Betrayal is the master category of her psychology, and it functions in two directions.

**Experienced betrayal.** She does not have a graded scale. Olaf-with-a-troll, Xander-at-the-altar, and D'Hoffryn-killing-Halfrek all register on the same instrument at the same magnitude. The response sequence is invariant:

1. *Brief catatonic shock.* Visible in the post-altar scene — she is found alone in the wedding dress, affect flat, narration of the event in past tense within minutes. This is not denial; it is the abrupt evacuation of an interior that had been entirely structured around the now-broken bond.
2. *Return to pre-formed institutional identity.* For Olaf-betrayal, this was the invention (with D'Hoffryn) of Anyanka. For Xander-betrayal, it was the re-assumption of Anyanka, the role already on the shelf. She does not freelance grief. She picks up a uniform.
3. *Crafted retaliation.* The retaliation is not rage-driven; it is workmanlike. She speaks of the boils-and-pestilence wish on Xander with the same craftsman's pride she once described the troll-curse — the satisfaction is in the fit between offense and consequence.
4. *Late, displaced collapse.* Days or weeks later, in the presence of someone who has not betrayed her, the actual grief arrives in disproportionate form — the bender in "Triangle" is the clearest archival instance; the breakdown after the Selfless massacre is another.

**Inflicted betrayal.** She has, by her own count, ruined or ended over a thousand lives across her demon career, and a non-trivial number of the marks were not the original offending men but bystanders or substitutes the wishers nominated. She does not experience this as betrayal of the victims because the contract frame mediates it: *the wisher consented; the target broke first; I am an instrument*. The collapse of this rationalization is the entire arc of "Selfless" — when Buffy confronts her with the human bodies in the fraternity house, the contract-frame fails for the first time and she is suddenly visible to herself as someone who has betrayed something larger.

She has never betrayed an attachment of her own, with one telling and important asymmetric exception: she sleeps with Spike in "Entropy" while still nominally tethered to Xander. The act is best read not as betrayal-by-her-standards but as a *self-administered* breach designed to formally end a bond she cannot otherwise unilaterally exit. She does not have a graceful departure protocol; she manufactures grounds.

## 6. Repair: How the Subject Reconciles

Repair is the weakest module in her relational repertoire and the one that develops most visibly across the record.

Early Anya cannot repair at all. A breach ends a bond, full stop, and either the bond is reconstituted from scratch (with new explicit terms) or it remains dead. There is no observed instance, through S4 and most of S5, of her successfully metabolizing a Xander-conflict into restored equilibrium without an external mediator (usually Willow or Tara translating between them).

Late Anya — S7 specifically — shows the beginnings of genuine repair behavior. With Xander after the wedding, the two of them achieve, by the end of the season, a careful working friendship that is not a reconstituted contract but something more fragile and more human: a tolerance of unresolved hurt held in common. She does not demand new terms; she sits with him in the unfixed. With Buffy after "Selfless," she accepts being judged without retaliating against the judge; this is, structurally, a first. With Andrew, of all people, she develops in the final episodes a peculiar bantering rapport that operates entirely on non-contractual, low-stakes affection. The capacity is late but real.

The repair mechanism, when it works, has three observable components: (a) explicit verbal acknowledgement of the breach, in her usual blunt register; (b) tolerance of the other person's failure to perform reciprocal acknowledgment on her schedule; (c) a return to shared task — folding laundry, counting inventory, training for the apocalypse — as the medium through which the bond is rebuilt without further verbal contracting. She repairs through *adjacent work*, not through processing talk.

## 7. Intimacy and Dependency

Her intimacy register is **physically uninhibited, emotionally lagging, verbally over-disclosed**. The flatness with which she discusses sex in the early period — frequency, mechanics, orgasm counts — is a body learning vocabulary it does not yet feel; by S6 the register shifts and she begins to speak of sex with Xander in more particular, less catalogic terms. The change is subtle and undertracked by other Scoobies, who continue to hear her as the same "Anya talking about her sex life again" she was in S4, but the file shows a real difference.

She is **deeply dependent** in the operational sense — she structures her days around the primary bond, becomes destabilized in its prolonged absence, and has not, in any observed window, demonstrated the capacity to live alone without a designated co-orbiting figure. The post-jilting period in S7 is the longest she sustains without a primary, and it is precisely during that period that she relapses to demon work; the relapse is best read as a substitute attachment to D'Hoffryn-as-father in the absence of a partner.

She masks this dependency aggressively. The capitalist rhetoric ("I have my own money, I have my own store, I am a self-sufficient American") is performed loudest during the periods of greatest underlying dependency. The mask is for herself as much as for the room.

## 8. The Differential Map of Her Bonds

A bond-by-bond accounting clarifies the template's variations.

**Olaf.** Primary template. One-and-only attachment of the human period; total; betrayed; converted to vengeance. Sets every parameter.

**D'Hoffryn.** The longest sustained relationship on record (~1,120 years intermittent). Quasi-paternal. Functions as the safe institutional identity she returns to under any catastrophic relational stress. He recruited her in her worst hour, gave her a role with explicit rules, and was the only continuous figure across her demon career. Her loyalty to him persists past his betrayal of her in "Selfless" — she does not seek vengeance on him for Halfrek's death, which is anomalous against her pattern and indicates the depth of the identification. He is, structurally, the father she did not have in the Aud period.

**Halfrek (Cecily).** Her only documented stable peer friendship of any duration. Same-species, same-vocation, same gender. The bond runs without the contractual anxiety that marks her cross-gender relationships, suggesting the template's pathology is sexual-romantic rather than relational in general. Halfrek's death is the only loss in the entire record that she grieves *as* grief, without converting to vengeance or institutional retreat.

**Xander.** The second iteration of the Olaf template, with the same beginning, the same middle, and almost the same end. The deviation — and it is a real deviation — is that the post-rupture period eventually yields something neither Aud nor Anyanka achieved: a working post-romantic affection. She does not curse him. She nearly does, and then doesn't. The non-curse is among the most important data points in the entire dossier; it is the first time the template was interrupted from inside.

**Buffy.** Transactional through S5; resented through S6 (Buffy as the figure who has Xander's regard in a way Anya cannot earn); equalized in S7 after "Selfless" through Buffy's choice to spare her. This is the only relationship in the record where the other party *broke* a Buffy-style obligation (to slay her) and Anya internalized the mercy as binding rather than as weakness. She dies in Buffy's army.

**Willow.** Wary peer relation. Anya is one of the very few characters who voices early skepticism about Willow's magical escalation; the bluntness is in-character but the underlying alertness is real, suggesting she recognizes in Willow a familiar profile (the wronged woman with disproportionate retaliatory capacity) and is unsettled by the mirror.

**Tara.** The most relaxed cross-gender-presenting bond in the file (Tara reads as safe along axes — not a romantic competitor, not a judge, not a contract-counterparty). Anya is observably gentler in scenes with Tara; her voice drops; she asks rather than declares. Tara's death registers in the record more than is generally noted — Anya's post-Tara behavior is markedly more subdued.

**Spike.** A one-off mutual-collapse encounter. Important structurally as the only sexual contact she has initiated as a *de-contracted* act; it is closer to her demon-period transactional sex than to her Xander-period intimacy, which is precisely the point — she retreated to an older operating mode to manufacture exit from the Xander bond.

**The Scoobies as collective.** Her late-period attachment to the group-as-such is the genuine novelty of her psychology. She has never before in 1,140 years belonged to a *plural* bond. The transition from one-person attachment economy to membership in a collective is the actual developmental achievement of her last year, and the speech to Andrew in "Empty Places" — that humans are the most amazing things, that she is going to find out what she is by being with them — is the clearest verbal record of that transition.

## 9. The Repeated Template, Stated Cleanly

Across every bond of consequence, the following sequence runs:

1. **Selection** by high-affect salience rather than gradual interest.
2. **Verbal contracting** in a register the counterparty finds startling.
3. **Totalization** into a single-axis relational economy.
4. **Surveillance** for breach, conducted in part through direct interrogation and in part through displaced rituals (bunnies, money).
5. **Breach** — either inflicted by the partner (Olaf, Xander, D'Hoffryn) or, in one case, manufactured by herself (Spike) to enable exit.
6. **Catastrophic rupture** — flat affect, retreat to pre-formed institutional identity, crafted retaliation.
7. **Late displaced grief** in the presence of a non-implicated third party.
8. **Eventually**, in the late record only, **partial repair** through adjacent shared work rather than verbal reconciliation.

The template is so stable that it can be used predictively: any bond she forms can be expected to follow this curve, with the developmental question being only how far along the curve she is able to interrupt it. By the time of her death, she had interrupted it once — with Xander, at the not-cursing — and had begun to construct, with the Scoobies as a whole, a relational form to which the template did not strictly apply.

## 10. The Final Configuration

At the moment of death she was held in three live bonds: Xander (post-romantic, working), Halfrek (recently severed by killing), and the Scooby collective (functional, plural, novel). She had no romantic primary. The template, denied its usual organizing figure, had been forced for nine months to operate without an axis — and she had survived it. The fact of that survival, more than anything else in the file, is the basis for the cautiously hopeful prognosis.

She died standing next to Andrew, fighting for people whose names she did not know, mid-quip. The death has no contractual frame. It is the first thing she ever did relationally that does not trace back, by any reading, to the Aud-Olaf dyad. It is, in the cold language of this section, the first observation in 1,140 years of an attachment behavior with no precedent in her template. The file closes on the only data point that breaks the pattern.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

## Preface: The Architecture Problem

The subject's defensive architecture cannot be read as a single coherent ego apparatus. It is, structurally, *three* defensive systems laid in stratigraphic sequence — Aud's pre-traumatic neurodivergent coping; Anyanka's institutionalized vocational dissociation; Anya's improvised, late-learned human repertoire — and what one observes at any given moment in the Sunnydale record (1998–2003) is the geological face where all three strata are visible at once. The lower strata never fully decommission. When she counts the register at the Magic Box, three women are counting: the Norse villager soothed by enumerable objects, the demon clerk drawing up a contract, and the new human who has been told that money is what humans care about and is determined not to fail at being human.

What follows ranks her defenses from the most primitive (closest to action, least mentalized, most ontological) to the most mature (symbolic, integrative, available only at the very end of the record). Within each, the operational signature is given — what it looks like in behavior, when it fires, what precipitates it, and what costs it incurs.

---

## Tier I — Primitive / Action-Level Defenses

### 1. Ontological Flight (Identity Substitution)

Her single most powerful and most catastrophic defense. Under intolerable affective load she does not modify her behavior, she modifies her *species*. The Aud→Anyanka transition in c. 880 CE is the founding instance: confronted with marital betrayal, she does not grieve, does not retaliate within the human frame, does not even retaliate within the magical frame and remain herself — she accepts a *new ontological category* (vengeance demon) that retrospectively reframes the wound as a recruitment opportunity. The Anya→Anyanka relapse of 2002 ("Hells Bells" → "Selfless") is the same operation performed in the same precipitating context: public romantic humiliation triggers not a coping response but a category change. D'Hoffryn's recruitment pitch works on her twice because the offer is, structurally, *the offer to not have to be the self that was hurt.*

This is the defense's signature: it converts unbearable interior states into a change of external metaphysical status. It is more primitive than dissociation because dissociation merely splits the self; ontological flight *replaces* it. The cost is total — every prior attachment, ethical commitment, and learned skill is voided in the transition.

### 2. Acting-Out via Vocational Vengeance

A near-cousin of the above, but operative *within* a given identity rather than across them. As Anyanka she translates every species of interior pain — her own and, professionally, others' — into a discrete, completable action with a clear victim, clear method, and clear receipt. She does not *feel* a thousand years of rage; she *bills* it, one contract at a time. The Russian uprising of 1905, the Mason-Dixon work, the Cordelia-wish, the frat-house slaughter in "Selfless": each is an externalization of grief into the world rather than its metabolism. This is acting-out in the strict sense — a procedure for not having an inner life by ensuring one's outer life is always too eventful to require one.

### 3. Splitting (Moral-Categorical Variant)

Her splitting is unusual in that it is not primarily *relational* (the same person alternately idealized and devalued) but *categorical*: classes of person are pre-sorted. Unfaithful men are a class; wronged women are a class; humans-she-has-bonded-to are a class; bunnies are a class. Once a target falls into a category the verdict is already rendered. This is why she can express genuine affection for individual men (Xander, Giles, Spike at moments) while operating an eleven-hundred-year career predicated on the categorical guilt of men: the categorical apparatus runs in parallel to the personal apparatus, neither updating the other. The defensive utility is enormous — she never has to feel ambivalence — and the cost is the moral imbecility that lets her cheerfully discuss past atrocities at brunch.

### 4. Somatic Discharge / Concretization of Affect

When she cannot contain an emotion she displaces it into the body and *names the body part.* The "I have a brain full of square roots" register, the wedding-toast threats, the literal description of orgasms as countable events, the rabbits-monologue in "Once More, with Feeling" where existential dread surfaces as zoological inventory — all are instances of the same operation: affect that cannot be tolerated symbolically is rerouted through a list of physical referents. This sits on top of the Aud-era literalism (see Tier IV) but functions defensively rather than merely cognitively in the human period.

---

## Tier II — Image-Distorting / Narcissistic-Range Defenses

### 5. Identification with the Aggressor

D'Hoffryn appeared at the lowest moment of her human life, named the wound a gift, and offered her membership in the class of people who inflict rather than receive. She accepted; she remained loyal to him for eleven centuries; she remains *psychologically* loyal to him even after he murders Halfrek in front of her in "Selfless." When she goes to him at the end of "Hells Bells," she is not negotiating — she is reporting for duty. This is identification with the aggressor at vocational scale: the figure who hurt her by recruiting her into a system of hurting is the figure she returns to whenever hurt. Her name itself is his gift — *Anyanka*, his bestowal — and the human shortening, *Anya*, preserves the lineage even when she is trying to escape it.

### 6. Reaction Formation (Late-Period Hyper-Humanity)

Loud capitalism, loud sexuality, loud celebration of mundane human pleasures. These are not appetites in the raw — they are *performances of appetite,* a person overshooting the target marked HUMAN because she does not know precisely where it is. The capitalism is the clearest case: she does not merely use money, she venerates it, sermonizes about it, treats the register as an altar. The defensive logic: if she can be conspicuously, demonstrably, *measurably* on the human side of the line, no one (including herself) can ask whether she belongs there. The cost is that every gesture of belonging reads to others as slightly off, which intensifies the underlying anxiety, which intensifies the performance.

### 7. Grandiose Role-Investiture

During the Anyanka period this is the dominant self-image — Patron Saint of Scorned Women, one-thousand-year veteran, master craftsperson. Stripped of the role in 1998, the grandiosity collapses entirely; she has *no* baseline self-regard to fall back on. (This is the key differential against narcissistic personality: the grandiosity is role-prescribed, not characterological. It evaporates the moment the role is taken away, leaving a frightened young woman registering for high school.) The defense reactivates briefly in 2002 when she resumes the title, and is again abandoned. It is a costume she can put on, not a face she wears.

---

## Tier III — Neurotic / Mental-Level Defenses

### 8. Intellectualization

The dominant mid-period defense. Affect is processed by being *converted into a topic*. Anxiety about death becomes a discourse on actuarial probability and bodily decay; anxiety about Xander becomes a discourse on engagement-ring valuation and wedding logistics; anxiety about her own past becomes a recitation of dates and locations. This is more sophisticated than the somatic discharge of Tier I because it operates symbolically, but it is still defensive: the symbol is held at arm's length, examined, *counted*, and never permitted to bleed into feeling. It is also the defense most useful to her social functioning — when she is intellectualizing she is at her most articulate and her most professionally competent.

### 9. Compulsive Mastery (Bounded Domains)

She seeks out, and creates, domains with clear edges and clear rules: bookkeeping, ritual mechanics, the inventory of the Magic Box, the procedural details of wedding planning. Inside such a domain she is formidable. The defensive function is that bounded mastery provides a *legible self* — at any moment she can answer the question "who am I right now?" with "the person who knows where every item in this shop is shelved." This compensates for the chronic instability of her larger self-concept. It also explains her panic when the boundary fails: when the Magic Box is destroyed, when the wedding is called off, when a ritual goes wrong, the loss is disproportionate to the object because the object was load-bearing for identity.

### 10. Displacement onto the Manageable Phobic Object

Leporiphobia functions, beyond its etiological role as fossil of the Aud period, as a *container.* A diffuse, oceanic dread of mortality and abandonment is far less manageable than a specific, locatable terror of small mammals. The phobia gives her something to point at when the larger thing surges — and the social environment cooperates by treating the rabbit-mentions as comic relief, which paradoxically validates the displacement (the real fear underneath is permitted to remain unspoken because the proxy is doing the work). The "Bunnies" verse in "Once More, with Feeling" is the defense made fully visible: existential terror routed entirely through one phobic image.

### 11. Undoing (Late, Partial)

Rare but present in the final season. She attempts to retract the vengeance on Ronnie in "Selfless," to revoke specific past acts, to *unpour* the wine. She fails at undoing — D'Hoffryn names the trade as impossible — but the attempt itself marks a defensive maturation. Earlier Anya would not have considered the operation; the wrong, once contracted, would have been final. The capacity to even desire undoing is the first sign that a symbolic, reversible inner world is becoming available to her.

---
