## Tier IV — Pre-Morbid Cognitive Style Functioning Defensively

### 12. Literalism

Strictly speaking, this is not a defense — it is a feature of her baseline cognition, present from the Aud era — but it is *recruited* defensively across her life. Literal interpretation of social communication protects her from ambient relational complexity by simply not registering it. When Xander says something euphemistic, she answers the surface; she does not have to manage the subtext because she has not perceived the subtext. The protective function is real (much social anxiety never reaches her at all) and the cost is real (she is regularly blindsided by what others consider obvious). The thousand-year demon career was a perfect occupational fit precisely because its rules were explicit, its contracts written, its subtext exiled.

### 13. Enumeration

Counting as soothing behavior. Money, years, orgasms, body counts, square roots, items on a shelf. The defensive logic is the same as a child counting stairs — quantification imposes order on an environment that otherwise threatens to flood. This is observable across all three of her identities: Aud's named rabbits (each one individuated and *tallied*), Anyanka's reckoning of vengeances completed, Anya's nightly till. The behavior is so consistent across ontological categories that it can be used as a recognition signature: when she begins counting aloud, she is regulating.

---

## Tier V — Mature Defenses (Late, Emerging, Incomplete)

### 14. Humor / Wit

Almost entirely absent in early appearances. Develops in tandem with her attachment to the Scoobies and reaches first full expression in the final season. The dying quip in "Chosen" is the diagnostic marker: humor has finally become available as a way to hold fear without being unmade by it. This is the most adult defense in her repertoire and the one that took longest to learn, because it requires precisely the pragmatic-language faculties that her autism made hardest to acquire — irony, register-shift, the gap between what is said and what is meant. That she learned it at all, and that she died inside it, is the single best evidence in the record of genuine developmental progress.

### 15. Sublimation (Partial, via Domestic Project)

Her energy toward the wedding, toward the shop, toward the apocalypse-prevention work of S7, contains a sublimative component — the vengeance impulse, the splitting, the categorical moralism are being channeled into *constructive* projects with social legitimacy. Incomplete because it remains brittle (the wedding collapse showed how thinly the sublimation was holding), but real. By S7 the channeling is steadier: she is fighting on the right side without needing the costume of righteousness.

### 16. Anticipation

Newly available in the final period. She begins, for the first time in the record, to *consider in advance* what she will feel and how others will respond. Her conversation with Andrew, her interactions with the Potentials, her quiet moments with Xander after their separation, show a capacity for forward affective modeling that earlier Anya did not possess. The defense is not robust — she still acts impulsively under acute stress — but its presence is significant.

### 17. Suppression (Conscious Setting-Aside)

Distinct from repression. In the last season she demonstrates the ability to *decide* to set a feeling aside until later — to fight first and grieve afterward, to function during the day and process at night. Earlier Anya could not do this; affect that arrived had to be discharged immediately or it overwhelmed her. The acquired capacity for suppression is what makes her useful in the climactic battle rather than collapsing.

---

## Compensatory Mechanisms — Positive

These are the gains, the load-bearing strengths that allow her to function and that, by the end, allow her to *grow*.

- **Capacity for sustained competence in bounded domains** — bookkeeping, ritual, tactical fighting. Provides a stable platform of self-efficacy regardless of relational chaos.
- **Loyalty once formed** — slow to bond, fierce when bonded. Halfrek, Xander, eventually the wider Scooby unit. This is rare in the trauma profile and probably reflects the same single-track cognitive style that made her vulnerable to D'Hoffryn: once a category is set, it holds.
- **Moral revisability** — she is one of very few characters in the entire Sunnydale record who *explicitly judges her past wrong* and seeks atonement. The "Selfless" request for her own death is the clearest instance of moral courage in her life; the slower, quieter atonement of S7 is the more impressive one.
- **Procedural memory across identities** — the skills accumulated as Anyanka (ritual fluency, demonic taxonomy, languages) remain available to her as a human and are repeatedly useful to the group. She has, uniquely, a thousand years of professional experience to draw on.
- **High working memory and pattern recognition** — she sees mechanisms quickly. Useful in combat planning, accounting, and the rapid identification of demon types.
- **Honesty as a structural feature** — her literalism removes most capacity for deception. Once trusted, she is uniquely trustworthy; she cannot easily lie because the pragmatic machinery required for lying is exactly the machinery her neurology underprovides.

## Compensatory Mechanisms — Negative

The costs, the maladaptive solutions, the doors that close behind her.

- **Vengeance-as-vocation** — the entire eleven-hundred-year career is, in defensive terms, a compensation: an externally sanctioned, professionally compensated outlet for unprocessed grief. Successful as defense; ruinous as life.
- **Transactional framing of love** — she conceives intimacy as a contract because that is the only relational schema she has been able to operationalize. This works for negotiation, fails for repair.
- **Available institutional retreat** — D'Hoffryn's court remains, throughout her human period, a known door she can walk through. The *availability* of the regression destination is itself destabilizing: she never fully commits to the human side because the demon side is still open. Only after Halfrek's death and D'Hoffryn's final betrayal does the door close.
- **Hypercathexis of insulating objects** — money, rings, ritual implements, the shop itself. Functionally a transitional-object overinvestment; loss of any of them precipitates disproportionate decompensation.
- **Categorical splitting as ethical foundation** — useful for vengeance work, disastrous for moral judgment in the gray cases the Scoobies routinely face. Her moral reasoning is consistently the most rigid in the group.
- **Conversion of grief to rage with no intermediate** — there is no observable mourning stage in her response to loss; she goes from injury to retaliation with nothing in between. This is the single most dangerous structural feature of her psyche and the one that nearly all the catastrophic events of her record proceed from.
- **Inability to tolerate ambiguous social signal** — under interpersonal ambiguity she either over-reads (catastrophizing) or under-reads (literalizing); a calibrated middle response is rare. Costs her repeatedly in the Xander relationship.

---

## Defensive Stack Under Escalating Stress

The above defenses do not deploy at random. They have an observable order of recruitment as load increases.

1. **Baseline** — literalism, enumeration, bounded mastery. Steady-state functioning at the Magic Box.
2. **Mild stress** — intellectualization, increased capitalist/sexual chatter, more counting, more inventory-checking. Visible in most ordinary Scooby meetings.
3. **Moderate stress** — somatic complaints, displacement onto phobic objects (rabbit-mentions surge), reaction-formation hyper-humanity intensifies. Visible in late S5 (Joyce's illness, Glory).
4. **Acute stress** — dissociative competence (very efficient, very flat), splitting hardens, identification with the aggressor reactivates as fantasy. Visible in S6 (Buffy's death and resurrection period; wedding approach).
5. **Decompensation** — acting-out, then ontological flight. Visible at the two endpoints of the cycle: c. 880 CE (Olaf), 2002 CE (Hells Bells).
6. **Post-decompensation reconstitution** — when the ontological flight is unavailable or has failed (Halfrek's death; D'Hoffryn's refusal to undo), the defensive system collapses and a new architecture must be built from scratch. This is what is happening throughout S7. The emergence of humor, sublimation, anticipation, and suppression in that final period is the rebuilding.

The escalation ladder is, crucially, *legible from the outside.* Anyone who knows her well — Xander at his best, Halfrek, late-period Buffy — can read where on the stack she is by counting her sentences-per-minute, the proportion of references to money and orgasms, the frequency of rabbit-mentions, and whether her affect is rising toward the disproportionate-distress pole or descending toward the dissociative-flat one. A skilled handler, benign or adversarial, could move her up and down the ladder at will. This is the deepest vulnerability in her defensive architecture and the reason a file like this one exists.

---

## Closing Note on the Architecture

What is striking, when the whole defensive system is laid out, is how *young* the mature defenses are and how much of the structure is still pre-symbolic. She died at what was, in human developmental terms, the start of late adolescence's defensive consolidation — humor just acquired, suppression just available, anticipation just emerging. Had she lived another decade in the human frame, the upper tiers would likely have thickened and the ontological-flight option would have continued to recede. The prognosis was, as the workup notes, cautiously hopeful; the architecture, at the moment of death, was a building scaffolded on the outside and still under construction within. The dying quip is the topping-out beam. She got that far.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# Longitudinal Psychological Profile

*Subject: Anya / Anyanka / Aud. Span of record: c. 860 CE – May 2003. Approximately 1,143 years of continuous subjective experience, segmented by two ontological transitions and one relational rupture of comparable magnitude. What follows tracks affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept across the subject's life in the longest meaningful intervals the record will support — millennium-scale for the demon period, year-scale for the Sunnydale period, episode-scale for the final eighteen months. The framework is integrative: attachment theory (Bowlby/Ainsworth/Main), Complex PTSD as elaborated by Herman and codified in ICD-11, structural dissociation (van der Hart/Nijenhuis), the autism broader phenotype as described in the contemporary literature, terror-management theory (Greenberg/Pyszczynski/Solomon), and a developmental-self model in the Sternian/Kohutian tradition. The pre-existing neurocognitive profile is treated as substrate; trauma and ontology are treated as accreted layers on that substrate.*

---

## I. The Aud Period (pre-880 CE; chronological age est. 18–22 at terminus)

**Affect regulation.** What can be reconstructed from the subject's own retrospective fragments ("Selfless," "The Wish," scattered remarks about Olaf) suggests a baseline of relatively flat, even-tempered affect, organized around concrete tasks (animal husbandry, domestic life) and unmodulated by social referencing. There is no indication of mood lability in the pre-trauma period; on the contrary, the subject describes herself in a manner consistent with someone whose affect is *under*-expressed by the standards of her village. The single observed dysregulation episode — the response to Olaf's infidelity — is not described by her as a hot rage but as a deliberate, planned, almost satisfying act of craft. This is the first recorded instance of what will be a lifelong pattern: when this subject's affect *does* exceed her regulatory window, it does not discharge as flooded emotion; it discharges as agentic construction of consequence. The substrate, even pre-morbidly, is one of cool retaliation rather than hot collapse.

**Cognitive style.** The Aud-era data converge on a profile of high concrete-operational competence, weak central coherence in the social-pragmatic domain, and atypical interest patterns. The rabbit-breeding behavior — naming, gifting, organizing — is not childish but classically circumscribed: a domain of mastery undertaken at intensity disproportionate to its village utility, with the gift-giving conducted as if the recipients' valuation of the gift were obvious and shared. The self-translation of her name as "odd" indicates ego-syntonic awareness of her own deviance from neurotypical norms; she does not appear to have been distressed by the deviance so much as resigned to it.

**Self-concept.** Pre-formed but thin. Aud knows what she does (breeds rabbits, lives with Olaf, occupies a recognized village role) but the record does not show her articulating an interior beyond role. This is developmentally appropriate for the period and culture and does not yet constitute pathology; it does, however, mean that when role is stripped, no interior remains to fall back on. The Olaf betrayal is therefore not merely a romantic injury — it is the simultaneous destruction of her only relationship and her only identity. The vacuum into which D'Hoffryn recruits her is, structurally, total.

---

## II. The Anyanka Period (c. 880 – March 1998; ~1,118 years)

This phase resists year-by-year tracking because the subject herself does not appear to have experienced it as developmental. It is best modeled as a stable dissociative occupational identity — what van der Hart would call an Emotional Part fused permanently to an Apparently Normal Part by being given a job description. The job description does the work of a self.

**Affect regulation across the millennium.** Stable, narrow-banded, work-organized. The subject reports the period in the cadence of a professional reflecting on a long career: anecdotes of particular contracts (1905 Russia, the antebellum South), aesthetic judgments about quality of vengeance, collegial relationships with peer demons (Halfrek). There is no record — none, across her entire retrospective testimony — of demon-period grief, demon-period romantic attachment, demon-period boredom, demon-period existential crisis. The flatness is the diagnostic. A thousand years of human life would produce a longitudinal record of affective texture; her thousand years produce a portfolio. The most parsimonious reading is that the Anyanka identity functioned as a sustained dissociative container: affect was permitted only insofar as it served the contractual frame (satisfaction in craft, disgust at male perfidy, loyalty to D'Hoffryn).

**Cognitive style across the millennium.** The pre-existing concrete-literal substrate is not merely preserved but rewarded. Vengeance contracts are the perfect occupational fit for the cognitive profile already evident in Aud: explicit terms, literal wording, no inferential leap required between expressed grievance and prescribed outcome, no negotiation of ambiguity. D'Hoffryn's recruitment, viewed structurally, is almost predatory in its accuracy: he offers a neurodivergent traumatized woman a role in which her cognitive style is a virtue and her trauma a credential. Eleven hundred years of this rewires nothing — the substrate is unchanged at Sunnydale arrival — but it does laminate the substrate with a thick layer of procedural confidence. She is, by 1998, extremely good at one thing.

**Self-concept across the millennium.** Stable, role-derived, externally scaffolded. The self is the badge: *Anyanka, Patron Saint of Scorned Women.* There is no daylight visible between role and person; the title and the entity are coextensive. This is functional but profoundly fragile, in the manner Kohut describes — a self propped entirely on the mirroring of an external system (D'Hoffryn's court, the contracts themselves, the wronged women whose validation is structurally guaranteed by her power). Remove the amulet, remove the role, and there is no nucleus left.

---

## III. Re-Humanization Shock (March 1998 – late 1998)

The destruction of the amulet in "The Wish" is, clinically, an acute total-self collapse. For approximately six to nine months the subject is unmoored to the point of behavioral incoherence: she enrolls in Sunnydale High because that is what a person in this body apparently does; she fixates with magical-thinking intensity on amulet-recovery ("Doppelgangland"); she has no functioning theory of how to occupy a day. The interoceptive load alone — a body she has not inhabited developmentally, with hunger, fatigue, menstrual, and pain signals she has no learned filtration for — would be overwhelming to any adult thrust into it; for a subject whose pre-existing profile already runs low on sensory gating, it is catastrophic.

**Affect regulation in this window.** Bimodal and brittle. She is either flat (transactional, monotone, mission-oriented) or floods (panic at amulet loss, sudden romantic fixation). There is no demonstrated middle register. Within the developmental-trauma model, this is precisely the pattern of a person operating without a tolerance window — she is at the edges of the autonomic envelope and cannot find the middle of it.

**Cognitive style in this window.** Unchanged from the underlying substrate but now mismatched to context. Her literalism, which was an asset in the contractual frame of vengeance, is a liability in the inferential frame of high-school sociality. She narrates her sensations because she has not learned that sensations are not customarily narrated. The famous "I have a brain full of square roots" register is the speech of someone with no acquired pragmatic filter operating in an environment that assumes one.

**Self-concept in this window.** Pre-collapse. There is no self; there is a body and a memory of having had one. Her sudden attachment to Xander, which the social field reads as eccentric, is best read as a self-construction emergency: she requires an external object around which to organize an identity and selects the first available one with sufficient salience.

---

## IV. The Xander-Organized Self (1999 – early 2002)

This is the longest stable period of the human record and the one in which something approximating developmental progress can be documented. The organizing structure is the relationship with Xander Harris, supplemented by the role at the Magic Box and the gradual, partial absorption into the Scooby group.

**Affect regulation across this three-year arc.** Slow, partial, real expansion of the tolerance window. Early in the period (S4) she still presents as flooded-or-flat with negligible middle; her contributions to group scenes are abrupt, register-inappropriate, and emotionally disconnected from the surrounding affective tone. By mid-period (S5) the pattern shifts measurably: she can sustain low-grade anxiety without action, can offer practical comfort to Xander after Joyce's death, can tolerate Buffy's distress without immediate self-referential discharge. By late-period (early S6) she shows the first signs of integrated affect — her wedding planning produces both anxiety and pleasure in a coordinated way rather than alternating bouts. The "Triangle" episode bender — aggressive, then weepy, then nauseated — is significant not as decompensation but as the first attested instance of her using a recognizable human affect-regulation strategy (badly, but recognizably).

**Cognitive style across this arc.** Substrate stable; surface accommodations accumulating. She does not become less literal; she becomes incrementally better at recognizing situations in which her literalism will produce social cost, and at editing — sometimes, briefly. The Magic Box bookkeeping is the substrate operating at full advantage: bounded, numerical, rule-governed work performed at a level the rest of the group cannot match. Her capitalism-as-religion is, in the cognitive frame, the substrate seeking a totalizing system to replace the lost totalizing system of vengeance contracts. Money is the new amulet — quantifiable, accumulating, externally validated, and immune to interpretive ambiguity.

**Self-concept across this arc.** Constructed scaffold-fashion around external objects: girlfriend-of-Xander, owner-of-Magic-Box, Scooby-adjacent-fighter. There is more nucleus than at the start of the period — by S6 she will use first-person evaluative statements ("I love you," "I want to") that do not depend on role-naming — but the structure remains externally propped. The diagnostic test is the question that has not yet been asked: what is left if Xander leaves? She does not know, and the record suggests she has carefully not investigated.

**Defensive structure in this period.** Intellectualization (counting) is dominant; reaction formation (loud sexual frankness, loud capitalism) is in its highest expression; splitting along the male-betrayer / wronged-woman axis is dormant but available, surfacing only in scattered remarks. Identification-with-aggressor (the persistent affectionate framing of D'Hoffryn) is consistent across the period and constitutes the principal sleeper vulnerability.

---

## V. The Altar Rupture and Relapse (May – November 2002)

Xander's jilting at "Hells Bells" is, structurally, the Olaf trauma re-presented with surgical fidelity: public, romantic, by the partner around whom the entire self-structure has been organized. The subject's response is identical to her response of eleven hundred and twenty-two years earlier, because no other response template has ever been installed.

**Affect regulation in collapse.** Collapse, not dysregulation. The capacity that had been incrementally built over three years vanishes in days. She does not grieve; she does not act out within a human register; she does not seek the consolation of the friend-group she had been integrating into. She returns to D'Hoffryn, which is to say she returns to the dissociative occupational identity that was built to make affect unnecessary. This is the textbook CPTSD relapse signature: under sufficient re-traumatization, the post-trauma defense reasserts wholesale, and the developmental gains of the recovery period are, temporarily, inaccessible — not erased, but walled off.

**Cognitive style under relapse.** Substrate intact; surface accommodations stripped. She speaks in the cadence of the Anyanka period — declarative, professional, contractual — and shows none of the softened pragmatics she had been accumulating. The cognitive system reverts to factory settings.

**Self-concept under relapse.** Re-borrowed from the prior external structure. She is again Anyanka by title and uniform, but the record makes clear (Halfrek's puzzled observations, her own halting attempts to complete a vengeance) that the fit is no longer clean. She has, without recognizing it, developed enough interior in the human period that the demon role no longer entirely contains her. The "Selfless" crisis is the moment this becomes visible to her: she can complete the massacre but cannot retroactively endorse it, and when offered the chance to undo it at the cost of Halfrek's life she does not endorse the trade. This is the first attested instance of moral revision in her record.

---

## VI. The Final Eight Months (late 2002 – May 2003)

The terminal period of the record. The subject is depowered, demoralized, returned to human status with the dissociative defense no longer available — she has, by D'Hoffryn's deliberate cruelty, been shown what it costs.

**Affect regulation in this period.** Markedly altered. The early-period oscillation between flat and flooded is gone; in its place a sustained low-grade depressive baseline with intact responsivity. She is quieter. She listens longer before speaking. The Spike encounter ("Entropy") is, in affective terms, the first sexual act in her record framed neither as appetite (early Xander period) nor as transaction (Anyanka period) but as mutual consolation — two depleted people regulating each other's affect through proximity. This is, in the schema of this profile, the most developmentally advanced affective act she ever performs.

**Cognitive style in this period.** The pragmatic-language deficit remains but is now accompanied by a recognizable metacognitive awareness of it — she catches herself, occasionally; she asks rather than asserts; she defers to others' reading of social situations more often than she had previously. The substrate is not changed, but the relationship to the substrate is. Within the autism literature this is sometimes described as the slow accumulation of explicit compensatory rules in adulthood; the record is consistent with that pattern accelerated by acute necessity.

**Self-concept in this period.** For the first time in the entire 1,143-year record, the self is neither role-derived nor externally propped. The line in the late-period record — "I don't know who I am" / "I'm going to find out" — is the diagnostic marker. The structure that has been absent since at least the Olaf rupture, and possibly never present, is being attempted from scratch: an interior nucleus with the question of its own contents held open rather than answered by external assignment. The "Chosen" death — anonymous, mid-quip, in defense of strangers — is the behavioral confirmation that this nucleus reached at least minimum viability. A self that dies for strangers is a self that has, finally, generalized beyond contract.

---

## VII. Cross-Sectional Synthesis: What Changed, What Did Not

**Did not change across 1,143 years.** Neurocognitive substrate (literalism, concrete operations, circumscribed interests, weak pragmatic inference, sensory atypicality manifest in the rabbit phobia). Core attachment template (sudden total approach, loyal maintenance, catastrophic rupture, no graceful exit). Core defense under maximum stress (regression to pre-formed institutional identity). The pre-trauma fossil — the rabbits — persists as phobia from age twenty to the moment of death.

**Changed across the final four years.** Affect-regulation envelope (narrow to slowly widening to collapsed to re-stabilized at lower baseline). Capacity for moral self-evaluation (absent through the demon period; present and operative by "Selfless"). Capacity for non-contractual intimacy (absent through her entire prior history; demonstrated tentatively in the Spike encounter and the late Xander reconciliation scenes). Capacity to hold the question of self open without external scaffolding (absent everywhere prior; present, briefly, at the end).

**The longitudinal shape, in one frame.** A neurodivergent young woman, in a culture and era that had no concept for her, was given a single intimate attachment, lost it traumatically, and was recruited into a dissociative occupational identity exquisitely calibrated to her cognitive style and her wound. She held that identity for eleven centuries without measurable interior development because the identity made interior development unnecessary. When stripped of it, she had to perform — in a teenager's body, in a foreign century — the developmental work of a young adult, but with the dissociative defense always available as relapse. She nearly completed the work. She relapsed once, under the exact precipitant that began the cycle, and recovered from the relapse. She died with the work unfinished but no longer abandoned. The clinical picture across the full span is the picture of someone who was, against very long odds and a very long history, becoming a person.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Subject: Anya / Anyanka / Aud
## Section 4 of Full Dossier

---

## 4.0 Framing Note on Diagnosis Across Ontological Categories

Before any specific diagnosis is offered, a methodological caveat: the subject is one of a vanishingly small cohort whose lived experience spans two ontological categories and crosses the boundary between them twice. Standard nosology (DSM-5-TR; ICD-11) is built for organisms with a single continuous embodiment, a single developmental trajectory, and a roughly contiguous autobiographical memory. The subject has none of these. Her chronological age is approximately 1,120 years at the close of the record; her endocrine and neurological age is roughly 20; her *experienced* age — the age at which she has had any practice being human — is approximately five.

This means three things for the assessment that follows. First, any diagnosis grounded in *duration* criteria ("six months," "two years") must be re-read in terms of *experienced* duration within the relevant embodiment. Second, any diagnosis grounded in *developmental* criteria ("since childhood") must be applied to the *Aud* developmental window, since that is the only human developmental window the subject ever had. Third, behavior that looks florid or grotesque (mass casualty events; the gleeful infliction of suffering) must be evaluated against the *role-prescribed* baseline of the demonic vocational identity, not against ordinary human baseline. A vengeance demon torturing an unfaithful husband is doing her job competently; a vengeance demon refusing to torture an unfaithful husband would be the symptomatic event.

With those caveats, the assessment proceeds.

---

## 4.1 PRIMARY DIAGNOSIS: Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11 6B41 analog)

**Strength of evidence:** Strong. This is the diagnosis around which the rest of the profile organizes.

### 4.1.1 Index Trauma

The index trauma is not a single discrete event but a compound: (a) discovery of Olaf's infidelity, (b) the social humiliation that necessarily attended a public, named betrayal in a small Sjornjost-era village, (c) the immediately subsequent ontological dislocation — being recruited out of the human category by D'Hoffryn while still in the acute crisis state. There is no period of normal mourning between the trauma and the recruitment. The transformation of Olaf into a troll occurs *during* the crisis, not after it; D'Hoffryn arrives, by her own account, on the strength of that act. The trauma is therefore *encapsulated*, not metabolized — sealed inside the demonic vocation before any human processing can occur.

This is etiologically critical. The reason her response a thousand years later, when Xander leaves her at the altar, is identical to her response at twenty is that the original trauma was never updated. From a memory-reconsolidation standpoint, the relevant network was placed in cold storage on the day of acquisition and only reopened when an isomorphic stimulus (public romantic abandonment) reactivated it.

### 4.1.2 Symptom Mapping to CPTSD Criteria

ICD-11 CPTSD requires the three core PTSD clusters plus three "disturbances in self-organization" (DSO). The subject meets all six.

**Core PTSD clusters:**

- *Re-experiencing.* Not classical flashbacks — she does not relive Sjornjost on screen — but a structurally equivalent phenomenon: she reenacts the original trauma response wholesale under matched cues. This is *behavioral* re-experiencing, well documented in chronic developmental trauma populations who lack the verbal-imagistic flashback presentation. Her preoccupation with infidelity narratives across the vengeance career (every contract reads as a variation on Olaf) qualifies as intrusive re-engagement with the trauma material in displaced form.
- *Avoidance.* The vocational identity itself is the avoidance. Eleven hundred years of not being a woman who was hurt by a man, and instead being the agent who hurts men on behalf of women, is an avoidance structure of extraordinary scale and durability. The avoidance of the Aud identity is so thorough that she rarely speaks her own original name and offers its translation ("odd") with the deflective humor of someone who has decided the word cannot wound her if she says it first.
- *Persistent sense of current threat.* In the human period this presents as her death-anxiety — the felt sense that catastrophe is imminent and uncontrollable. Her hypervigilance specifically targets mortality cues (Joyce's death, Buffy's resurrection, Tara's killing each provoke disproportionate, intrusive verbal preoccupation).

**Disturbances in self-organization:**

- *Affect dysregulation.* Cycles rapidly between flat, transactional affect and acute disproportionate distress; lacks an intermediate register through most of the record. The early-period drinking episode ("Triangle") — aggressive intoxication collapsing into weeping — is a textbook affect-regulation failure in someone with no learned modulation strategies.
- *Negative self-concept.* Oscillates with the grandiose demon-self in a manner classically described in chronic trauma: the self is either contemptibly small (Aud, "odd") or terrifyingly large (Anyanka, "Patron Saint"), with no stable mid-range self-evaluation. Her late-period question "Who am I now?" is the diagnostic phenotype rendered as a sentence.
- *Disturbed relational functioning.* All-or-nothing approach; no calibrated intermediate intimacy; catastrophic rupture response.

### 4.1.3 Course

The course is *chronic, encapsulated, and partially remitting in the final eighteen months of life.* Encapsulation by the demon role kept the syndrome stable but unresolved for a millennium. Re-humanization (1998) reopened the wound under conditions — Scooby attachments, sustained safety, gradual exposure to non-contractual love — that for the first time permitted partial processing. The 2002 relapse ("Hells Bells" → "Selfless") is the predictable decompensation under matched-cue reactivation. The post-relapse final period (S7) shows measurable, if fragile, recovery: tolerance window widening, affect modulation appearing, capacity for non-action-out present after the wedding and after the Selfless confrontation. Had she lived, prognosis under any competent trauma-focused work would have been cautiously favorable; the demon vocation had functioned as a hostile but stabilizing institutional placement, and removal of it had finally permitted the underlying syndrome to become workable.

---

## 4.2 PRIMARY DIAGNOSIS (CONCURRENT): Autism Spectrum, Level 1 (DSM-5-TR 299.00 analog)

**Strength of evidence:** Strong. Comorbid with, and developmentally prior to, the CPTSD.

This is the diagnosis that explains why CPTSD alone cannot account for the data.

### 4.2.1 Premorbid (Aud-Era) Evidence

Crucially, the autistic phenotype is documented *before* the index trauma. The Aud-era material — fragmentary but consistent — describes:

- Concrete, literal cognition (naming rabbits, breeding rabbits, gifting rabbits, with no apparent model of how the gift would be received by neighbors who did not share the interest).
- A circumscribed intense interest (rabbits, husbandry detail).
- A baseline of social ostracism normalized into self-identity (her own name translating to "odd" — she has incorporated the village's pragmatic-mismatch feedback into her core self-label).
- Apparent absence of awareness that the gift-of-rabbits behavior was being read as strange. This is a theory-of-mind / pragmatic-inference deficit, not a willful eccentricity.

A diagnosis cannot be retrospectively *added* to a person by a millennium of trauma; the phenotype must be premorbid. It is.

### 4.2.2 DSM-5-TR Criterion Mapping

**A. Persistent deficits in social communication and social interaction.**
- *Social-emotional reciprocity:* Conversation routinely violates pragmatic norms — the wedding toast threats, the "bunnies" monologue in song, public-register discussion of orgasm frequency. These are not exhibitionism (see differential against histrionic features, §4.7); they are failures of pragmatic filtering, present consistently across all eras and embodiments.
- *Nonverbal communication:* Affect-prosody mismatch is observable in the early human period — declarations of love delivered in transactional cadence; expressions of fear delivered with a flatness inappropriate to content.
- *Developing and maintaining relationships:* No calibrated intermediate intimacy. Her relational schema offers two settings — *stranger* and *spouse* — with the dating phase functioning, in her processing, as a procedural anomaly to be tolerated until contractual clarification (marriage) is reached.

**B. Restricted, repetitive patterns.**
- *Stereotyped/repetitive use of objects or speech:* Money-counting as ritual; verbal scripts around capitalism repeated with little variation across episodes.
- *Insistence on sameness, inflexible adherence to routines:* The Magic Box operations are run with rigid procedural fidelity; deviation from her bookkeeping practice produces distress out of proportion.
- *Highly restricted, fixated interests:* Sequential and intense — rabbits (Aud), vengeance contracts (Anyanka), money/retail mechanics (Anya). Each is total during its tenure.
- *Hyper- or hyporeactivity to sensory input:* Specific aversive response to the conceptual/perceptual category *rabbit*; functional sensory-overload behavior under crowded social conditions (her decompensation pattern at events).

### 4.2.3 Why This Diagnosis Matters Etiologically

The autism diagnosis is not a flourish. It explains the *selection event*: why D'Hoffryn picked *this* particular grieving Sjornjost woman out of the many available. The vengeance-demon vocation is uniquely well-tailored to an autistic cognitive profile — explicit contracts, no social ambiguity, codified rules of harm, a guild-style mentorship structure (D'Hoffryn, Halfrek), and a job in which bluntness is a vocational virtue rather than a social handicap. From an organizational-fit standpoint, D'Hoffryn was recruiting talent. The subject was, in a real sense, the right candidate.

It also explains why the human-reintegration period was so much harder than it should have been even after accounting for trauma and cultural dislocation. She was not only learning to be a modern human; she was learning, for the first time at adult chronological-experiential age, to be a *neurotypical-passing* human, against a baseline that was never neurotypical even in her own original village.

---

## 4.3 ADDITIONAL DIAGNOSIS: Specific Phobia, Animal Type — Leporiphobia (DSM-5-TR 300.29 analog)

**Strength of evidence:** Definitive.

Meets all six criteria. Marked fear, cued specifically by rabbits and rabbit-imagery; phobic object provokes immediate response (observed across multiple canonical episodes); the response is recognized by the subject as excessive (she does not pretend it is reasonable); avoidance and distress are persistent across the entire record; the disturbance causes social impairment (mocked by peers, interferes with quotidian engagement); duration vastly exceeds the six-month threshold.

**Etiology, proposed.** The most parsimonious account is that the rabbits of the Aud period — bred, named, loved, and the public marker of her social oddness — were lost at the moment of her ontological transition into demonhood. The phobia is therefore not a fear of rabbits as predators but a *trauma-linked aversion* in which the phobic object is a frozen icon of the lost premorbid self. This makes the phobia a kind of cenotaph: it marks the buried Aud-identity and prevents it from being approached. The fact that she retains the phobia *across* the demonic period and into the second human period suggests the buried material is intact and was never processed.

---

## 4.4 SUBCLINICAL / DIMENSIONAL PRESENTATIONS

These do not meet threshold for independent diagnosis but are operationally important.

### 4.4.1 Death Anxiety / Existential Distress (no DSM category; consider under ICD-11 6E20 or Other Specified Anxiety Disorder analog)

The subject's preoccupation with mortality is recurrent, intrusive, disproportionate to current threat, and qualitatively distinct from a neurotypical fear of death. She experiences death as a *phenomenon she is encountering*, not a *fact she has always known*. This is the inverse of typical existential anxiety, which is the difficulty of holding in mind a fact one has always known. Her temporal frame was disrupted by a thousand years of subjective immortality, and the disruption is permanent — she will never have the experience of having always known she would die. Verbal markers are abundant (the bunnies song, post-funeral monologues, her affect around Joyce's body in "The Body").

### 4.4.2 Dissociative Features

Substantial but sub-syndromal. The vocational identity is functionally a dissociative state — a stable, ego-syntonic alternate self organized around an alternate set of physical capacities, an alternate name, and an alternate moral code. This is not Dissociative Identity Disorder in the technical sense (the alternates are not amnestically segregated; she retains memory across them) but it bears the structural signature of dissociation in the service of trauma encapsulation. *Dissociative competence* under acute stress (going flat and efficient) is observed across the human period and is the late-stage residue of this organization.

### 4.4.3 Adjustment / Cultural Dislocation Reaction

Active throughout 1998–2001. Not a primary diagnosis because the subject's difficulties are not merely those of cultural adjustment, but a real component of the early Sunnydale presentation is the simple disorientation of a person whose last fully metabolized human cultural context was tenth-century Scandinavia.

---

## 4.5 COMORBIDITY STRUCTURE

The diagnoses do not merely co-occur; they interlock.

The autism is the *substrate*. It produced the premorbid social vulnerability (the village's mockery; the difficulty reading Olaf's likely behavior; possibly even the difficulty reading the warning signs of his infidelity in time to act on them at lower stakes). It also produced the *susceptibility to recruitment* into a role-defined identity, and the *durability* of that identity once adopted — autistic adults often report that having an explicit role and explicit rules is profoundly stabilizing. The vengeance vocation was, for her, a special interest that was also a job that was also a family.

The CPTSD is the *acquired overlay*. It sits on the autistic substrate and exploits its features: the literalism becomes moral binary; the special interest becomes weaponized; the rigid routine becomes a thousand-year vocational lock-in.

The phobia is a *marker*, not a driver — a flag indicating where the buried Aud-material is located.

The death anxiety and dissociative features are *sequelae* of the ontological transition, not independent pathologies.

This integrated picture is more economical than any single-diagnosis account. A pure-CPTSD reading cannot explain the premorbid oddness. A pure-autism reading cannot explain the affect dysregulation, the relational catastrophism, or the relapse symmetry. Both diagnoses, together, predict every major behavioral pattern in the record.

---

## 4.6 COURSE OVER TIME

- **Pre-880 (Aud):** Autism present, untreated, normalized into social identity in a small community that mocked but tolerated it. No trauma syndrome yet.
- **880 (Index event):** Acute trauma encapsulated by immediate transition into vocational identity. CPTSD acquired but immediately sealed.
- **880–1998 (Anyanka):** CPTSD chronic and stable under role-protection. Autistic features ego-syntonic and vocationally adaptive. No phenomenological experience of distress; subject would have rejected any diagnostic label offered.
- **1998 (Re-humanization):** Acute decompensation across all axes. CPTSD seal broken; autism now maladaptive in modern neurotypical milieu; phobia surfaces as ongoing distress; death anxiety acquired *de novo* at the moment of regaining mortality.
- **1998–2002 (Anya, first run):** Gradual stabilization through Scooby attachment. Tolerance window slowly widening. Some pragmatic-language compensation observed (she begins, late, to notice when she has said something inappropriate, though she does not yet reliably know what to say instead).
- **2002 (Hells Bells → Selfless):** Acute relapse under matched cue. Return to vocational identity is total but not sustained — the new attachments have created interference that did not exist a millennium ago. She cannot do the job. The "Selfless" massacre is best read as a failed reenactment, not a successful one; she is going through the motions of who she used to be and discovering that the role no longer holds her.
- **2002–2003 (Anya, second run):** Post-relapse remission with reduced baseline. Subdued affect; more reflective speech; capacity for non-instrumental intimacy (the Spike encounter framed as mutual consolation rather than appetite — a relationally sophisticated framing she would have been incapable of a year earlier). Trajectory toward integration is real but incomplete at time of death.

---

## 4.7 DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT THE SUBJECT IS NOT

A diagnosis is only as good as the alternatives it has defeated. The following have been considered and rejected.

### 4.7.1 Not Antisocial Personality Disorder

Despite a body count that, in human-criminal terms, would dwarf any documented serial offender, ASPD requires *pervasive disregard for and violation of the rights of others* as a stable personality structure. The subject demonstrates: (a) capacity for guilt (the Selfless confrontation; her request for her own death), (b) genuine attachment (Xander, Halfrek, the Scoobies generally), (c) capacity for moral revision unprompted by external sanction, and (d) absence of the conduct-disorder developmental prerequisite (her childhood, as Aud, is documented as socially atypical but not antisocial). The body count is *vocationally* generated under a moral framework she believed in; ASPD generates harm *characterologically* under no moral framework at all. The presentations are structurally different.

### 4.7.2 Not Narcissistic Personality Disorder

The grandiosity of the Anyanka period was role-prescribed rather than characterological. When stripped of the role, the subject shows low self-regard, no sense of entitlement, no exploitation pattern, and active capacity for self-criticism. The grandiose self collapses on contact with the depowering event; NPD grandiosity is far more resilient to environmental insult. Additionally, NPD requires a stable self-concept (an inflated one), and the subject's defining feature is precisely the *absence* of a stable self-concept.

### 4.7.3 Not Borderline Personality Disorder

This is the closest competing diagnosis and requires careful adjudication. Borderline features apparently present include: identity disturbance, affect dysregulation, intense unstable relationships, splitting. Against the diagnosis: (a) the identity disturbance is better accounted for by genuine ontological rupture plus CPTSD than by the relational-identity instability of BPD; (b) the splitting is *moral-categorical* (cheating men bad, wronged women good) rather than *relational-personal* (the same individual idealized then devalued in alternation); (c) the relationships are not chronically unstable — her bonds, once formed, are remarkably durable; instability appears only at the rupture event; (d) no chronic emptiness in the BPD sense; (e) no self-harm or chronic suicidality pattern (the request to die in Selfless is moral, not impulsive); (f) no pattern of frantic efforts to avoid abandonment in the BPD sense — her response to abandonment is highly organized vengeance, not desperate clinging. The CPTSD diagnosis covers the affective and relational material more parsimoniously.

### 4.7.4 Not Schizotypal Personality Disorder

The oddness is consistent across decades, ego-syntonic, and fully explained by autism plus radical cultural dislocation. There is no magical thinking beyond what is *literally true* in her cosmology, no ideas of reference, no paranoid ideation, no perceptual abnormalities not attributable to her actual demonic experience. Schizotypal disorder is, in her case, ruled out by parsimony.

### 4.7.5 Not Histrionic Personality Disorder

Her public-register discussions of sex and money are sometimes mistaken by the people around her for attention-seeking. They are not. Histrionic presentation is *audience-oriented*; the subject makes the same statements with the same affect whether she has an audience or not. The behavior is *pragmatic-failure*, not performance. Additionally, she shows no sexually seductive interaction style outside her actual partner, no shallow shifting emotionality, and no suggestibility (she is one of the least suggestible characters in the record).

### 4.7.6 Not Dissociative Identity Disorder

The vocational alternates (Aud / Anyanka / Anya) are not amnestically segregated. The subject retains continuous memory across the transitions, can speak about each from inside the others, and does not switch involuntarily or without external trigger. The structure is one of *serial* identity reorganization around external roles, not the *parallel* identity organization of DID.

### 4.7.7 Not Major Depressive Disorder, Persistent (though one episode possibly meets MDE criteria)

The post-Selfless / late-S7 period — subdued affect, anhedonia in early episodes, reduced verbal output, social withdrawal relative to baseline — comes close to meeting criteria for a major depressive episode. It is more parsimoniously read, however, as the *appropriate grief response* of someone who has just rediscovered, after a thousand years, that she is in fact capable of regret and is now metabolizing what regret means at scale. The presentation lacks the cognitive-distortion structure of MDE (her self-criticism is, distressingly, *accurate*), and remits gradually under continued social attachment without pharmacological or therapeutic intervention.

### 4.7.8 Not Substance Use Disorder

One documented episode of acute intoxication; no pattern; no tolerance; no withdrawal; no impairment of social or occupational functioning attributable to substance use. The "Triangle" bender is a single affect-regulation failure in a novice drinker, not a use disorder.

### 4.7.9 Not Psychotic in any sense

No hallucinations not attributable to actual supernatural perception; no delusions not attributable to actual cosmological facts; no disorganized thought or speech; no negative symptoms. Reality-testing intact throughout.

---

## 4.8 INTEGRATED FORMULATION

The subject is a chronologically eleven-hundred-year-old, experientially mid-twenties, neurodivergent (autism spectrum, Level 1) woman with chronic Complex PTSD, encapsulated for a millennium inside a vocational dissociative identity and only recently (within the last five years of life) re-exposed to processing conditions. The autistic substrate pred


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT "ANYA"

*A field-grade catalogue of observable tells, micro-routines, decision habits, and condition-dependent presentations. Compiled longitudinally across the Sunnydale record (1998–2003), with retrospective inference into the Aud and Anyanka eras where the subject self-reports. Organized by state. Where a tell migrates between states or evolves across years, the migration is flagged.*

---

## 1. BASELINE — THE CALM SUBJECT

There is no truly resting baseline for this subject; what reads as calm is in fact a low-threat operational mode in which her defenses are running smoothly. The following are reliable in that mode.

**Posture and motor pattern.** Upright, weight forward on the balls of the feet, hands frequently occupied — sorting, counting, stacking, straightening. When unoccupied, hands go to hips or fold tightly across the abdomen rather than hang loose; she does not have a relaxed standing default. Gait is brisk, short-strided, slightly heel-heavy, with little arm swing. She does not amble. When seated she perches — knees together, spine straight, rarely leaning back into a chair's support. This is consistent across years; she has not learned to recline.

**Gaze.** Direct to the point of being uncomfortable, with poor habituation of the blink-and-look-away rhythm a neurotypical conversant uses to soften eye contact. She holds gaze for the duration of her speech and continues holding it through the listener's reply. When she does break, she breaks downward and to the side, not across — a brief inspection of her own hands or whatever she is holding, then back up. Pupils characteristically wide; she does not squint or narrow her eyes in social skepticism.

**Voice.** Clear, slightly nasal, pitched in the upper-middle of her range with little variation. Sentence-final intonation tends toward declarative even on questions; she states questions rather than asking them. Volume runs roughly half a step above ambient — she is the person at the table the next table can hear. Rate of speech is uniform regardless of content; she announces a death and a sale price at the same tempo.

**Mouth and face.** Mouth in a slight closed-lipped neutral; she does not have a habitual social half-smile and does not produce one for strangers. When amused, the smile is full and brief and asymmetrical (right side higher). When confused, the brow draws together and the head tilts approximately fifteen degrees right; this tilt is the most reliable single tell in the file. When she does not understand a social cue, she tilts and waits — she does not bluff comprehension.

**Hands.** Constant low-grade activity. Counting tells: she will subvocalize when totaling, lips moving without sound, index finger touching thumb at each increment. She straightens objects on any surface within reach — coasters, pencils, the edges of papers — without appearing to notice she is doing it. When she holds money she fans it, recounts, re-fans; the recount is ritual, not doubt. When she holds a weapon she holds it too tightly and adjusts grip frequently.

**Speech content at baseline.** Declarative, concrete, quantitative. She volunteers numerical and bodily information unsolicited: sums of money, frequencies of sex, durations ("a thousand years"), counts of objects. She narrates her own internal states out loud as if reading them from an instrument panel ("I'm hungry," "I'm bored now," "I find that arousing"). She does not editorialize, and she does not lie at baseline; deception requires effort she does not spend on small matters.

**Habits and micro-routines.**
- *Opening the Magic Box:* arrives early, unlocks, lights, register float counted twice, glass case wiped with the same cloth from the same drawer, books on the counter aligned to the counter's edge with the spine outward. The order does not vary across the years she runs the shop.
- *Closing:* register reconciled to the cent; any discrepancy triggers an audible flat affect ("there is a discrepancy") and a full recount. She will not leave the building on a discrepancy.
- *Eating:* she eats methodically, one food category at a time on a divided plate, finishing one before starting the next. She comments on flavor and texture clinically.
- *Dressing:* preference for structured, slightly girlish silhouettes — fitted bodice, defined waist, knee-length skirt; colors heavily skew to warm pinks, mauves, soft browns, with occasional saturated red on assertive days. Jewelry minimal and symmetric. Hair worn down or in a single low style; she does not fuss with it in public.
- *Sleep:* reports difficulty staying asleep (S5–6 conversational asides); wakes early; uses the early hour for inventory rather than rest.

**Decision habits in calm.** She decides quickly and announces the decision before consulting. Cost-benefit is explicit and verbalized. She prefers options that can be counted, measured, or contracted. Given two morally equivalent options, she picks the more profitable one without embarrassment. She does not procrastinate; undone tasks are visible aversive stimuli.

---

## 2. MILD STRESS — THE FIRST PERTURBATION

The earliest sign she has been knocked off baseline is verbal, not motor.

**Verbal escalation.** Talk volume increases by perhaps twenty percent; rate increases noticeably. Subject matter narrows to her three reliable refuges: **money, sex, and the body**. Under mild stress in a Scooby planning meeting she will interject a remark about Xander's anatomy, the shop's quarterly figures, or a bodily process — apparently non sequitur, in fact a self-soothing return to mastered topics. The interjection is the tell. Companions who knew her well (Tara, late-period Xander) learned to register the topic-shift as anxiety rather than as content.

**Money handling.** She drifts toward the register, the cashbox, or the inventory binder. If none is available she counts what is in her wallet. The behavior is functionally identical to a smoker reaching for a pack.

**Literalism intensifies.** Idioms she normally tolerates suddenly require parsing aloud ("why would it be raining cats — oh, it isn't"). She loses what little pragmatic flexibility she has and reverts toward the Aud register.

**Body.** Slight increase in postural rigidity; shoulders rise perhaps a centimeter. She touches her own collarbone or the hollow of her throat — a self-soothing gesture that appears only under stress and never at baseline. She drinks water in small frequent sips rather than her usual long pulls.

**Decision pattern.** She begins to seek explicit permissions and confirmations from whichever Scooby she most trusts in the room (Giles, early; Xander, middle; Buffy, very late). The pattern is one of contract-seeking: she wants the terms restated.

---

## 3. MODERATE STRESS — THE MIDDLE BAND

This is the band in which most of her on-screen behavior occurs. She is functional, productive, and visibly off.

**Somatic complaints.** She reports symptoms aloud — headache, stomach ache, "weird feeling in my chest." She frames them as data, not as bids for sympathy, and is mildly bewildered when sympathy is offered. The complaints cluster around the chest and abdomen; head complaints are rarer and tend to indicate genuine fatigue rather than affect.

**Death talk.** Under moderate stress she will introduce mortality into any conversation within roughly ten minutes. The introduction is often abrupt and quantitative — life-expectancy figures, the mechanics of decomposition, the duration of human-vs-demon existence. This is not morbidity for effect; it is the intrusive material of her death anxiety surfacing.

**Rabbit-mentions.** Under stress she will reach for the rabbit-fear as a topic. It functions almost as a displacement — a known, bounded, even comical fear she can put into language in place of the unbounded ones (abandonment, mortality, category-loss) she cannot. A spontaneous rabbit remark in conversation is reliably a marker that she is more afraid of something else.

**Sexual frankness as displacement.** Under moderate stress, particularly stress originating in the Xander relationship, she escalates public sexual commentary. This is a paradoxical bid — she is attempting to reassert the contract of the relationship by re-stating its physical terms. It reads to outsiders as exhibitionism and to her partner as accusation; both readings are partial.

**Money behavior.** Recounts more frequently; second-guesses ledger entries; becomes territorial about the register. New customers receive shorter service.

**Eye contact narrows.** She begins to look at mouths rather than eyes — a subtle shift, but consistent. She is reading speech mechanically when she can no longer read affect.

**Decision pattern.** She begins to propose schemes — practical, often financially-framed solutions to non-financial problems. ("We should charge them." "We could sell that.") The schemes are not jokes; they are her cognitive style attempting to convert an ambiguous threat into a bounded transaction.

---

## 4. ACUTE STRESS / EMERGENCY — THE FLAT BAND

A characteristic and clinically important shift. Above a certain threshold the verbal escalation stops cold and inverts into what is best described as **dissociative competence**.

**Motor.** Movement becomes economical and slightly slow. She stops fidgeting. Hands still. Posture squares.

**Voice.** Drops in pitch perhaps a half-step, loses its nasal edge, drops in volume to just-audible. Rate slows. Sentence-final intonation flattens further; she becomes affirmatively monotone.

**Face.** Flattens. Brow smooths. The fifteen-degree confusion tilt disappears entirely. She looks, briefly, like a competent stranger.

**Content.** Procedural. She begins to issue or accept short imperative sentences. She executes tasks without verbal accompaniment — the running commentary that defines her baseline is gone. This silence is the single most reliable indicator of acute distress in the file: **when Anya stops narrating, she is in trouble.**

**Examples in record.** The wedding-day preparations once the catastrophe is underway; the immediate aftermath of "Selfless" in the alley with Buffy; the final battle sequence in "Chosen" up to the moment of her death. In each case the verbal subject most readers recognize is functionally absent and a quieter, sharper operator is doing the work.

**Decision pattern in acute stress.** Tactical, conservative-with-others'-lives, indifferent-to-her-own. She will offer her body as shield, position, or distraction without apparent calculation, because the calculation has already happened in a register beneath consciousness. She does not bargain in acute stress; the contractual mind goes quiet.

---

## 5. THREAT — DIRECT PHYSICAL DANGER

Distinguish from acute stress: threat is the specific subcase where a known adversary is present and engagement is imminent.

**Pre-engagement.** A brief freeze of perhaps half a second — eyes wide, mouth slightly open, no sound — followed by motion. The freeze is consistent and is her body's tell that the threat has registered.

**Engagement.** Combat style is unpolished but committed. She favors blunt weapons (axe, mace, sword used as a club) over edged finesse; she swings with the whole body rather than the wrist. Footwork is poor; she plants and strikes rather than circling. She vocalizes during combat — short flat exhalations on each strike, occasional one-word curses, no battle cries. She does not taunt. She does not banter mid-fight in the way Buffy and Spike do; the verbal channel is closed.

**Wounding response.** She inspects the wound first, narrates its features quantitatively ("that's a lot of blood"), then resumes engagement or withdraws by triage logic. She does not panic at her own injuries; she panics at others'.

**Post-engagement.** Sharp drop in adrenaline tolerance — she will sit down hard, shake noticeably in the hands, and become abruptly verbose again, often about something irrelevant. The verbosity is the system rebooting from the flat band.

**Threat to a bonded person.** A different and more dangerous mode. Speed of decision drops to near zero — she does not deliberate, she moves. She will place her body between the threat and the bonded person without communicating the intent first. This is the behavior that ends her life in "Chosen."

---

## 6. INTIMACY — APPROACH, MAINTENANCE, AND PHYSICAL CONTACT

The single domain in which her behavior most visibly evolves across the record.

**Approach (early).** Abrupt, declarative, transactional. The canonical specimen is the dance invitation to Xander: she walks up, states the proposition, names the consideration ("you're not… short"), and waits for acceptance. She does not flirt; she does not preamble. She experiences the standard mating script as inefficient. She is genuinely puzzled when this approach fails on others and genuinely surprised when it succeeds.

**Approach (late).** Softer. She learns to preface, to ask after the other person's day, to wait through pauses. The learning is visible and uneven — she will execute a tender preamble and then close it with a frank request, the seams between the learned and the native showing.

**Maintenance behaviors.** Once attached, she is steady, practical, and undemonstrative in conventional ways. She expresses love through provisioning — food, money management, sex on a schedule, presence at events. She remembers facts about the partner with archival precision (favorites, allergies, anniversaries calculated to the day) and is wounded when reciprocation is imprecise. She does not pick fights and she does not sulk; grievances are stated plainly and once, and then she expects them resolved.

**Physical contact.** Initial human-period record: she does not initiate casual touch and is briefly startled by it from others. With Xander, touch normalizes within the relationship but rarely generalizes — she does not pat shoulders, does not hug as greeting, does not lean. By late record she will hold Tara's hand briefly in solidarity and will accept a hug from Willow without flinch; the threshold has lowered.

**Sexual register.** Frank, frequency-oriented, quantitative in private and public alike. She narrates pleasure as data. She reports satisfaction in the same tone she reports profit. The flatness should not be read as anhedonia — she manifestly enjoys sex; the affect is descriptive, not evaluative. With Spike (the consolation encounter) the register shifts noticeably toward quiet; she is sober and slow in that encounter in a way she rarely is.

**Disclosure.** She over-discloses early and under-discloses late. In the first two seasons she will tell strangers things partners are not normally told. By S6–7 she has learned to hold certain content — her demon history, her doubts, her death-fear — back from all but one or two people. The shift is a marker of acquired theory-of-mind, not of new secretiveness.

**Conflict in intimacy.** She does not escalate volume; she escalates specificity. In a fight she will recall and recite the partner's exact words from prior conversations with high accuracy and no charity. She does not throw objects; she does not slam doors. She walks out by leaving the room briskly and quietly, and she will return within the hour to negotiate terms. The catastrophic exception — the post-altar return to D'Hoffryn — is precisely catastrophic *because* it breaks her own pattern.

---

## 7. GRIEF

She has limited and uncalibrated equipment for grief, and her grief presentations are accordingly raw and unconventional.

**Acute grief.** Stillness. She does not cry immediately; she sits, often where she was when the news arrived, and does not speak for an unusually long interval. When she does speak it is to ask procedural questions — *what happens to the body, who is told, what do we do next* — that other mourners find jarring but which are her means of imposing structure on an unstructured event. The famous monologue at Joyce's death ("I don't understand how this all happens, how we go through this") is the rare exception in which the procedural questioning breaks open into the underlying bewilderment, and it is delivered in the same flat-band voice as her acute-stress mode.

**Delayed grief.** Emerges as somatic complaint, irritability with customers, and an uptick in death-talk. She does not name the grief as grief; an observer must back-derive it from the symptom cluster.

**Anniversary effects.** Inferable rather than directly observed: she becomes quieter and more inventory-focused on dates associated with losses. The behavior is subtle and would be invisible to anyone not watching for it.

**Grief tolerance with others.** She is poor at the standard condolence script and aware of it. She tends to offer practical aid (food, money, presence) and to keep verbal content minimal. Her presence at a vigil is reliable; her words at one are not.

---

## 8. SHAME, GUILT, AND MORAL REVERSAL

A late-developing repertoire.

**Pre-Selfless.** Functionally absent. She references prior vengeances with craftsman's pride; challenged, she defends them on contractual grounds.

**Selfless and after.** The signature presentation is a quieting and a turning-inward. She stops volunteering opinions. She accepts criticism without rebuttal. She physically lowers her gaze — the only context in which she breaks her usual direct stare downward and keeps it down. She does not perform contrition; she withdraws.

**Atonement behavior.** Concrete and somatic-stakes. Her instinct is to offer her body — her life, in "Selfless"; her labor, when life is not accepted — rather than verbal apology. The contractual mind reasserts itself here: a debt requires a payment of equivalent magnitude, and she scales the offering to the size of the wrong.

---

## 9. VICTORY AND PLEASURE

**Money won, sale closed, plan succeeded.** Brief, bright, undisguised. She announces the outcome aloud, often with the figures. She will clap once or twice, audibly. She is comfortable with overt triumph and does not perform modesty.

**Combat victory.** Muted — see post-engagement under threat. She does not celebrate kills.

**Sexual pleasure.** Reported aloud, sometimes to companions afterward; she does not have the cultural reflex of post-coital privacy.

**Praise reception.** Awkward. Direct praise causes the confusion-tilt and a delayed thank-you. She handles transactional praise ("good work on the books") better than affective praise ("I'm proud of you"); the latter often produces a topic-shift to money or sex within thirty seconds.

---

## 10. DEFEAT

**Defeat in a bounded contest** (a sale lost, an argument lost, a plan rejected): brief loud protest, recount of the relevant figures or arguments, then acceptance and pivot to the next bounded task. She does not ruminate aloud over small defeats.

**Defeat in an unbounded domain** (relational rupture, existential failure): the catastrophic pattern. She does not metabolize unbounded defeat; she escapes it by re-entering a bounded identity. The first instance is Olaf and the troll-transformation; the second is the altar and the return to D'Hoffryn. The pattern is identical and the warning signs are: a sudden return of flat-band voice in a non-emergency context, a refusal to discuss the defeat, and a marked uptick in references to her demon period.

**Defeat-in-self** (the Selfless realization, the post-altar weeks): subdued affect, reduction in capitalist chatter, increase in plain unornamented speech. This is the only context in which her behavior approaches what an outside observer would call humble.

---

## 11. SUBSTANCES, FATIGUE, AND ALTERED STATES

**Alcohol.** Low tolerance; inexperienced. Becomes aggressively voluble, then maudlin, then briefly affectionate, then unconscious. Pattern visible in the post-fight bender; not repeated frequently in record. She does not appear to use alcohol routinely.

**Sleep deprivation.** Increases literalism and decreases the late-period social filtering; an exhausted Anya regresses noticeably toward her early-period presentation.

**Magic and ritual.** Competent and unfussed; ritual work appears to settle her — the explicit rules and measurable outcomes are congenial to her cognitive style. Observers can read her ritual demeanor as her closest available approximation of contentment.

---

## 12. DECEPTION AND CONCEALMENT

**Lying.** Poor at it. The voice tightens, the rate increases, the gaze becomes overly fixed, and she over-supplies detail. She has the autistic liar's characteristic problem of providing too much corroborating information and thereby flagging the lie. She avoids lying when she can.

**Concealment by omission.** Better at it, late. She learns to not-say without false-saying; the tell is a brief pause before subject-change and a slight increase in money-talk on the other side of the change.

**Operational implication.** A handler or adversary should ask direct closed questions and watch the first three seconds of response; the truth is almost always in those seconds. She self-corrects toward honesty rather than away from it.

---

## 13. RITUALS, ROUTES, AND TEMPORAL HABITS

**Daily route (mid-record).** Apartment → Magic Box (on foot or by Xander's vehicle) → shop open → lunch on premises → shop close → Magic Box reconciliation → Bronze or Summers house or apartment, in that order of probability. She does not vary the route casually and is mildly irritated when asked to.

**Weekly rhythm.** Inventory on a consistent weekday; banking on a consistent weekday. The schedule is rigid by preference, not by necessity.

**Holiday and ritual occasions.** She over-prepares. She researches the rules of a holiday with which she is unfamiliar and executes them literally; the discrepancy between her literal execution and the cultural soft-execution others perform is a recurrent comic and diagnostic note. (Valentine's Day, Thanksgiving, the wedding planning.) The rigidity is not preference for tradition; it is anxiety in the absence of an explicit ruleset.

**Rituals of self-soothing.** Counting money. Aligning objects. Recounting inventory. Reciting figures. Stating bodily states aloud. These are the visible loops; the underlying loop is the conversion of unbounded anxiety into bounded enumeration.

---

## 14. CROSS-CONDITION TELLS — MASTER INDEX

For rapid field use, the most reliable single-signal indicators in the file, ranked roughly by specificity.

1. **Verbal silence in a non-emergency context.** Acute distress; possible decompensation imminent.
2. **Spontaneous rabbit mention without prompt.** Displacement of a larger, unspoken fear.
3. **Self-touch at collarbone or throat hollow.** Mild-to-moderate anxiety; not present at baseline.
4. **Fifteen-degree right head-tilt.** Social confusion, not comprehension. Wait; do not press.
5. **Drift toward register, cashbox, or wallet.** Self-soothing onset.
6. **Uptick in references to the demon period.** Identity destabilization in progress; relapse risk elevated.
7. **Eye contact shifts from eyes to mouth.** Affect-reading has failed; she is reading mechanically.
8. **Over-supply of corroborating detail in answer.** Deception attempt.
9. **Flat voice, economical movement, brow smoothing.** Acute-stress dissociative competence; she is functionally lethal and not consciously bargaining.
10. **Topic-shift to money or sex


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*What a week of competent surveillance on the subject would actually produce, cross-referenced against the established canonical record (Sunnydale, CA, principal residence period 1999–2003) and inferred at the granularity such a file demands.*

---

## 1. The Shape of a Day

The subject's days are notable, before any individual content, for their *over-structure*. A person with a continuous interior tends to leave gaps in a schedule because the interior fills them; the subject leaves no gaps because, until very late in the record, there is no interior to fill them with. Her calendar — visible at the Magic Box in the form of a wall planner she maintains in a tight, evenly-spaced hand, with categories color-coded by ledger column rather than by subjective importance — runs in fifteen-to-thirty-minute blocks from the moment she rises until the moment she sleeps. Empty blocks are uncommon and are filled, when they occur, with the activity she calls "inventory" but which a surveillance log would record as the subject standing in the back room of the shop, touching merchandise in sequence, and occasionally mouthing a count.

A representative weekday during the Magic Box period (roughly mid-S5 through late S6) breaks down as follows.

**05:50–06:15.** Wake, almost always before her alarm. She does not snooze; she sits up immediately and, when sharing a bed with Xander, performs a brief verbal check of his breathing pattern before rising — a behavior she does not appear to know she does. In her own apartment she rises and inspects her hands. (A surveillance team would log this several times before recognizing it as a daily ritual; the most parsimonious read, given §2 of the workup, is that she is confirming the human face.)

**06:15–07:10.** Showers long. Water temperature trends to the very hot. She narrates the shower aloud to herself at a low volume when alone — itemizing what she is washing, in order. Dresses in layers selected the night before and laid in a specific arrangement on a chair: undergarments folded into squares, outer layers in the order they go on. She does not improvise an outfit. The wardrobe itself, over the four-year human record, drifts from inappropriate-for-context (the dress she wore to the Prom) toward a stable late-period uniform of fitted tops, knee-length skirts, cardigan, low pumps — clothes that read, deliberately, as a costume of *young adult woman with job*.

**07:10–07:45.** Breakfast is the same week to week within a given month and then changes wholesale: she will eat cereal every morning for six weeks and then never again. Coffee is taken with what an observer would describe as an excessive amount of sugar, counted in spoons (audibly, when she thinks no one is listening). She reads — and this is one of the more telling artifacts — the *business* section of the *Sunnydale Press* before any other, and she reads it cover to cover, including the small-type market listings. She has been observed circling figures with a mechanical pencil.

**07:45–08:20.** Commute. On foot when weather permits, by car (Xander's, borrowed; she does not own one and never gets a license on record) otherwise. She walks the same route every time, varying it only when construction or a known vampire nest forces a detour, and even then she returns to the canonical route at the first opportunity. The route is not the shortest available; it is the route she walked the first time she walked it. Pattern of foot traffic: she stops at the same newsstand for nothing (she has already read the paper), looks at the headlines, moves on. She has nodded at the same proprietor for years without ever, on record, exchanging a name.

**08:20–09:30.** Opens the Magic Box. The opening ritual is *fixed* and would be the easiest single thing for a surveillant to predict. She unlocks the front door with a particular two-handed motion, steps in, relocks behind her, walks the perimeter of the main floor counterclockwise, touches the register, the bell, the till drawer, the front display, the side display, and the back-room threshold in sequence. She unlocks the till, counts the float, writes the float figure in the day-book, places the day-book at a forty-five-degree angle to the register. She turns on lights in a specific order (back room first, then floor, then window). She flips the sign. She does this whether or not anyone has watched her do it.

**09:30–13:00.** Trading. She is — and this is corroborated repeatedly across the record by Giles, Willow, and Xander — *good at this*. Receipts are entered in real time. Customer interactions are competent at the transactional layer and erratic at the social one: she will quote prices, recommend substitutes, and upsell with skill, then volunteer that the customer's spouse is probably cheating on them, then return immediately to the transaction without apparent awareness of the break. She has a tic of repeating the final dollar amount three times, once to herself, once to the customer, once into the register as she rings it.

**13:00–13:45.** Lunch. Taken alone in the back room when possible. She eats from a brown bag prepared the previous night.
