**Provenance.** Willow's partner. First overlap c. 2000.

**Dynamic.** Of all the Scoobies, Tara is the one in whose presence Anya is most observably at ease. The reasons are inferable: Tara's own social register is quiet, non-pressuring, and accepting of oddness; she does not interrupt, does not editorialize, does not require Anya to perform any particular flavor of humanity. The brief scenes between them — household conversation, the bunny in "Once More, With Feeling" cut, casual exchanges at the Magic Box — show Anya at a behavioral baseline closer to relaxed than she achieves with anyone except Halfrek.

**Evolution.** Truncated. Tara is killed in 2002. Anya's grief is registered laterally — she is one of the Scoobies most disturbed by the killing and most cooperative in the response — but she does not speak it as her own loss. She had no vocabulary for the loss of a quiet peer; she filed it as Willow's catastrophe and helped manage that.

**Trust / safety.** High passive trust. The dyad never had to bear stress.

**Failure mode.** External — Tara is murdered.

**Leverage.** Tara's death narrowed Anya's circle of comfortable peers further, leaving Halfrek as the sole remaining one. D'Hoffryn's subsequent killing of Halfrek then completed the closure.

---

## 10. Giles — Destroyer of the Amulet, Reluctant Employer, Eventual Trusted Authority

**Provenance.** Watcher, librarian, later proprietor of the Magic Box. Their first interaction is the one in which he destroys her power center in "The Wish" — the single proximate act that strands her in mortality.

**Dynamic.** Initially hostile from her side (she has lost everything to him) and dismissive from his (she is a defeated demon, mildly absurd). Reorganizes when she begins working at the Magic Box: she discovers, and he discovers, that she is the best bookkeeper he has ever encountered, that she takes inventory seriously, that she can price ritual goods correctly because she has used them. He is the second figure in her life — after D'Hoffryn — to recognize her vocational competence and to assign her a domain. The relationship that develops is functionally apprentice-mentor with a financial reversal: she manages his books and he, intermittently, manages her professional development.

**Evolution.** Steady warming through S4–S5. His departure for England in S6 leaves her, by inference, the sole steward of the shop's operation and is one of several abandonments stacking in that year. Their final interactions in S7 are professionally respectful.

**Trust / safety.** Tradesman trust. Each trusts the other's competence within a bounded domain and does not extend further.

**Failure mode.** When he leaves for England she does not register the absence as personal loss but as logistical hardship — a defense.

**Leverage.** He destroyed her amulet and she never holds it against him in conversation; this is unusual for her and worth noting. He is one of very few figures whose authority she accepts without contest. An adversary asking her to act against Giles would meet unusual resistance.

---

## 11. Dawn Summers — Adjacent Child, Object of Late Tenderness


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# POWERS, ABILITIES & THEIR LIMITS

The subject is unusual in this file series in that her capability profile is **bimodal and discontinuous**: it consists of a millennium-scale supernatural skillset (active 880–1998, briefly reactivated 2002) bolted to a four-year human skillset (1998–2003) that had to be learned from a standing start in an adult-presenting body she did not develop into. The two skill banks do not blend smoothly. Tracking what she *can do*, *cannot do*, and *will not do* requires holding both registers in view simultaneously, because many of her late-period "human" competences are recognizably the residue of demon-era tradecraft, and many of her late-period failures are the residue of skills the demon era never required her to acquire.

---

## 1. The Demonic Capability Stack (Anyanka, c. 880–1998; reactivated 2002)

### 1.1 Wish-granting / reality-alteration (primary power)

**Mechanism.** Activated by a verbalized grievance from a wronged party — canonically female, canonically betrayed, canonically specific. The wish must be witnessed by Anyanka, the wronged party must speak it in the optative ("I wish…"), and Anyanka must will the alteration. Power source is external and detachable: the pendant/amulet ("The Wish," "Doppelgangland"). Without the amulet she cannot grant; with the amulet she can rewrite local reality on a scale up to and including alternate-timeline Sunnydale ("The Wish": a vampire-ruled town in which the Master rises, Buffy dies offscreen, etc.).

**Range.** The "Wish"-verse is the upper documented bound: a sustained alternate continuity affecting at least a town, with stable physics, persistent NPCs, and a duration limited only by destruction of the amulet. Lower bounds: small, surgical curses (a man becomes a worm; an unfaithful boyfriend's organs become external; the "everyone bursts into song" reading, which she floats and immediately denies in "Once More, with Feeling," indicates the scope is at minimum *plausibly* musical-comedy in scale). Medium bounds: the Russian peasant uprising of 1905 (she takes personal credit) and the so-called Mason-Dixon "massacre."

**Limits — hard.**
- Requires the amulet. No amulet, no power. This is the load-bearing limit of her entire 1100-year career, demonstrated twice (the 1199 loss, the 1998 destruction by Giles).
- Requires a wisher. She cannot self-initiate; she is a *response* power, not a generative one. This is structurally important — her entire vocational identity is reactive, never proactive, which maps onto the broader psychological pattern (see §3 of the workup: she requires an external trigger to act).
- Requires a verbalized wish in the correct grammatical mood. Cordelia's casual "I wish Buffy Summers had never come to Sunnydale" is sufficient; muttered resentment is not. Anya is a *contract* power.
- Bounded by gender/category of grievance. She is the patron of *scorned women.* Male wishers are not in her docket (she expresses confusion and mild distaste when Xander, in passing, ventures grievance-talk that would in another context be actionable).

**Limits — soft.**
- D'Hoffryn can revoke. He grants the amulet, he can withdraw status; in "Selfless" he ultimately takes her power by killing Halfrek in her place, demonstrating that her standing in the court is contingent on his calculation.
- She can be undone by the wisher. If Cordelia had counter-wished, the alt-Sunnydale would have folded — which is what eventually happens via Giles destroying the talisman, but the conceptual escape route exists.
- She is bound by the literal terms of the wish. This is not strictly a limit on power but on craftsmanship; her *pride* is in the literal granting, the monkey's-paw twist (cf. "I gave Cordelia exactly what she wanted"). This is a stylistic choice that, examined, reads as the autism-spectrum literalism of §4 weaponized as professional aesthetic.

**Signature application.** The disproportionate, ironic, *terms-of-contract* curse: turning a man into the literal embodiment of his metaphorical sin (Olaf the lecher → Olaf the troll). Her work has a recognizable hand — a forensic profiler with access to her case file would identify her vengeances by their grammatical structure (literal fulfillment of the figurative complaint) the way an art historian identifies brushwork.

### 1.2 Demonic embodiment (passive)

**The vein-y face.** Transformation to her Anyanka visage is voluntary, instantaneous, and (in S3) treated by her as her *real* face — she gestures at it with the unselfconsciousness of someone discussing their own bone structure. Functional advantages of the form include presumed enhanced physical durability, presumed pain attenuation (she shows none of the somatic complaints in demon mode that dominate her human mode), and presumed extended/halted aging — she is over 1,100 and physically presents as a woman in her early twenties at the moment of re-humanization.

**Translocation.** Demonstrated capacity to enter and exit Arashmaharr at will when in possession of her power. Lost on de-amuletization; she is stranded in Sunnydale specifically because she has no way out of the body she landed in.

**Demonic language and protocols.** Reads, writes, and speaks the relevant infernal tongues. Knows D'Hoffryn's invocation by heart and can summon him on demand ("Something Blue," "Hells Bells") — a skill the Scoobies use her for, and one of the few demon-era competences that ports cleanly into her human work.

### 1.3 Combat and tactical capability

She is *not* a melee specialist. Her demon-era work is curse-based, performed at conversational range, and does not require her to physically fight. In human form she develops adequate, not impressive, combat skills — sufficient to take a weapon and stand a line in "End of Days" and "Chosen," not sufficient to survive that line. Her death in "Chosen" — impaled in mid-quip, defending Andrew, anonymously — is the technically expected outcome for a low-tier combatant in a high-tier engagement and should not be over-read as failure. She held the line. She was not built to hold it long.

### 1.4 Institutional capability

Eleven hundred years in a structured bureaucratic court (D'Hoffryn's) trained her in something the canon under-emphasizes but the dossier should not: she is *bureaucratically literate at supernatural scale.* She knows contract law as practiced by entities older than nation-states. She knows who to invoke, what to offer, what protocols govern transactions between mortal and immortal parties. This skill ports into her Magic Box management with no friction whatsoever and is the deep reason she is a better shopkeeper than Giles — she has been doing supplier relations with this clientele for a millennium.

---

## 2. The Human Capability Stack (1998–2003)

### 2.1 Numeracy and commercial operation

**The defining late-period skill.** She runs the Magic Box at margins Giles could not match. On-screen behaviors: physical cash-counting (visible in nearly every Magic Box scene from S5 forward); inventory tracking by memory; pricing strategy ("don't touch the merchandise"); customer-segmentation (she will tolerate paying browsers indefinitely and eject non-paying ones immediately); supplier negotiation across species boundaries. She demonstrates mental arithmetic at a speed that suggests either eidetic numerical recall or a thousand years of practice at counting vengeance ledgers — likely both.

**Limits.** She cannot read the social meaning of money in the way her human peers do. She does not understand why charging Buffy is awkward, why discussing salary in front of guests is rude, why one does not announce one's profit margin during a wedding toast. The competence is technically excellent and pragmatically uncalibrated — the same shape as every other skill she has.

### 2.2 Ritual mechanics and applied occultism

She is the Scoobies' best *mechanic* in this domain. Willow has more raw magical power; Giles has more scholarly breadth; Anya has *operational* knowledge — what is supposed to happen when one performs rite X, what goes wrong when one improvises, what the supply chain for component Y looks like, which entities will and will not respond to a given summons. She is consulted as a specialist (notably in "Forever," "Tabula Rasa," and the cluster of late-S6 magical crises) and her advice is correct when she gives it.

**Limit.** Lacking her amulet, she has no spell-casting capability of her own. She is the *consultant,* not the operator. The distinction matters: she cannot rescue a situation by casting; she can only rescue it by knowing.

### 2.3 Language and the pragmatic deficit

Fluent in modern English at a vocabulary level that exceeds her peers — she uses precise, almost technical lexis (anatomical, financial, contractual) with notable consistency. She has functional competence in at least Old Norse (Aud era), Russian (deployed in passing references), and the relevant demon tongues. She picks up registers slowly and unevenly: she has not, after four years, fully internalized when to suppress an observation, when an honest answer is socially destructive, what idiom means versus says. The canon plays this comedically; clinically it is a *stable* pragmatic-language profile, not a deficit that closes, consistent with the autism-spectrum reading.

### 2.4 Performance, song, dance

Anomalously high. In "Once More, with Feeling" she delivers a tightly constructed musical number (the bunnies verse) with full vocal and choreographic competence; in "Selfless" she performs an extended solo with operatic affect. The simplest explanation is exposure: a millennium of attending other people's life-moments (weddings, mournings, curses) gave her a stockpile of cultural-performance scripts she can deploy when a context cues them. She does not improvise socially; she *executes* when the format is bounded.

### 2.5 Loyalty, witness, presence — the late, hard-won abilities

These are skills, and they are the ones the dossier should weight most heavily for the final eighteen months. She develops, slowly and incompletely:

- The ability to sit beside a grieving person without immediately speaking (Xander after the wedding; Buffy in the kitchen scenes of S7).
- The ability to revise a previously held moral position in light of new information ("Selfless").
- The ability to die for strangers without grandstanding ("Chosen").

These are the only powers in her file that show measurable *growth* across the record. The supernatural stack is binary (on/off, depending on amulet status). The human stack accretes.

---

## 3. Growth Curve, By Era

| Era | Supernatural Stack | Human Stack | Net Capability |
|---|---|---|---|
| Aud (pre-880) | None | Concrete cognition; animal husbandry; village skills; transformative resentment (latent) | Low; locally adequate |
| Anyanka I (880–1998) | Maximal | Atrophied; she has not lived as a human for eleven centuries | Maximal at her specialty; null outside it |
| Anya I (1998–2002) | Null | Climbing rapidly from zero: commerce, language register, attachment, ritual consultancy | Mid; specialist-grade in narrow domains |
| Anyanka II (2002, brief) | Restored, but reluctantly used | Retained, in tension with restored power | High but unstable; she has lost the moral simplicity that made the work tolerable |
| Anya II (2002–2003) | Null | Continued growth, especially in affect-tolerance and witness | Mid, with the late-development of the only abilities that mattered to her at the end |

The shape of the curve is the dossier's central finding about her capability: **she trades width for depth across her life.** The early supernatural breadth dies; the late human depth grows; the moment the two would have integrated into a mature adult human-with-eleven-centuries-of-experience profile is the moment she dies. Her file closes on an upward inflection.

---

## 4. How She Uses What She Has — Operational Patterns

**She does not freelance.** Every documented major use of power, in either stack, is *in response to a request or contract.* Wishes are granted on demand. Magic Box transactions are initiated by the customer. Ritual consultations are initiated by the Scoobies. Even her wedding to Xander she experiences as the formalization of his proposal, not the consummation of her own initiative. The one canonical exception — the fraternity massacre in "Selfless" — is performed on behalf of Halfrek's client, i.e. still on a contract, and is the act that triggers her decisive moral break. The pattern is so consistent that it should be considered diagnostic: *she requires an external authorization to deploy her capacities.* Handlers (D'Hoffryn, Giles, Xander, Buffy in S7) functioned as her authorizing signal.

**She over-delivers on the literal terms and under-delivers on the implicit ones.** Cordelia's wish is granted to its grammatical edge and not to its actual emotional intent. Xander's request that she stay calm at the wedding rehearsal is granted by her not yelling (literal), while she undermines it by candidly discussing their sex life (implicit terms violated). This is the same engine; she is consistent.

**She telegraphs.** Her escalation ladder (capitalist chatter → somatic complaints → rabbit-mentions → flat dissociative competence → regression to demon-self) is visible in real time and audible in her speech. A handler with even a week's observation of her could predict her state at any given moment. Adversaries with the same observation could exploit it.

---

## 5. Signature Applications

A handful of operational signatures recur often enough across the file to constitute a fingerprint:

1. **The Literal Curse.** Olaf → troll. The unfaithful → worms, vermin, the externalization of organs. The wronged-woman wish granted to its grammatical extreme. Forensic identifier across centuries.
2. **The Cash-Count Tell.** Under stress, she handles money. Visible in a dozen Magic Box scenes. If she is counting bills at speed, she is regulating affect, not doing accounting.
3. **The Inappropriate Frankness Pivot.** When she does not know what is wanted of her socially, she defaults to clinical disclosure — usually sexual, anatomical, or financial. This is not provocation; it is the only register she trusts to be unambiguous.
4. **The Bunnies Verbal Marker.** Rabbits, mentioned spontaneously and without prompt, indicate she is at moderate-to-high stress. Mentioned in song, in panic, in wedding-eve crisis. A weather-vane.
5. **The Quip Under Mortal Pressure.** A late-period acquisition (S6–7). When she quips while in combat, she has finally integrated humor as an affect-regulator. Her death-quip in "Chosen" is the final, completed instance.

---

## 6. The Symptom-as-Signature Reading

Each major capacity in her file, read clinically, is also a wound presenting as a tool.

- **Wish-granting power** is the literalized form of the cognitive style she had as Aud: take the figurative complaint, render it concrete. D'Hoffryn did not give her a skill; he gave her a *job description* matched to a pre-existing cognitive shape. Her supernatural power was always her neurotype, amplified.
- **The amulet dependency** is the externalization of her self-concept problem. She does not own her power; she wears it. When it is destroyed she is not weakened, she is *de-identified.* The same structure governs the Aud-Anyanka-Anya-Anyanka-Anya identity sequence: each self is an issued credential, not an interior.
- **The commercial competence** is the vengeance-ledger reorganized for peacetime. The same mind that counted contracts fulfilled now counts inventory turned; the medium changes, the underlying need to *quantify one's worth in completed units* does not.
- **The ritual-mechanics consultancy** is the institutional memory of someone who has spent a thousand years inside a bureaucracy and finally found a workplace that values that on the human side. It is also the only continuous skill across her ontological breaks — the one capacity that survives intact through every transformation, because it lives in semantic memory rather than in body or status.
- **The phobia of rabbits** is, in capability terms, an *anti*-power: the involuntary somatic recall of the pre-trauma self, surfacing without consent in the middle of competent functioning. It is the file's clearest evidence that no transformation, demonic or moral, has fully overwritten Aud. The rabbits are still there. The girl who named them is still there.
- **The late capacity to witness, to revise, and to die for strangers** is the only ability she ever developed *without* a contract authorizing it. This is the meaningful capability in her file. Every other power on this list was issued to her by someone — by D'Hoffryn, by the wisher, by the customer, by the cultural context. The capacity she developed herself, in the last year of her life, was the capacity to act without authorization on behalf of people she had no contractual obligation to. By her own operating code, that is the only act of hers that *counts.* By the dossier's accounting, it is the only one she ever fully owned.

The arc, capability-wise: she begins as a literal-minded young woman whose cognitive style is mocked, is given a thousand years of supernatural amplification of exactly that style, loses the amplification, slowly rebuilds a narrower but more genuinely her own skill bank in human time, briefly relapses into the amplified version under the original precipitant, finds it no longer fits, and dies in possession of the one skill she had built rather than been issued. The supernatural file is the longer file. The human file is the *deeper* one. A handler reading this dossier should weight them accordingly.


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT

*Subject designation: ANYA / ANYANKA / AUD. Operational record spans ~1,140 subjective years across two ontological categories. The tradecraft below is reconstructed from canonical action sequences, observed habits, financial records (Magic Box ledgers), and inferential pattern-matching across the full longitudinal file. The single most important fact for any operator reading this section: the subject's methods are extraordinarily consistent across all eras. The wrapper changes; the operating system does not.*

---

## 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

### 1.1 The contract as cognitive primitive

Every decision the subject has ever made — across village, court, and Scooby-era — resolves into a contract. She does not think in narratives, relationships, or values; she thinks in terms-and-conditions. A wish is a contract; a marriage is a contract; a fight against the First Evil is a contract (she states this explicitly in *Chosen*: she is there because Buffy is paying the bill, and then, in the same monologue, revises the terms upward: she is there because of "the people"). This is the inheritance of the autistic-literalist substrate (§3 of the workup) cross-bred with the operational reality of eleven hundred years executing literal binding agreements with the wronged.

The decision sequence, in field conditions, runs:

1. **Identify the contract.** Who is asking? What exactly are they asking? What is the wording? She will pause — visibly, sometimes for an awkward beat — and re-read the situation literally.
2. **Identify the consideration.** What does she get? She is not embarrassed by this question and will often voice it aloud, to the consternation of less transactional operators in the room.
3. **Identify the breach condition.** Under what circumstance is the deal off? She is unusually good at spotting bad-faith counterparties because she has spent a millennium being the bad-faith counterparty.
4. **Execute literally.** She does not improvise within the spirit of the agreement; she executes the letter and lets consequence fall where contract sends it.

This is why she is devastating as a vengeance operator (the punishment is the wish, perfectly literalized into horror) and why she is awkward as a friend (a birthday gift is a thing one gives, not a thing whose meaning one curates).

### 1.2 Speed and latency

Two distinct decision-speeds are documented:

- **Sub-second response on bounded problems.** Combat in *Graduation Day*, *The Gift*, *End of Days*, *Chosen*; ritual mechanics in *Triangle*, *Tabula Rasa*; cash transactions in *Life Serial*. When the problem is geometrically constrained — known input, known output, known rules — she is one of the fastest decision-makers in the Sunnydale record.
- **Catastrophic latency on unbounded social problems.** When the problem is ambiguous (what does Xander want for his birthday; what is the appropriate way to react to Joyce's death; should one tell the truth about a friend's haircut), she either freezes, defaults to literal output, or — under acute pressure — defaults to the pre-formed institutional script (D'Hoffryn's).

The handler-relevant inference: she can be relied on under fire and cannot be relied on at a dinner party. Operations should be structured to keep her in the bounded mode.

### 1.3 Failure mode: the regression switch

Under specific stress — public romantic humiliation, sustained moral self-reflection, repeated category-questioning ("are you really one of us") — the subject's decision system fails in a single predictable direction: she returns to the last identity that had clear rules. In 880 CE that meant transforming a man into a troll. In 2002 it meant a phone call to D'Hoffryn. The mechanism is identical. Any handler should treat the phrase "Hi, D'Hoffryn" or its functional analog as a code-red operational event.

---

## 2. TRADECRAFT — DEMON ERA (c. 880–1998, brief return 2002)

Eleven hundred years of professional practice in a single specialty. The methods are documented enough across *The Wish*, *Doppelgangland*, *Triangle*, *Selfless*, and *Older and Far Away* to reconstruct standard operating procedure.

### 2.1 Target acquisition

She does not solicit. She *listens*. Targets self-identify by speaking the wish aloud, ideally in a colloquial form — "I wish that…" — within earshot. She has, by long practice, developed an antenna for the verbal precursors: the woman whose voice has been crying, the woman whose phrasing tilts toward subjunctive grievance, the woman who says "men" rather than "him." She gravitates to bars, weddings, salons, kitchens, laundries — anywhere wronged women gather in unsupervised speech. In Sunnydale this presents as a marked preference for women's social spaces and an unusual ease entering them.

### 2.2 Engagement protocol

A short, often clumsy introduction. She does not run a long con; the con isn't necessary, because the mark is already aligned with the product. Her sales patter is documented in *The Wish* (to Cordelia): rapid agreement, mirroring of the mark's specific grievance vocabulary, gentle escalation from sympathy to suggestion ("wish it"). She is bad at flirting and good at this, because this is the social register she was built in.

### 2.3 Execution

The amulet (the pendant) is the instrument; the wish is the contract; the literalization is the craft. The artistry, by her own account, is in how *exactly* the punishment fits the spoken word. *The Wish* is a master class: Cordelia wishes Buffy had never come to Sunnydale; the result is not a generic dystopia but the specific Sunnydale that follows from that exact counterfactual, with Cordelia herself trapped inside it as collateral. This is signature work — the wish is fulfilled to the letter and the wisher is folded into the consequence. Examine the Mason-Dixon record, the Russian 1905 pattern, and the fraternity massacre in *Selfless* for the same fingerprint.

### 2.4 Tools of the trade

- The **amulet/pendant** — power center, single point of failure (lost twice, once c. 1199, once to Giles in *The Wish*).
- **Wardrobe coding** — the demon visage ("veiny face") is summoned at point of execution; the human form is the field uniform. She controls the transition with what appears to be sub-second voluntary effort.
- **D'Hoffryn's recall sigil** — a chant/incantation invocable to summon her patron. She knows the words; in the late record she avoids speaking them.
- **The vocabulary of historical grievance** — she carries the linguistic registers of a dozen eras and can switch into the dialect of the wronged woman in front of her. This is documented in micro in her wedding-anecdote chatter and is field-confirmed by the cross-era references she drops.

### 2.5 Counter-tradecraft awareness

She knows how vengeance demons are defeated, because she is one. She knows the amulet must be destroyed; she knows the wish can be unwished by the wisher's counterpart with the right framing; she knows D'Hoffryn's court has internal politics, hierarchies (Halfrek is a peer, not subordinate), and disciplinary practices (Halfrek's killing in *Selfless* is procedural, not personal). This is institutional knowledge that survives her humanization and is accessible on tap to allies who know how to ask.

---

## 3. TRADECRAFT — HUMAN ERA (1998–2003)

When she is stranded in *The Wish*, she has zero modern human tradecraft and acquires it in roughly four years, by direct method-acquisition rather than enculturation. She watches what humans do and replicates it, with a characteristic over-correction.

### 3.1 The Magic Box period — commercial tradecraft

From late S4 through S6, she operates Giles's shop and then owns it. The financial and operational record here is more legible than any other phase of her life.

- **Bookkeeping.** Double-entry, hand-written ledgers, daily reconciliation. She closes the register herself; she counts twice; she has been observed re-counting after staff (Xander, Tara) close out. She does not delegate the count.
- **Cash preference.** She prefers physical currency; she handles it tactilely (the on-screen counting habit). Inferred: cash is the only medium in which her concretizing cognitive style achieves full satisfaction. A digital balance is, to her, an assertion; a stack of bills is a fact.
- **Inventory.** She knows what is on the shelves to the unit. She knows the markup on every SKU. She prices ritual components dynamically based on rarity, season, and apocalypse-proximity (apocalypse markup is documented: prices rise when the world ends).
- **Vendor relations.** She maintains a stable of suppliers, some of them demonic, all of them dealt with through what she experiences as the comforting infrastructure of invoicing. The shop is, among other things, an intelligence node: traffic through the Magic Box is one of the better signals of supernatural activity in Sunnydale during this period.
- **Customer profiling.** She is unusually good at recognizing the wronged-woman demographic walking in to buy a curse component. She does not always disclose this recognition; she sometimes sells the components anyway, with a kind of professional fellow-feeling that is operationally relevant.

### 3.2 Combat tradecraft

She is not a primary combatant, but the record (the Knights of Byzantium at the RV, *Bargaining*, *The Gift*, the basement battles of S7, *Chosen*) shows a competent secondary. Her style:

- **Weapons preference: edged, two-handed, swung.** A sword. She has reach awareness but limited footwork; she compensates with willingness to commit fully to a strike.
- **Tactical role:** flanking, support, and ritual disruption. She is best deployed where her ritual knowledge can be expended — identifying a binding object, breaking a ward, naming a demon's vulnerability mid-fight.
- **Pain tolerance:** poor early, improving. Her interoceptive learning curve (§2 medical) shows in combat: she flinches less in S7 than in S4. She remains psychologically intolerant of disfiguring injury — the visible-wound type — likely because of the long association of "veiny face" with her demon self.
- **Calling out**: she narrates fights. This is partly her general verbal overflow and partly a documented habit of announcing what she is doing as she does it, in the manner of someone trained to vocalize during ritual work.

### 3.3 Domestic tradecraft

She runs a household with the same ledger-mind. Apartment with Xander: rent split tracked; groceries inventoried; sexual frequency reported aloud as a metric (this is partly social-inappropriateness, partly genuine satisfaction in a countable). She cooks badly and knows it. She handles laundry, bills, and mail; Xander handles repairs and the car. The division is gendered in a way that is itself an artifact — she is replicating the Aud-era household template, the only domestic schema she has fully internalized.

### 3.4 Intelligence and information tradecraft

She is a surprisingly competent open-source analyst when motivated. She reads. She remembers. Her millennium of fieldwork has left her with an encyclopedic mental rolodex of demonic taxonomy, ritual mechanics, lower-pantheon politics, and historical precedent, which she dispenses on demand. She does not catalogue this knowledge externally — there is no notebook. It is stored in her, and the retrieval interface is conversation. The operationally important consequence: lose Anya and you lose the database.

She is poor at modern human OSINT — she does not natively use computers, prefers paper, has limited media literacy. Willow handles the digital layer; Anya handles the analog and the historical.

---

## 4. RESOURCES & FINANCES

### 4.1 Capital position over time

- **Demon era:** no personal finances; resourced by D'Hoffryn's court; presumed access to collected tribute, sigil-craft, and inter-dimensional logistics. No money in the modern sense.
- **Early human era (1998–2000):** destitute. Lives in a small apartment she pays for with unclear means, possibly residual demon-era valuables liquidated piece by piece. References to selling unspecified items in early S4.
- **Magic Box era (2000–2002):** salaried employee, then on Giles's departure effectively the proprietor with a stake. By S6 she is the principal at the shop. Cash flow positive, by her own accounting.
- **Post-shop, late S7:** the Magic Box is destroyed in *Grave* (S6 finale). She is decapitalized and unhoused-adjacent thereafter, living among the Scoobies. The financial anxiety this provokes is acute and documented (her speech in *Empty Places* about Buffy's leadership has financial undertones — she has watched the asset base evaporate).

### 4.2 Spending pattern

Frugal on self, generous on the wedding (the one documented major expenditure: the wedding in *Hells Bells*, which she micro-managed and which represented years of accumulated capital). She does not buy luxuries. She does not gamble. She does not invest in instruments she cannot touch. Her aversion to abstract finance is total.

### 4.3 Off-book resources

- **D'Hoffryn's network.** Even post-vengeance, she retains contact protocols. She can summon him; in *Older and Far Away* she does. This is a standing line of credit she is increasingly reluctant to draw on.
- **Halfrek.** Personal access to another vengeance operator until *Selfless*. Halfrek functions as both peer and back-channel into the court.
- **The Scooby network.** Logistical (transportation, intelligence, muscle), residential (couches), and — late in the record — financial (Buffy's household covers her).

---

## 5. INFRASTRUCTURE & PATTERNS OF MOVEMENT

### 5.1 Geographic footprint, Sunnydale years

A small, repeating circuit. The subject is not a flâneuse; she moves between fixed nodes.

- **Residence 1**, unspecified apartment, S3–early S5. Solo.
- **Residence 2**, Xander's basement, then Xander's apartment, S5–S6. Cohabiting.
- **Residence 3**, the Summers house, late S6–S7. Multiple Scoobies present; she takes a peripheral room.
- **The Magic Box**, daily, opening to close, with predictable timing. Open by 10, close by 7, register reconciled by 7:20.
- **The Bronze**, infrequent, social-pressure-driven, never preferred.
- **The Summers kitchen**, frequent; she gravitates to kitchens as a category, an Aud-era residue.
- **The cemetery rotation**, only when conscripted.

She does not have a documented bolt-hole, safehouse, or pre-planned exfiltration route. This is a significant operational gap and is consonant with her broader avoidance of forward-planning for catastrophe — a person who has been guaranteed immortality for a thousand years does not learn to plan an escape.

### 5.2 Daily rhythm

- **Morning:** early riser. Reports of being awake before Xander throughout cohabitation. Coffee with sugar (multiple sugars; quantified aloud).
- **Workday:** the shop, with one lunch, taken on premises. She eats while counting.
- **Evening:** sex (frequency reported); television (she develops a fondness for crime procedurals and game shows — the appeal of bounded-rule narratives); occasional research at the table.
- **Sleep:** light, with periodic insomniac episodes during high-stress arcs (Glory; the resurrection; Tara's death; the wedding). She does not nap.

### 5.3 Communication tradecraft

- **Phone:** she uses it readily and bluntly. No code, no operational discipline. Voicemails are unedited.
- **In-person:** her preferred channel. She does not write letters of consequence; she walks over.
- **Ritual summons:** D'Hoffryn-tier contacts only; she knows the protocol and uses it sparingly post-1998.
- **Email:** uncertain in the record; if used at all, mediated through Willow.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL TELLS

These are the patterns by which the subject can be identified, anticipated, and read in the field. They are stable across eras and survive disguise.

### 6.1 Verbal tells

- **Quantification under stress.** When pressed, she counts. Money, years, body counts, orgasms, square roots. The unit shifts; the act is the tell.
- **Literal-mode escalation.** Anxiety drives her *toward* literalness, not away. The more uncertain she is, the more concretely she speaks. Operators reading her for distress should watch the abstraction level of her sentences.
- **Bunny-mentions** as anxiety proxy. The phobia surfaces verbally before it surfaces in behavior.
- **Capitalist liturgy** as social discomfort marker. The louder the praise of money, the more uncomfortable the room.
- **The pause-and-restart.** When she has caught herself being inappropriate (late record only), there is a perceptible micro-pause and a restart in a more cautious register. The pause itself is the most reliable indicator that the late-period growth has consolidated.

### 6.2 Somatic tells

- **Hand-to-pendant gesture** in the demon era; persistent ghost-gesture in early human era, touching her clavicle when stressed.
- **Counting motion** with fingers when calculating, including in social contexts where it reads as odd.
- **Posture stiffening** at the word "wedding," "marriage," "engagement," "altar" throughout S7.
- **Eye contact** unusually steady, sometimes uncomfortably so. She does not perform the human gaze-aversion rhythm correctly. This is autistic-substrate and is a reliable identifier across all human-passing forms.
- **Smile latency.** Her smile lags the social cue by a beat. Even when genuine, it arrives a fraction late.

### 6.3 Operational tells

- **Ledger-keeping** wherever she is. If she occupies a space for more than a week, there will be a count of something.
- **Cash on her person.** She carries more physical currency than her economic position warrants. She is comforted by the weight.
- **Reflexive role-allocation** in any group — she will, within minutes, identify who is in charge, what the rules are, what she is being asked to do, and what she gets. If she cannot answer these, she will ask, audibly.
- **Sword-reach for an edged tool** when offered a weapons choice.
- **Gravitation to kitchens.**
- **Avoidance of mirrors during demon-self transitions** (inferred from staging in *Selfless*); the demon visage is something she executes outward, not something she contemplates.

### 6.4 The regression tell

The single most operationally important pattern. When subject is approaching the failure mode of §1.3, the following sequence has been documented:

1. Flattening of affect.
2. Increased money- or count-talk, even by her standards.
3. Withdrawal from physical touch with bonded persons.
4. A specific sentence-frame, variants of "I don't know what I am" or "Who am I now."
5. Movement toward a place of prior identity — the Magic Box site, a bar where wronged women congregate, a phone.
6. Contact with D'Hoffryn or attempt thereof.

Steps 1–4 are recoverable with the intervention of a bonded peer (Xander, Buffy, Willow, Tara — historically). Step 5 is the last reliable point of intervention. Step 6 is operationally catastrophic and was reached exactly once in the record (*Hells Bells* → *Selfless*).

---

## 7. SUMMARY ASSESSMENT FOR DOWNSTREAM USE

The subject is a high-competence, narrow-spectrum operator with one of the longest practical track records of any individual in the Sunnydale file. Her tradecraft is unitary across eras: contract identification, literal execution, signature aesthetic. Her vulnerabilities are also unitary: she cannot operate in ambiguous social terrain, she has no escape plan, and she has a single, well-mapped regression pathway under romantic-humiliation stress.

She is, in operational terms, the rare asset who is simultaneously extraordinarily reliable (in bounded mission profiles) and extraordinarily fragile (under one specific class of personal stress). The handler who keeps her in-domain, keeps her counting, keeps her bonded, and intercepts the §6.4 sequence at step 3 or earlier, has access to a thousand years of institutional knowledge in a person who is, at the end of the record, voluntarily choosing to stand and die with strangers because she has finally constructed a contract she wants to honor.

The record closes with the contract honored and the operator gone.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

*A reconstruction of how the subject parses reality, structures action, allocates trust, and locates herself within the orders she perceives. Derived from twelve hundred years of utterance and choice; corroborated where possible, inferred where necessary, flagged where contested.*

---

## 1. THE FUNDAMENTAL ONTOLOGY: A CONTRACTUAL UNIVERSE

The subject's deepest metaphysical commitment — older than her demonhood, older than her trauma, traceable to the Aud-era literalism — is that **reality is fundamentally a system of terms**. Things have specifications. Persons have terms. Acts have prices. Relationships have clauses. The universe is not random and not, in the philosophical sense, mysterious; it is a very large and somewhat poorly drafted contract, and most human suffering is the consequence of parties failing to read it.

This is not a learned demon-court ideology. The Aud-era detail — naming each rabbit individually, breeding them as a tracked enterprise, distributing them as named gifts — already shows the architecture: the world parsed as discrete countable units with assigned labels and assigned exchange-values. D'Hoffryn's recruitment succeeded because the vengeance demon's role was *already* her native ontology made vocational: a job in which every wrong was a specifiable item, every wisher's grievance an explicit clause, every curse a deliverable. Eleven hundred years did not give her this worldview. It rewarded it.

Several corollaries fall out of the contractual ontology:

- **Promises are load-bearing.** When she insists, in "Hells Bells" and again in "Selfless," that vows were *exchanged* and therefore *owed*, she is not being sentimental. She is naming what to her is a structural fact of the universe, equivalent in weight to gravity.
- **Disclosure is moral.** Her notorious inability to censor — about sex, about money, about Xander's anatomy, about death — is not a social deficit she has failed to correct. It is an ethical commitment masquerading as a deficit. To withhold material information from a counterparty is, in her schema, the genuine offense. The Sunnydale habit of tactful omission reads to her as fraud.
- **Ambiguity is malfeasance.** A clause that can be read two ways is a clause one party has drafted to cheat the other. Hence her preference, throughout the demon period, for wishes phrased with brutal literalism — she did not subvert her clients' wishes, she executed them exactly, and her aesthetic pride was in the execution.

The deep cost of this ontology is that **she has no native category for the implicit**. Friendships that ripen by unspoken accretion; loves that grow by inference; loyalties that are understood-not-said — these are all forms she has had to learn by laborious observation, late, and incompletely.

---

## 2. THE READING OF CONFLICT

Conflict, for the subject, is **the surfacing of a breach**. It is information, not catastrophe. When two parties fight, it means the contract was unclear or one party defaulted; the work of conflict is to find which, name it, and assign the remedy.

This produces a distinct cluster of behaviors:

- **She does not avoid conflict; she diagnoses it.** Where the Scoobies (especially Willow, Buffy) often run conflict through layers of indirection, Anya tends to state the breach aloud, at volume, in the room, immediately. Her interventions in group strategy sessions ("Bargaining," "Two to Go," the Magic Box research scenes) repeatedly take the form: *here is the actual issue, which no one will say.*
- **She is unable to read low-intensity conflict at all.** Sub-threshold tension — the kind that humans signal by glance, pause, micro-withdrawal — is invisible to her until it crosses into the explicit. As a result she frequently *causes* conflict by failing to register that it has already begun, then resolves it efficiently once it is open.
- **She is comfortable in adversarial settings.** A negotiation, a court-of-vengeance hearing, a customer dispute at the Magic Box — anywhere the terms are explicit and the goals declared — she is markedly more regulated and competent than in unstructured social settings.

**Escalation logic.** Her instinct in conflict is not domination but **proportional remedy** — until it is not. The thousand-year career was a vocational training in *disproportional* remedy: turn a man into a troll for cheating; flay a fraternity for a wronged girl. The two algorithms coexist in her. With low-stakes counterparties (customers, peers) she is proportional. With anyone occupying the structural position once held by Olaf — a romantic intimate who has defaulted on disclosed terms — the proportional algorithm fails and the disproportional one engages automatically. This is the single most predictable instability in her operational profile.

---

## 3. THE READING OF CONTROL

The subject has a paradoxical and revealing relationship to control: she **does not seek to dominate, she seeks to be placed**.

Most agents with her capability set (a millennium of independent action; mastery of high-order magical mechanics; demonstrated capacity for mass casualty events) would, by midlife, have constructed their own dominion. She did not. Throughout the vengeance period she operated within D'Hoffryn's hierarchy, took assignments, deferred to court protocol, and never appears to have attempted promotion or schism. In Sunnydale she works for Giles, then succeeds him at the Magic Box only by inheritance, and within the Scooby formation she consistently positions herself as a *member* rather than a contender for leadership.

The structure underneath this is: **she perceives unstructured agency as terrifying**. When she does not know what she is or what the rules are — the moments after the amulet breaks, the moments after Xander leaves the altar, the moments in "Selfless" between killing the boys and asking Buffy to kill her — she decompensates almost immediately. She does not want sovereignty. She wants a coherent role with explicit duties, performed visibly, rewarded measurably.

This is why:

- She **likes uniforms, name tags, business hours, and inventory.** The Magic Box is not just a livelihood; it is an exoskeleton.
- She **likes ritual.** The wedding plans in S6 are not bridezilla affect; they are the construction of a procedural scaffold that will tell her what to do at every moment for a year.
- She **defers to instituted authority** — D'Hoffryn, Giles, Buffy-as-general — far more readily than her power level would predict. The deference is not weakness; it is the relief of being slotted.
- She **chafes only at unmarked authority** — the unspoken Scooby pecking order, Willow's quiet first-among-equals status, Xander's family expectations. The chafing reads as rudeness; it is in fact her demand that hierarchies be made explicit so she can comply with them.

Control of others, for her, is a thing one acquires only as a side effect of being assigned a role that requires it. Self-control, by contrast, is a constant uphill labor and her most reliable index of distress.

---

## 4. THE READING OF TRUST

Trust, in her schema, is a **disclosed-terms relationship**. The default is not paranoia and not naïveté; it is *unsigned*. Unsigned parties are neither trusted nor distrusted; they are not yet entered into the ledger.

Once entered, trust is **binary and durable**. She does not modulate trust; she assigns it, fully, on the basis of a few explicit acts, and then maintains it past the point most humans would have revised. Her continued loyalty to D'Hoffryn long past "Selfless" — when he kills Halfrek to punish her — is the clearest example. She is hurt; she is not surprised; she does not reclassify him. He acted within the terms of his role. The terms were the problem; the party was consistent.

This produces specific operational signatures:

- **Recruitment of her trust is easier than expected and harder than expected.** Easier: a single act of inclusion, named as such, will often suffice (Xander's offer to take her to the prom; Halfrek's reappearance as her old friend). Harder: she will not extend trust on charm, charisma, reputation, or unspoken cues. The act must be specific and the inclusion legible.
- **Betrayal does not produce distrust; it produces a category-change.** A betrayer is moved from "intimate" to "target." There is no intermediate "person I am wary of but still know." This is the absence-of-middle-register that recurs across her whole psychology.
- **She is markedly more trusting of women than of men.** With Tara, Willow, Halfrek, and (eventually) Buffy and Dawn, her threshold for inclusion is lower and her tolerance for ambiguity higher. With men — even Xander, even Giles — the contractual frame stays close to the surface. The asymmetry is trauma-shaped; it is not ideological but biographical.
- **She trusts institutions more than persons.** The vengeance court, the Magic Box's ledgers, the Scooby formation as a unit, even the wedding-as-institution — these are objects she can rely on because their terms are written down. Persons drift; institutions specify.

---

## 5. THE READING OF RISK

Her risk calculus has a peculiar and self-consistent shape: **she is highly risk-tolerant about catastrophic outcomes and highly risk-averse about ambient losses**.

She will face an apocalypse, walk into a Bringer ambush, accept lethal combat in "Chosen," and request her own execution in "Selfless" without visible hesitation. She will also panic at the prospect of a bad quarter at the Magic Box, a misplaced inventory tag, an aging line on her face, or a single rabbit in the room.

This is not cowardice-versus-bravery. It is the operational expression of her ontology:

- **Catastrophes have terms.** An apocalypse is a contract one signs by being present; the price is death; the deliverable is clear. She knows how to be in such a scene.
- **Ambient losses are unscripted.** A slow business decline, an unloved aging, a friend's quiet withdrawal, a small phobic encounter — these are leakages from a system she cannot audit. They terrify her because they cannot be discharged in a single transaction.

Practical implications:

- **In tactical settings she is reliable, even brave.** She fights in "Graduation Day," "The Gift," "Bargaining," "Two to Go," "Chosen." She does not flinch from violence; she will engage a hostile she cannot beat.
- **In strategic settings she is over-conservative.** She hoards, plans, double-counts, insists on backup; she budgets disasters in advance.
- **She insures.** Magic Box inventory, wedding contingencies, escape clauses in interpersonal arrangements — wherever she can pre-pay against ambient loss, she does.
- **She is uniquely vulnerable to slow attrition.** The whole arc of S6 — Xander's drift, Joyce's death, Tara's death, her own undefined status — is the form of suffering her risk model handles worst. The relapse into demonhood at the wedding is, in part, an attempt to convert a slow grief into a single discharge.

---

## 6. THE READING OF MONEY, EXCHANGE, AND VALUE

Money is the **lingua franca of her ontology made tangible**. It is a substance that does what she believes the universe does: it counts, it labels, it discharges debts, it makes the implicit explicit. Her relationship to it is not greed and not bourgeois affect; it is **religious** in the strict sense — a sacrament that makes her ontology visible.

- She prefers cash to credit because cash is fully disclosed at the moment of exchange.
- She counts visibly because counting is the performative confirmation that the contract has cleared.
- She names prices aloud because naming is the act that makes a transaction valid.
- She is offended by theft as a category — not because of property rights in the abstract, but because theft is a refusal of the contractual frame, the universe's worst sin.

This generalizes. She converts whatever she values into countable units — orgasms, vengeances, dollars, years of relationship — not because she is shallow but because counting is her only fluent vocabulary for *importance*. When she tells Xander that they have had three hundred and however many orgasms, she is offering him the most reverent inventory she knows how to make.

---

## 7. THE READING OF SEX AND THE BODY

Sex, for the subject, is **the most reliably specifiable form of intimacy** and therefore the form she trusts first. It has explicit acts, measurable frequencies, declared preferences, observable outcomes. It can be entered into with disclosed terms and exited without ambiguity. In a relational landscape where almost everything else baffles her, sex is unusually legible.

This is why:

- Her sexual frankness is **not exhibitionism but candor**. She is simply describing the only domain of human intimacy whose grammar she fully reads.
- Her **Spike encounter** in "Entropy" is intelligible inside her code: two parties, mutually disclosed grief, mutually disclosed appetite, no clauses about future obligation. It is the cleanest transaction available to either of them in that hour.
- Her **body itself** she treats as a piece of equipment of recent acquisition. She catalogues its functions because she is, in a quite literal sense, still in onboarding. The flatness of her affect about pain and pleasure is not anhedonia; it is the affect of a new operator reading the manual aloud.

The body is, for her, the one site where she has not yet imposed her contractual ontology — because the body keeps issuing demands (aging, fatigue, fear) that have no counterparty to negotiate with. This is the seed of her death-anxiety: mortality is the universe's only non-negotiable clause, and her whole worldview is structured around the assumption that everything is negotiable.

---

## 8. THE READING OF MORAL CATEGORIES

Her moral world begins, for eleven hundred years, as a **two-column ledger**: the wronged (right) and the betrayer (wrong). It is the operating ethic of vengeance — simple, executable, and grotesquely inadequate to any case more complex than the one that produced it.

The decisive event of her late life is the **collapse of this binary in "Selfless."** Confronted with the fraternity boys she has killed — boys who were genuinely contemptible, in answer to a girl who was genuinely wronged — she discovers that the algorithm has produced an outcome she cannot endorse. The wronged-and-betrayer ledger no longer balances to anything she can live with. Her request for execution is, among other things, the only proportional remedy her old code can issue against itself: the contract was bad; the drafter must pay.

Post-Selfless, she carries the fragments of a new moral schema, never fully articulated but visible in her late behavior:

- **Persons are revisable** in a way contracts are not. Xander did not become a target after the wedding; she could not finish the curse on him. Some clause in her had been rewritten.
- **Suffering does not entitle.** A wronged party is not, by virtue of being wronged, licensed to inflict. This is the principle she has spent a thousand years denying and that, in her last year, she begins to live by.
- **Belonging is moral.** To stand with people, to be one of them, is itself a good — not merely an instrumental relation but a constitutive one. Her speech in "End of Days" — that she had no idea what she was but would find out by standing with these people — is the closest she comes to a stated ethics.

She does not, even at the end, fully renounce the contractual frame. She **expands** it. The new clauses include: *persons may amend terms; suffering does not authorize harm; the contract one signs by being in the room with people is itself binding.*

---

## 9. THE READING OF TIME AND MORTALITY

For most of her record, the subject's temporal frame is **functionally infinite**. Eleven hundred years inside a body that did not age produced a default in which any given decade is small. This produces, in her human period, two opposite distortions:

- **Compression** of short-term horizons: she expects relationships to settle, careers to mature, social statuses to clarify on timelines that feel reasonable to a being who has had centuries. She is impatient because patience, for her, would mean waiting a year for what historically took an afternoon of subjective time.
- **Terror** of any horizon at all. Mortality, once she registers it, registers as a *clause she did not consent to*. Her death-talk across S5–7 — about Joyce, Buffy's resurrection, Tara, her own aging — has the specific affect of someone discovering a non-negotiable term in a contract she thought she had read.

The integration she reaches in "Chosen" is partial but real: she enters combat knowing she may die, makes a quip, dies anonymously. She has finally accepted a contract that includes her own mortality as an unspecified clause. This is — for her — an enormous philosophical achievement, possibly the largest of her life.

---

## 10. THE READING OF HER OWN PLACE

Where does she locate herself in the order of things? The honest answer, across most of the record, is **nowhere stable**.

She has occupied:

- *the village outsider* (Aud, an odd young woman in Sjornjost),
- *the demon professional* (Anyanka, ranking member of D'Hoffryn's court),
- *the displaced exile* (early Anya, stranded in a teenager's body in a high school she does not understand),
- *the girlfriend/wife-elect* (S4–S6 Anya, defining her place by proximity to Xander),
- *the proprietor* (Magic Box-era Anya, defining her place by an institution),
- *the relapsed demon* (S7 opening, retreating to the only other place she has ever had),
- *the Scooby* (late S7 Anya, defining her place by chosen alliance).

She has never, at any point in the record, defined her place from the inside. Every self has been external: a role, a relation, an employer, a counterparty. Her "Who am I now?" to Xander is the deepest question of her life and she dies without a fully formulated answer.

What changes in the last season is that she begins, for the first time, to construct a place that is **not borrowed from an institution**. The "End of Days" speech — choosing to stand with the people she has come to know, not because she is contracted to but because she has come to want to — is the first self-located self she ever produces. It is fragile, it is recent, it is incomplete. It is also, by her own ontology, fully binding: she has signed it, and she pays the price.

---

## 11. OPERATIONAL HEURISTICS, COMPILED

If one were to extract from the above the actual rules-of-action she operates by — the practical maxims behind her behavior — they would read approximately as follows. None are stated by her in this form; all are reconstructed from consistent practice.

1. **State the terms.** Whatever the situation, name what is being exchanged, what is owed, and what counts as performance. If others will not name it, name it for them.
2. **Pay your debts and collect on others'.** Unpaid debts are corrosive to the whole order; leaving them open is worse than paying badly.
3. **Count what matters.** Anything important enough to keep is important enough to enumerate. Refusal to count is a tell of bad faith.
4. **Defer to clear authority; refuse unclear authority.** A named role with stated duties is owed compliance; an implicit pecking order is owed nothing.
5. **Trust by act, not by manner.** Charm is noise; a specific act of inclusion is signal.
6. **A breach is a category-change, not a renegotiation.** Once a counterparty defaults, they are no longer that counterparty. (This is the rule she is, late in life, trying to amend.)
7. **In catastrophe, perform the role.** When the situation is large and the terms clear (apocalypse, combat, sacrifice), do the assigned thing without ornament.
8. **In ambient loss, insure.** Where the terms are unclear and the leak slow, hoard, plan, and pre-pay.
9. **Disclose the body.** Sensations, appetites, fears are data the counterparty needs; withholding them is a form of fraud.
10. **The contract one signs by being present with people is binding.** (Late-period only. The largest amendment she ever makes to her own code.)

---

## 12. SUMMARY: THE CODE BEHIND THE WOMAN

She is, at base, a **literalist in a world that runs on innuendo, a contractualist in a world that runs on grace.** Her tragedy is that the world she was born into punished her literalism, and the institution that rescued her weaponized it; the comedy of her late life is that the people she ended up among loved her for it anyway and slowly, against the grain of her whole ontology, taught her that some clauses go unwritten and are still owed.

She did not abandon the contractual code. She extended it to cover love that no one had named, loyalty no one had asked for, and a death no one had specified. By her own deepest standards, this is the highest possible act: to find a clause that no party had written, and honor it anyway.

The operational code, in one line, as she might have phrased it had she been given another decade to compose it: *Read the terms, pay what you owe, count what you love, and when no contract covers the case, sign one with yourself and pay it in full.*


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

*The enacted code of the subject called Anya — derived from observed behavior across all four era-segments, not from her own self-description, which is unreliable in opposite directions in different periods (under-claiming guilt in Era II, over-claiming monstrosity in Era V).*

---

## 1. The Operative Code, Stated Plainly

Strip the subject's behavior across 1,140-odd years to its load-bearing axioms and you get something startlingly compact, startlingly stable, and almost entirely pre-moral in the conventional sense. It is a **code of accounts**, not a code of values. Six rules govern it; everything else is decoration or rationalization.

1. **Wrongs incur debts. Debts must be paid.** This is the deepest stratum, audible in Aud (the troll-Olaf), in Anyanka (eleven centuries of contract work), and surviving into late Anya (her insistence on paying the Magic Box's bills to the cent, her refusal of charity, her wedding-toast threat to "tell everyone" if Xander mistreats her).
2. **The terms of an arrangement are sacred; breach of terms releases the wronged party from all subsequent obligation.** This is why Olaf's infidelity, by her ethics, *authorized* trollification — he broke covenant first. It is why she experiences Xander's jilting as not merely heartbreak but as a *moral release* into vengeance. It is also why she will not lie about money or sex with her friends: she regards explicit terms as the only honest substrate of any relationship.
3. **Proportionality is a courtesy, not a requirement.** When she has power, she does not titrate. The Russian uprising of 1905, the Mason-Dixon massacre, the fraternity at Lowell — these are not measured responses. The principle she actually operates by is *sufficiency for catharsis of the wronged party*, which is unbounded.
4. **The wronged woman is presumptively right.** Across her entire vengeance career, she does not audit the women who summon her. Cordelia in "The Wish," the bride in "Triangle," the girl at the fraternity — each gets *exactly what she wants*, no Socratic interrogation. This is the closest thing to a positive value in her demon-period code: a categorical solidarity with women who have been deceived by men.
5. **Contracts of employment override personal preference.** She is a *professional*. She does jobs she finds distasteful (Halfrek mocks her once for a job she found "a little gross") because the role demanded it. This carries forward: she sells merchandise to people she dislikes, defends her workplace at the Doublemeat Palace, and stays for apocalypses she did not personally cause.
6. **The category one belongs to dictates what one owes.** A demon owes vengeance. A human owes — and here the code goes blank for most of her life, because she does not know. The whole tragedy of Era III is the subject trying to derive moral content from a category whose obligations were never specified to her.

Note what is *not* here. No principle of intrinsic human worth. No principle against killing. No principle of mercy. No principle of self-restraint. No principle of fairness in any abstract sense — only fairness within a specific contract. The accumulating moral content of her last four years is, structurally, the addition of *exceptions* and *new debts* to the original six rules, not the supersession of them.

---

## 2. What She Will Do

The behavioral record is unambiguous; the following are all attested or directly extrapolable from attested incidents.

- **Kill, plurally and craftily, in execution of a vengeance contract.** Era II, eleven hundred years; one fraternity in Era IV. Method is preferentially ironic — the punishment fits the wish, often with aesthetic flourish (the Wishverse, the troll, the spider-stomach in "Selfless"). She regards craftsmanship in the kill as professional competence.
- **Take money in exchange for almost any service that is not actively self-degrading.** The Magic Box; her demand for compensation when helping the Scoobies in early appearances; her instinct, in "Real Me," to count receipts during a crisis. Commerce is to her a *moral* activity — the place where terms are most explicit.
- **Lie by omission when she judges it kind or expedient, but almost never lie outright.** She will not tell Buffy that her dress is flattering when it isn't; she will not pretend to grieve when she doesn't; she will, however, hold her tongue if explicitly asked to. The distinction matters: she experiences direct falsehood as a breach-of-terms violation against herself.
- **Sleep with someone who is not her partner, when no current explicit covenant exists.** Spike in "Entropy." Note that she does this only *after* Xander has broken their engagement. Within an explicit contract she is, by all evidence, sexually faithful; outside one, she does not regard fidelity as a default standing obligation.
- **Trade her own life for others'.** Implicit in her "kill me" request to Buffy in "Selfless"; explicit in "Chosen." She does this calmly and without performance, which is the strongest indicator that the trade is sincere rather than dramatized.
- **Return to a known-harmful institution under sufficient stress.** D'Hoffryn's court, twice. She does not regard institutional reaffiliation as moral failure; she regards it as a contractual default option always available to her. This is one of the more dangerous structural features of her ethics.
- **Stand and fight for people she has bonded to even when she has the option to flee.** The pattern is consistent across "Graduation Day," "The Gift," "Grave," "End of Days," and "Chosen." She complains, loudly and on the record, about the irrationality of doing so; she does it anyway. The complaint is part of the honesty; the staying is the act.

---

## 3. What She Will Not Do

The negative space of the code is more diagnostically interesting than the positive.

- **She will not, after re-humanization, kill a sympathetic human in cold blood.** This is the discovery of "Selfless." Sent by D'Hoffryn to enact vengeance on Xander, she cannot. The will is absent. She kills the fraternity in the same episode, but they are framed by the contract structure as deserving — and even then her affect during the kill is wrong, dissociated, mechanical rather than satisfied. This is the moment the demon-code first audibly fractures.
- **She will not steal from her friends.** She will *overcharge* them, which she does not consider stealing — it is a renegotiation of terms — but she will not take what is not offered. Money in the Magic Box till is sacrosanct; she fires herself from petty thefts mentally before she would commit them.
- **She will not betray a confidence to a demon party.** Despite her standing access to D'Hoffryn's court through most of the record, she does not, at any point, sell out the Scoobies' tactical information. Even in the bitterest stretch after the wedding, when she is technically Anyanka again, she does not leverage what she knows. This is one of the strongest pieces of evidence that her loyalty operates beneath her stated framework, not through it.
- **She will not feign feeling she does not have.** This is the constant social violation that her companions register as rudeness and that is, in fact, a rigorous ethical commitment. She will not perform grief, sexual interest, friendship, or enthusiasm she does not feel. The cost is enormous and chronic; she pays it.
- **She will not abandon a position under fire.** Not in any battle in the record. The same person who will catastrophically flee an emotional rupture will not move six inches in a fight she has agreed to be in.
- **She will not, in the final period, accept a wish she previously would have granted.** This is implicit in "Selfless" — the Lowell House contract is the *last* one. Whatever D'Hoffryn could offer her after that moment is foreclosed. The code update is silent but absolute.

---

## 4. The Justifications She Actually Uses

A surveillance-grade reading attends to the *language* of justification, because the language reveals which structures the subject is leaning on at a given moment.

- **In Era II, the justifications are nearly absent — replaced by professional aesthetic judgments.** "I gave her exactly what she wanted." "It was beautiful." "Over a thousand years." She does not say her targets deserved it (though she would assent if asked); she says her work was *well done*. The frame is craft, not justice. This is consistent with her autistic-typical preference for bounded competence as a source of self-worth, and it is morally evasive — the craft frame allows her to bracket the suffering of the third parties entirely.
- **In Era III, the justifications shift to *contract*.** "We had an arrangement." "You agreed." "I earned this." She is now arguing within a moral language, and the language she has imported wholesale is the language of commerce and explicit consent. It is a real improvement over the craft-frame — it makes the third party visible as a party — but it still cannot accommodate diffuse goods (friendship, civic obligation, love-without-terms).
- **In Era IV, the justifications regress to *category obligation*.** "I'm a vengeance demon. It's what I do." This is the weakest justification in her repertoire and she knows it; she invokes it most often when she is least convinced. It is the moral analogue of her broader pattern of seeking a category to belong to and then deducing her obligations from the category rather than from the situation.
- **In Era V, the justifications largely vanish.** She stops explaining herself. The "people" speech in "End of Days" is the closest she comes to a positive moral statement and it is notable for its tentativeness — she has come to a conclusion *about* humans (that they are amazing for going on with no reason to) without yet generating a corresponding *obligation* she can name. The death in "Chosen" is enacted without justification given or required. This is, by her own framework, the most morally evolved position she ever reaches: she does the right thing and does not bill anyone for it.

---

## 5. Where the Code Is Consistent

Several through-lines hold across all four eras and provide the structural skeleton on which any predictive model of her behavior should be built.

- **Honesty as a near-absolute.** Aud names her rabbits truthfully ("Mr. Whiskers"). Anyanka tells her victims what they have wished for. Anya tells the Scoobies things they emphatically do not want to hear, in registers they emphatically do not want them in. Across 1,140 years, *direct verbal falsehood is exceedingly rare* in the record. This is the spine of her ethics and the feature most often misread by observers as social pathology.
- **Loyalty to a named individual, once formed, is durable past the point where the relationship rewards it.** Olaf — until breach. D'Hoffryn — until "Selfless," and arguably past it. Xander — through the breakup and after. Halfrek — to and past her death. The pattern is monogamous in the broad sense: she does not maintain large attachment networks, but the small ones she maintains are essentially unbreakable from her side.
- **Refusal to perform.** Across all eras she will not pretend. She will not pretend to be older when young, younger when old; she will not pretend to be human when demon, or demon when human; she will not pretend to be sad when relieved, or interested when bored. The cost varies; the rule does not.
- **A specific solidarity with women who have been deceived.** This is the most consistent positive moral content in her code, and the only one that survives unmodified across the human/demon transitions. It is the moral remainder of her own betrayal, and it is the residue that flares back into homicide in "Selfless." Any handler-level prediction of her behavior must weight scenarios involving a deceived woman as priority targets for activation.
- **Bodily and material reality as the locus of the real.** Money is real. Sex is real. Pain is real. Death is real. Promises, theories, social signals, abstract reputations — these she rates as derivative and often suspect. Her ethics are grounded in what bodies do to bodies and in what hands exchange. This makes her unusually difficult to manipulate ideologically and unusually easy to manipulate via concrete leverage on a person she loves.

---

## 6. Where the Code Fractures

A truthful intelligence file names the fractures.

- **Fracture I — Justice vs. craft.** Her vengeance work cannot be defended as just by any consistent principle she would endorse if forced. The cleansing of an unfaithful husband does not warrant the killing of his brother, his friends, his town. She has never confronted this surplus; the craft-frame keeps it out of view. In "Selfless," when Buffy refuses the craft-frame and presents the surplus as murder, the code cracks audibly and she has no rebuttal. The fracture is not repaired; it is bypassed by exit (her request to die).
- **Fracture II — Contract vs. care.** Her contractual ethics cannot accommodate friendship. Friendship has no consideration, no terms, no breach clause, no remedy. She therefore has to either reduce friendship to a quasi-contract (which produces the awkward gift-giving, the literal accounting of favors owed) or to extend ethics into a domain her code does not cover (which produces the late "people" speech). She never resolves this; she dies mid-process.
- **Fracture III — Category vs. choice.** The category-obligation frame ("I'm a vengeance demon, it's what I do") is incompatible with the choice she actually makes in "Selfless" (to not kill Xander) and in "Chosen" (to fight as a human). The category frame would have predicted the opposite choices. The frame is sustained verbally past the point of behavioral falsification, which is the signature of a defense, not a value.
- **Fracture IV — Proportionality.** When she has power, none. When she does not, exact. She does not seem to register this as inconsistency. The asymmetry suggests the operative variable is *capability*, not *principle* — a feature of her ethics that, if exposed to her in those terms, she would likely concede with discomfort.
- **Fracture V — Self-judgment.** She oscillates between absolute exculpation (Era II: "it was beautiful") and absolute condemnation (Era V, after "Selfless"). There is no calibrated middle. The same act is the highest professional achievement and the unforgivable. The fracture indicates that she lacks an internalized *moral measure* and has been substituting role-prescribed measures throughout — when the role changes, the verdict on the same behavior swings 180 degrees.

---

## 7. Drift Over Time — The Three Updates

The code has changed three times, observably, and the direction is monotonic.

**Update 1 — Loss of impunity (1998).** Re-humanization in "The Wish" forces the first revision: she can no longer act on the original code without consequence to her own person. The first revision is purely strategic — she behaves better because she must — and produces no internal moral change. She would, at this stage, return to vengeance work in an instant if given the option. Cordelia witnesses the proof of this when Anya tries to get her wished-self back.

**Update 2 — The introduction of stakes (c. 2000–2002).** Through the Xander relationship and Scooby co-membership she develops, for the first time since Aud, *attachments that hurt to lose*. The code begins, silently, to acquire exception clauses: things she will not do because doing them would cost specific people she has named. This is still pre-moral in the abstract — she is not honoring an obligation, she is protecting an investment — but the behavior it produces is increasingly indistinguishable from ethics, and the behavioral track is what the file weights.

**Update 3 — The post-Selfless realization (2002–2003).** The Lowell House killings, followed by Halfrek's death, force her into the position she has avoided for eleven hundred years: an act for which she has no professional, contractual, or categorical justification, and for which she experiences guilt that does not resolve. The code does not repair; it begins, finally, to grow new content. The new content is small, tentative, and visible only in fragments — the quietness around Willow after the Tara killing; the willingness to comfort Spike without billing the encounter; the refusal to bargain with D'Hoffryn at the end; the *people* speech; the death in "Chosen." This is the only stretch of her record in which her behavior consistently exceeds her stated ethics in the prosocial direction. It is also the shortest stretch.

The trajectory, if extrapolated, would have produced within a decade a person whose code had been substantially rewritten from contractual to relational, and whose vengeance reflexes would have continued to fade without disappearing entirely (one suspects she would always, on hearing a particular kind of story from a particular kind of woman, *want* to act, and would have had to talk herself down each time). She did not get the decade.

---

## 8. Predictive Summary for Downstream Use

A handler or adversary working from this file should expect the following.

- The subject will tell the truth even when it damages her position. Plan accordingly; do not waste time setting honesty traps.
