- The subject will honor explicit agreements with a precision uncommon in human counterparties. Get terms in writing; she will keep them.
- The subject will not be moved by appeals to abstract values (human dignity, the greater good, patriotism, faith). She will be moved by appeals to named individuals she has bonded to, by debts she perceives as owed, and by craft pride in a bounded task.
- The subject's ethical reflexes can be activated, with high reliability, by the presentation of a wronged woman seeking redress against a deceiving man. This is the single most exploitable feature of her code and the one most likely to override her late-period restraint.
- The subject under acute stress will regress to category-based ethics and seek reaffiliation with a prior institutional identity. The window in which this can be intercepted by a trusted attachment figure is narrow but real.
- The subject will trade her own life for another's, calmly, if the trade is presented to her as a clear contract with a specific named beneficiary. She will not trade it for an abstraction. The file should record that she did, in the end, do exactly this — and that the beneficiaries were strangers, which means the code, in its final state, had quietly extended the category of *named individuals one owes* to include *the species*. That is the last entry.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE — SUBJECT "ANYA"

*Compiled from longitudinal verbal record, 1998–2003, cross-referenced against fragmentary self-report regarding the Aud (pre-880 CE) and Anyanka (880–1998, 2002) periods. Subject's speech is among the most distinctive in the entire Sunnydale cohort and arguably the most diagnostically transparent: she leaks information at a rate substantially above baseline for any other observed party, and the leaks are patterned.*

---

## 1. Baseline Register and Acoustic Profile

The subject speaks in a flat-to-bright American English with no detectable substrate of her natal language (Old Norse / proto-Scandinavian per the Aud-era self-report), no period diction left over from any of her intervening centuries, and no demonic phonological residue. This is itself notable. Eleven hundred years of multilingual operational life have been overwritten by what appears to be a deliberately acquired late-twentieth-century Californian idiolect, modeled — the canon strongly suggests — on whatever speech she heard first and most after re-humanization in 1998: the Sunnydale High peer group. She is, in this sense, a *linguistic mimic who chose her donors badly*: her English is a teenager's English, retained into a chronological adulthood, which contributes to the persistent uncanniness of her register.

**Prosody.** Pitch is mid-range, with a tendency to terminal rises on declaratives when she is uncertain whether she has spoken correctly and terminal falls — abrupt, conclusive — when she is delivering what she believes to be a factual or contractual statement. The contrast is sharp enough to serve as a reliable affect-state indicator: rising = checking, falling = asserting. There is essentially no middle contour. She does not modulate for the gentle, hedged, socially lubricating register that most native speakers default to in casual exchange.

**Rate.** Variable and stress-correlated. At baseline she speaks slightly faster than the Scooby median, with very few filled pauses ("um," "uh," "like") — far fewer than her age-presenting peers, another tell that English is acquired rather than native. Under stress, rate increases dramatically and clause-boundaries collapse: she produces long compound sentences with stacked subordinate clauses, often inventorying her concerns in serial order ("And then this, and then this, and also this") rather than prioritizing. Under acute distress, rate paradoxically *slows* and she becomes flatly declarative — the dissociative-competence register noted in §5 of the workup.

**Volume.** Loud baseline, particularly in private/domestic settings where she has no register-calibration. She does not whisper effectively; her "whispers" are stage-whispers, audible across rooms. This is consistent throughout the record and is treated by the cohort as a recurring comic embarrassment (she announces sexual activity at audible volume in shop, home, and battlefield settings alike).

---

## 2. Diction and Lexicon

Three lexical fields dominate her speech:

**(a) The economic register.** "Money," "cash," "currency," "dollars," "profit," "customers," "merchandise," "inventory," "ka-ching." This is the densest lexical cluster in her record after roughly 2000, when she begins managing the Magic Box. She refers to money with the same affect that other speakers reserve for romantic partners or religious objects — she greets it, addresses it directly, sometimes physically caresses bills on screen. The vocabulary is precise (she distinguishes profit from revenue, gross from net, in casual speech) and is deployed both as genuine interest and as defensive filler when emotional content threatens to surface.

**(b) The bodily-clinical register.** "Orgasm" (her preferred term, used at noticeably higher frequency than any synonym), "penis," "intercourse," "menstrual," "ejaculation," "anatomy." She avoids slang substitutions almost completely; where peers say "sex" she will often specify the mechanical referent. This is not prurience — the affect is flat, almost taxonomic. It reads as someone who learned the words from a textbook or a pamphlet and has not yet absorbed the social conventions that govern their deployment.

**(c) The contractual-legal register.** "Wish," "terms," "vengeance," "justice," "warranted," "punishment," "deserve," "owe." This is the residual professional vocabulary of the Anyanka period and surfaces especially when she is morally aroused. It is a register she never fully unlearns, and one of the cleanest diagnostic markers when she is reverting toward demon-self: the contract words return before the demon does.

**Conspicuously absent or impoverished registers.** She has almost no vocabulary for *hedged emotion*. The words "maybe," "kind of," "sort of," "I guess," "I feel like," "it's just that" — the entire English apparatus for socially-padded affect — appear at a fraction of expected frequency. She does not say "I'm a little upset"; she says "I am very angry" or she says nothing. Similarly, her religious/spiritual vocabulary is bizarrely sparse for someone who spent a millennium in a literal supernatural cosmology — she names entities (D'Hoffryn, Halfrek, the Lower Beings) but does not generalize them into theological abstractions. Her ontology is populated, not principled.

**Malapropism and pragmatic misfire.** She produces what looks superficially like malapropism but is in fact something stranger: she uses correct words in technically correct meanings that violate pragmatic constraint. She does not say "infer" when she means "imply"; she says "I find you suddenly very attractive sexually" when she means "I like you." The lexicon is right; the *situation* is wrong. This is one of the cleanest behavioral markers of the broader-phenotype autistic profile noted in the workup.

---

## 3. Sentence Architecture

Her preferred syntactic structures are revealing.

**(a) The declarative inventory.** She lists. Faced with a complex situation, she will produce a numbered or quasi-numbered enumeration of components ("Okay, so: there are demons, we have weapons, Xander is annoying me, and I am hungry"). The mental model is itemized rather than narrativized. This is the same architecture that makes her a competent bookkeeper and a poor consoler.

**(b) The transactional conditional.** "If X, then Y" structures are over-represented. She thinks in contracts at the grammatical level. When she proposes an action she will frequently structure it as a quid-pro-quo even where none is required ("If you do the dishes, I will reward you with sexual congress"). She extends this even to grief and apology, which is part of why her attempts at consolation read as so peculiar.

**(c) The blurted disclosure.** A signature pattern: a sentence begins on-topic, runs through a relevant clause, and then — without intonational warning — appends a private piece of information that ought to have been filtered ("We should get going, the demons are gathering, and also Xander and I had loud sex this morning"). The appended clause is delivered at the same prosodic weight as the others. This is a *pragmatic-filter failure*, not a deliberate provocation, and remains stable across the entire record though it lessens slightly in the final season.

**(d) The terminated question.** She asks questions and then answers them herself, often before the addressee can speak. This is most pronounced in early seasons when she is uncertain of social rules and treats interaction as a script to be completed.

**(e) The aborted sentence — late only.** A new pattern in the final season: sentences started and abandoned, trailing off, sometimes replaced with silence. This was not in her repertoire in earlier years. Its emergence coincides with the post-"Selfless" period and marks the development of, for the first time, something a competent observer would have to call self-monitoring.

---

## 4. Communication of Love

Her romantic-affective speech moves through three distinct phases.

**Early Xander period (1999–2000).** Love is communicated in propositions and inventories. She tells him she finds him attractive; she tells him she wishes to engage in sexual activity; she informs him of her schedule and asks him to fit himself into it. There is no metaphor. The vocabulary is borrowed from the categories she does have — economic exchange, physical mechanism — because the relational categories are still vacant. When she is moved, she becomes more explicit, not more poetic.

**Middle period (2000–2002).** A halting, partially-successful acquisition of conventional romantic register. She produces, with visible effort, lines like "I love you" and "I want to spend my life with you," and the production is observably effortful — she sets them up, pauses before them, and watches Xander's face afterward for confirmation that she has performed the line correctly. The wedding-vow draft she writes ("Hells Bells") is a key document in her file: it is a literal accounting of her future intentions toward him, structurally indistinguishable from a contract, but suffused with what reads as genuine devotional intent. She has learned to write love letters in the only genre she knows.

**Late period (2002–2003).** Love is communicated, when at all, in negative space: in things she does not say, in the absence of the chatter that previously filled silences with him, in the small physical accommodations she begins to perform without announcing them. The "Entropy" encounter with Spike is verbally minimal on her part — she is, for once, almost wordless — and what speech she produces is grief-coded rather than appetite-coded.

The signature: *she will say something declarative and economic and slightly off, and then her face will do work her voice will not*. The verbal channel is the channel she controls; the somatic channel is where her actual affect leaks.

---

## 5. Communication of Threat

Threat language in the subject's record divides into two utterly different modes.

**Anyanka-mode.** Formal, near-ritual, semi-theatrical. The threat is the work product. It is delivered in a register slightly elevated above her baseline — more archaic vocabulary, more parallel structure, more invocation of the wronged party's grievance as a frame. "I, Anyanka, hear your plea" and its analogues. This is professional speech, and it carries the affective signature of pride in craft rather than personal animus. When she threatens *in this mode* she is fully composed and her diction is the cleanest it ever is.

**Anya-mode threats.** Awkward, often domestic, frequently inserted at the wrong moment ("If you hurt him, I will cause you to suffer in ways I have, at the moment, not invented yet"). These are real — she will, if powered, follow through — but they are delivered in the register of grocery-list grievance. The wedding-toast threat to former vengeance-targets at her own engagement party is the canonical example: a guest list of past victims announced as boasting.

**Diagnostic note.** When her threats lose their playful or grandiose framing and become flat, short, and concrete ("I'll kill you"), the threat is operative. This shift in register is the single most reliable verbal marker of true intent-to-harm in her file. She becomes, in the moment before violence, briefly *normal-sounding*. This is the inverse of most subjects, in whom escalation is marked by stylization; in her, escalation is marked by stylistic compression.

---

## 6. Communication of Grief

Grief is the affect she has the worst vocabulary for, because grief in her natal cosmology was foreclosed — Aud did not grieve Olaf, she punished him; Anyanka did not grieve, she contracted. The human Anya is therefore a grief-illiterate person trying to acquire a grief register in real time, mostly from observation of Buffy, Willow, and Xander.

**Joyce's death ("Forever").** Her speech in that scene is the textbook artifact and worth catalogue-quoting in summary: she asks concrete procedural questions about death (what happens to the body, why there is a ceremony, what one is supposed to do) in a tone of genuine confusion. She is mocked for the inappropriateness and then defended by Willow when it becomes clear she is not being cruel. This is a person who has *witnessed* a thousand years of death without ever attending a funeral as a mourner. The verbal pattern — interrogative, concrete, procedurally-oriented — is her grief register throughout the rest of the record.

**Tara's death and Willow's collapse.** She is markedly quieter than usual. Her speech in this period is shorter-clause, more checking-in, fewer blurted disclosures. She has learned that there are situations in which her default loudness is inappropriate, even if she has not learned what the appropriate alternative is. The compensatory strategy is silence.

**Her own grief at being jilted ("Hells Bells" / "Entropy").** She does not initially produce a grief register at all — she produces a vengeance register, because that is the script the situation triggers. The slow re-emergence of grief over the following episodes is marked by a striking new linguistic feature: *self-reference in the past tense*. She begins to refer to "the person I was" and "what I thought I was doing," which is essentially a new grammatical move in her record and the verbal signature of her late-period self-revision.

---

## 7. Deflection, Avoidance, and Defensive Speech

Her deflections are unusually identifiable because she is a poor deflector. Most people deflect by indirection; she deflects by *substitution of register*. The mechanism is:

- When emotional content threatens to surface, she pivots into the **economic register**. ("Anya, are you okay?" "We sold three orbs today, that's eighty-five percent margin.")
- When intimate vulnerability is requested, she pivots into the **bodily-clinical register**, often weaponized to discomfort the asker into changing topic.
- When her past is invoked, she pivots into the **contractual register** and recites it as résumé — listing centuries, regions, notable jobs, as if the request had been for a CV.

These pivots are *legible*. A trained observer can identify her stress level in any given conversation by counting register-switches per minute. The pivots also tend to escalate in absurdity as the threat increases, which produces the surface impression of inappropriateness or insensitivity but is more accurately read as panic-response.

A separate deflective mechanism: **technical literalism in answer to non-literal questions**. "How are you?" answered as a survey of physical states. "What do you think?" answered with a frequency distribution. This is partly the autistic profile; it is also functionally evasive, because it prevents the asker from extracting the requested emotional content.

She does not lie well. Her record contains very few attempts at deception and most of them fail within a sentence or two; her preferred deception strategy is *omission combined with confident topic-change*, and even this is detectable by anyone tracking her register-switching.

---

## 8. Verbal Tics, Catchphrases, and Idiosyncratic Forms

- **"Bunnies."** The single word that functions for her as a stress-trigger, an exclamation, and on at least one occasion an extended musical complaint. Her pronunciation of the word becomes notably tighter and higher-pitched than her baseline vowels.
- **Frequency adverbs.** "Constantly," "always," "never," "every," "all the time" — used with uncalibrated absoluteness where peers would hedge.
- **Address-by-full-name.** She addresses people, particularly Xander, by full name more often than peers do, and tends to introduce herself with formal completeness even in casual settings.
- **"Humans."** She refers to humans as a third-person category for years into her own re-humanization. The pronoun usage ("you humans," then "we humans," then eventually unmarked "we") tracks her categorical re-affiliation over time and is one of the cleanest longitudinal markers in her record.
- **D'Hoffryn invocations.** Phrases like "By the pleasing aroma of D'Hoffryn" appear as semi-oaths well into the human period. She never fully expunges the demonic idiomatic substrate; it surfaces under stress and under levity in roughly equal measure.
- **Numerical specificity.** She quotes exact numbers — years, dollars, body counts, orgasm counts — where vague quantifiers would be normal. Her file is a treasure trove of unintentional metrics.
- **"Mister."** She uses the honorific "Mister" in odd places — "Mister Manners," "Mister Funny-Pants," "Mister I'm-So-Big-and-Strong" — as a sarcasm marker. This is a sub-pattern stable enough to be a fingerprint.
- **Apostrophizing inanimates.** She speaks to money, to merchandise, to the cash register. These are not metaphors; she addresses them in second person and waits, briefly, in a way that suggests the boundary between addressed and addressee is, for her, weak.

---

## 9. Code-Switching and Cross-Context Variation

She maintains essentially **one register across all contexts**, which is itself diagnostic. Most adult speakers shift markedly between work, intimate, professional, and combat registers. She does not. The Magic Box customer hears approximately the same Anya as the Scooby strategy meeting, the bedroom, and the demon negotiation. There are micro-shifts — slightly more economic vocabulary at the shop, slightly more bodily-clinical at home — but no genuine code-switch.

The exception is the Anyanka register, which she puts on like a uniform when she resumes that identity and which is a true register-shift: vocabulary, prosody, pronoun usage, and syntactic preference all change. The presence or absence of this register is a binary diagnostic for which identity is currently operative.

A second exception, very late: in the final season, with Buffy and with Halfrek separately, she demonstrates the first true intimate register of her record — quieter, slower, less inventoried, more aborted-sentence. It is fragile and rare and present only with women she trusts. It is the verbal evidence of the prognosis the workup describes as "cautiously hopeful."

---

## 10. Tells — A Compact Reference

For operational use, the following verbal markers should be tracked:

1. **Register-switch frequency** is the primary stress index. Three or more switches per minute indicates moderate distress; sustained single-register speech for unusually long stretches indicates either acute dissociative competence or genuine calm — disambiguate by prosody (flat = dissociative, modulated = calm).
2. **Pronoun drift on "we/they humans"** indicates her current categorical self-placement; reversion to "you humans" is a serious destabilization signal.
3. **Re-emergence of contractual vocabulary** ("terms," "wish," "deserve," "owe") in personal contexts precedes vengeance-mode reversion by, in the one observed case, hours.
4. **Compression of threat register** — short, plain, declarative threats — indicates true intent. Florid threats are performative.
5. **Aborted sentences** indicate genuine self-monitoring and are, paradoxically, a *positive* prognostic sign; their absence in late-record interactions would indicate regression.
6. **Bunny-mentions** are involuntary distress vocalizations and should be logged regardless of the conversational context in which they appear.
7. **Silence in her** is anomalous and meaningful. She fills space by default; when she does not, something has reached her that she has no register for. Most of her real disclosures, when they come, come after silences — not within speech.

---

The overall picture is of a speaker whose words are easier to read than she knows, because the architecture of her speech was assembled too late and too piecemeal to acquire the camouflaging conventions native speakers use to hide themselves. She is, linguistically, naked. The whole apparatus of small talk, hedging, polite circumlocution — the verbal equivalent of clothing — she never quite put on. What makes her case unusual in the broader cohort is that the nakedness is not a stylistic choice or a defect of socialization in the ordinary sense; it is the trace of an entire human developmental window that was, for her, occupied by something else entirely. Every sentence she speaks is, in a small way, a recovery effort.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*A behavioral forecast engine. Each entry: a GIVEN condition (situation, stimulus, or social input the canonical record never depicts) and the EXPECTED behavior, derived from the longitudinal pattern in §§1–5. Confidence is graded HIGH / MODERATE / SPECULATIVE based on density of corroborating canon. Where escalation paths exist, they are mapped.*

---

## A. WAKING, BODY, AND THE SOLO DAY

**GIVEN: Subject wakes alone in her apartment, no scheduled obligation until midday.**
EXPECT: Immediate verbal self-orientation — she will speak aloud on waking, even with no auditor present. A run-through of the day's plan delivered in declarative sentences ("Today I will go to the bank, then the store, then I will buy lunch"). Subject does not tolerate unstructured time; the first act of the day is the imposition of a schedule on it. She makes the bed with hospital-corner precision (carryover from Magic Box inventory habits — she organizes objects in space the way she organizes ledgers). HIGH confidence.

**GIVEN: Subject has a head cold.**
EXPECT: Catastrophic verbalization. She will narrate symptoms in clinical detail to anyone within range — temperature in Fahrenheit, mucus consistency, throat pain on a self-invented numeric scale. Underneath the comic register is genuine alarm: a body that produces unpredictable fluids is, to her, evidence of mortality in progress. She will measure medication doses precisely, take them on the dot, and re-take her temperature at fixed intervals. She will also overconsume citrus — she retains folk-remedy habits from the Aud era and will trust them above pharmaceutical instructions. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject menstruates.**
EXPECT: Calendar-tracked to the hour. She experienced this for perhaps two or three years as Aud before the transformation; the return of it in 1998 was a shock she absorbed by quantification. She buys supplies in bulk, stores them visibly, and references the cycle in conversation without filter ("I am bleeding today, so I am irritable, so do not ask me about the inventory until Thursday"). HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject cannot sleep.**
EXPECT: She gets out of bed within twenty minutes — does not lie still. Insomnia activates the death-anxiety substrate immediately; horizontal stillness in the dark replicates too closely the imagined state of being dead. She will turn on every light in the apartment, count cash, reconcile a ledger, or reorganize a drawer until physical exhaustion overrides the loop. She does not read for pleasure under stress; reading requires the kind of associative cognition that fails her at 3 a.m. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject is alone for a full weekend with no contact from the group.**
EXPECT: Day one — productive, almost euphoric: deep-cleans, runs errands, optimizes some system in the shop. Day two — degrades. By afternoon she is calling someone with a manufactured pretext ("I needed to confirm the Tuesday meeting"). The pretext is transparent and she knows it; what she cannot tolerate is asking directly for company. The transactional frame is a face-saving device for an attachment request she has no other grammar for. HIGH.

---

## B. MONEY, COMMERCE, AND THE TRANSACTIONAL FRAME

**GIVEN: Subject is overcharged $1.40 at a grocery checkout.**
EXPECT: She will halt the line. Not from rudeness — from a conviction that contractual error is a moral matter. She itemizes the receipt aloud, identifies the discrepancy, and refuses to leave the register until reconciled. Manager-summoning is on the table within two minutes. She is incapable of the small American social gesture of letting a small overcharge go to preserve the queue's comfort; the queue's comfort is not in her calculus. HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject is given a gift with no occasion attached.**
EXPECT: Visible confusion, then suspicion. Gifts in her schema are exchanges — birthday for birthday, favor for favor. A gift without a hook reads to her as either an upcoming ask (she will brace for it) or a coded romantic overture (she will misread platonic affection as proposition). She will ask the giver, literally, "What do you want?" — and mean it cleanly. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject is asked to lend money to a friend.**
EXPECT: She agrees but produces a written note with terms, including interest at a modest rate. She does not understand that the written instrument is, to her counterparty, an insult; she understands it as a kindness, because writing terms down protects both parties from future ambiguity, which is the thing that destroys relationships. If asked to waive the note, she will, reluctantly, and will privately track the debt in a ledger anyway. HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject negotiates the price of a used car.**
EXPECT: Extremely effective. She has no embarrassment about silence, no need to fill the social pressure with concessions, and a thousand years of contract-craft. She will walk away from a bad deal three times before lunch. She will, however, fixate on the price to the exclusion of mechanical due diligence — she does not naturally model second-order consequences in domains where she has no schema. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: A tip-jar at a café.**
EXPECT: She tips, but exactly the displayed-customary amount, calculated to the cent, never rounded up. Rounding up reads to her as innumeracy. She will, however, tip in coin so she can hear it land — auditory confirmation of the transaction. SPECULATIVE-MODERATE.

---

## C. FOOD, DRINK, AND APPETITE

**GIVEN: Subject orders at a restaurant.**
EXPECT: She reads the menu beginning to end before speaking, takes the longest of any party member, and asks the server one or two questions that the server will find faintly aggressive (volume of dish, exact contents). She orders the same thing on return visits — once a satisfactory contract with a kitchen has been established she does not revise it. She finishes her plate completely; food-waste is offensive to a worldview formed in a subsistence village. HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject is offered an unfamiliar cuisine.**
EXPECT: Outwardly performative enthusiasm, inwardly cataloguing. She will eat it and report the verdict in measurable terms ("the spice level is approximately equal to last week's Thai, the texture is unpleasant but tolerable"). If she dislikes a dish she says so to the cook directly, which she experiences as honesty and they experience as cruelty. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject has had three drinks.**
EXPECT: Disinhibition along axes already loose. She becomes more transactional, not less — proposes deals, recounts vengeance anecdotes with insufficient discretion, attempts to settle running interpersonal grievances on the spot. She is a clinging, anecdotal, occasionally weepy drunk, not a fighting one. The canon datum from "Triangle" — aggressive then weepy — generalizes. She does not vomit; she goes silent and falls asleep upright. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject is offered coffee.**
EXPECT: She drinks it strong and black with sugar — sugar is the legible reward signal, milk muddies the contract. She holds the cup with both hands. She uses caffeine instrumentally, never socially. HIGH.

---

## D. ROUTINES, ROUTES, AND SPATIAL HABITS

**GIVEN: Subject walks from her apartment to the Magic Box.**
EXPECT: One route, fixed, traversed at a steady fast pace, on the right-hand side of the sidewalk regardless of traffic flow. She does not window-shop. She nods to recognized merchants on the route — a fixed inventory of about six — and does not engage in conversation with them; the nod is the protocol. She times the walk and complains if it varies by more than two minutes from baseline. HIGH.

**GIVEN: Construction or a closure forces a detour.**
EXPECT: Visible irritation, then a swift re-optimization. She is good at this — recalculation is a bounded task. Once a new route is plotted she will commit to it the same way she committed to the old one, but for several days she will reference the construction with hostility, as a personal slight. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject in a crowd (festival, sale, parade).**
EXPECT: Discomfort masked by transactional activity. If she can attach herself to a vendor's table or a Scooby's elbow she stabilizes. Untethered in a moving crowd she becomes brittle and short-tongued. Her ability to track the eyes of many strangers is poor; she defaults to scanning for known faces and hands-near-her-purse. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject seated at a table — restaurant, meeting, Magic Box.**
EXPECT: Back to a wall when possible. Demon-period habit; the human period has not unlearned it. Hands stay on the table or on a counted object (cash, a pen, a glass). Empty hands invite a verbal tic. HIGH.

---

## E. PHONE, MAIL, AND MEDIATED CONTACT

**GIVEN: The phone rings.**
EXPECT: She answers on the second ring — not the first (looks desperate), not the fourth (looks rude). She identifies herself by full first name and surname even on personal lines. She does not employ small talk; the call opens with the business of the call. She ends calls abruptly, without the social-American "okay, talk to you later" ramp-down; the contract is complete, the channel closes. HIGH.

**GIVEN: An answering machine collects a message from a friend.**
EXPECT: She replays the message twice — once for content, once for affective parsing she did not catch the first time. She returns the call within an hour, with a written note of the bullet points she intends to address. She finds voicemail anxiety-provoking precisely because tone-of-voice carries the social information she is least equipped to decode. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject receives a letter from a stranger.**
EXPECT: Opened immediately at the mailbox, read standing. Junk mail is offensive — she sees it as a forced contract she did not consent to — and she will write back at least once in her life to a credit-card offer informing them, in formal language, of her displeasure. SPECULATIVE-MODERATE.

---

## F. STRANGERS, AUTHORITY, AND CIVIC LIFE

**GIVEN: Subject is approached by a panhandler.**
EXPECT: She stops, listens to the request, and treats it as a transaction. If she gives, she gives a precise amount and expects a specific verbal acknowledgment. If she refuses, she explains why ("I do not believe your story about the bus fare; you asked the same of three others on this block"). She does not perform the urban-American non-engagement; her categories do not include the polite pretense of not having heard. HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject pulled over by police for a minor traffic matter.**
EXPECT: Compliant, literal, dangerously over-disclosing. She will answer every question fully and offer adjacent information not requested. She has no functional concept of the right to silence; she has the demon-era reflex that explicit cooperation with an authority structure is the fast resolution. She does not lie well to a uniform. The encounter ends without escalation unless the officer mistakes her literalism for sarcasm — a real risk. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject votes.**
EXPECT: She votes. Civic procedure is contractual, and she honors contracts. She researches candidates by reading their printed materials end-to-end and votes the local ballot completely, including obscure judicial races. She is suspicious of campaign rhetoric and trusts itemized policy documents; she will vote for a dull competent candidate over a charismatic one nine times out of ten. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject in a doctor's waiting room.**
EXPECT: Punctual to the minute. She fills the intake form completely and accurately, including the question about prior surgeries, where she may write "see attached" and attach a separate sheet that begins in 880 CE. With a human-appearing physician she rapidly translates; with one she trusts, she does not. She reports pain in numeric scales without performance, asks for the exact name of every drug prescribed, and goes home and looks them up. HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject in a long DMV line.**
EXPECT: Acute distress, expressed as commentary. She narrates the inefficiency to whoever is nearest. She does not budge from line, does not abandon process; she completes the transaction and remembers the agent's name for years. MODERATE.

---

## G. SOCIAL EVENTS AND GROUP DYNAMICS

**GIVEN: Subject invited to a party of mostly strangers.**
EXPECT: Arrives precisely on the stated start time, which is wrong by American convention by about forty-five minutes. Brings a gift, wrapped, with a tag. Within ten minutes she has either attached herself to the host or the food table. Conversation she initiates begins with a direct personal question of the kind most people consider a third-meeting topic ("What do you do for money? Are you married? Do you want to be?"). She is remembered. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: Subject at a wedding (post-2002, post-Hells Bells).**
EXPECT: She accepts the invitation, attends, and is visibly destabilized through the ceremony — eyes elsewhere, body very still. She is markedly better at the reception, where there is a contractual frame (eat, drink, dance, give gift). She will not catch a bouquet. She will leave before the cake-cutting, citing a fabricated obligation. HIGH for the avoidance, MODERATE for the specific timing.

**GIVEN: Subject at a funeral.**
EXPECT: The "Body" speech from canon is the template — she says the wrong thing because she is trying to say the right thing without the social grammar for euphemism. She approaches the bereaved directly and asks the questions she actually wants answered. With family she trusts (Xander, in the alternate timeline where she lives), she becomes the practical executor — she will manage logistics, payments, and casseroles, because grief in others activates her competence. HIGH.

**GIVEN: A baby is held out to her to hold.**
EXPECT: Genuine, undefended terror — different in register from the rabbit phobia, more existential. Babies are concentrated mortality (fragile, demanding, transformative of the adult who holds them). She declines verbally and concretely ("No, thank you, I will drop it"). She is privately ashamed of the response. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: Small talk with a coworker about weather.**
EXPECT: Three to four turns before she pivots to substance — usually money, weather-as-economic-input, or a personal disclosure that ends the small talk. She does not enjoy weather-talk. She does, however, comment specifically on temperature in numeric terms more than the average speaker, because her body's thermoregulation is something she has consciously learned. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: She is teased lightly by a friend.**
EXPECT: Initial literal response (defending the position teased), then — late-period — a delayed laugh as the joke parses. The lag is the diagnostic. With Xander the lag shortens to near-zero by S6; with strangers it remains conspicuous. HIGH.

**GIVEN: A sexual joke at a mixed-company dinner.**
EXPECT: She matches or exceeds it, immediately, with clinical detail, derailing the table. She is genuinely confused by the resultant silence — the contract of the topic was opened, why is participation now penalized? MODERATE-HIGH.

---

## H. WORK AND THE MAGIC BOX

**GIVEN: Subject opens the shop alone in the morning.**
EXPECT: Fixed sequence — door, register, lights, inventory glance, broom, kettle. The sequence varies by no element. Cash drawer count is the second act of the day, before kettle on a busy week, after kettle on a slow one. She prefers to open alone; the ritual is meditative. HIGH.

**GIVEN: A customer attempts to shoplift a small ritual item.**
EXPECT: Confrontation, loud, immediate, without de-escalation training. The category of theft activates the moral-binary engine that ran the vengeance career; her response is closer to outrage than to commercial loss-mitigation. She will physically block the door if she has to. The shoplifter is rarely the one who escalates further. HIGH.

**GIVEN: A vendor delivers wrong stock.**
EXPECT: She refuses the shipment at the door, makes the driver wait while she writes a discrepancy memo, and signs nothing. She will fax (or, post-fax, e-mail) a follow-up the same hour. She develops over time a reputation among local suppliers as exact, harsh, and never wrong; preferential pricing follows, which she experiences as natural reward for craft. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: A regular customer is in tears at the counter.**
EXPECT: Early-period — flat awkwardness, possibly an inappropriate quip. Late-period — a tissue handed across the counter, a glass of water, a chair pulled up, and silence. She has learned the protocol by observation (likely from Tara) and executes it precisely; she does not improvise comfort, she deploys it as a kit. The customer often feels surprisingly held. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject asked to train a new employee.**
EXPECT: Excellent technical instruction, terrible affective management. She gives written procedures, demands recall on day two, and corrects errors in front of customers. Employees either thrive on the structural clarity or quit within a week. There is no middle outcome. HIGH.

---

## I. DOMESTIC LIFE AND COHABITATION (with Xander; transferable model)

**GIVEN: Shared apartment, weekday evening.**
EXPECT: She is home first; she has eaten or is eating on a schedule; she logs his late arrival without complaint but does mention the duration in passing. The apartment is hers in organization (filing system, kitchen layout) and his in mess (which she tolerates within zones — bathroom yes, kitchen no). She insists on a weekly accounting conversation, fifteen minutes, Sunday evening, of finances and the coming week's logistics. HIGH for the meeting; MODERATE for the timing.

**GIVEN: A disagreement about household labor.**
EXPECT: She quantifies. She produces a count of dishwashing turns over the prior month. Her case is airtight and infuriating. The fight is not about dishes; it is about whether quantification is a legitimate move in an intimate dispute. She does not understand why it is not. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: Partner is sick in bed.**
EXPECT: She is a superb nurse — fluids on a timetable, medication labeled, soup made from a recipe she will follow exactly. She is also a hovering one, and she will narrate the patient's symptoms back to him at intervals he finds unsettling. She does not catch what he has; she has been ill perhaps four times since 1998 and treats her own immune system as a personal asset. HIGH.

**GIVEN: A houseguest stays one night.**
EXPECT: Linens laid out in advance, breakfast inventoried, departure time confirmed at check-in. She is hospitable in a Scandinavian-village register that reads to coastal Americans as faintly martial. The houseguest leaves feeling correctly hosted and slightly evaluated. MODERATE.

---

## J. LEISURE, RECREATION, AND HOBBIES

**GIVEN: Subject has a free Saturday.**
EXPECT: She does not idle. The day is organized around a project — a closet, a window-box, a re-reading of a ritual text, a financial review. She experiences leisure as itself a task. Suggested "just relax" by Xander, she will attempt it for approximately twenty minutes before generating a project from within the relaxation (rearranging the magazines she was reading). HIGH.

**GIVEN: A movie night with the group.**
EXPECT: Talks during the film. Asks literal questions of plot mechanics. Cries at unexpected places (background animals in danger, contractual betrayals depicted onscreen) and remains dry-eyed at the romantic climaxes the group cries at. She likes documentaries and heist films — the genres where motivations are explicit. She dislikes art films and psychological thrillers — withheld information reads to her as a contract violation by the author. MODERATE-HIGH.

**GIVEN: A board game.**
EXPECT: She plays to win. She knows the rules better than anyone else at the table within fifteen minutes of opening the box. She is unpleasant in victory — recapitulates the winning move — and worse in loss. The group eventually steers her to cooperative games where her tactical talent serves the table; she enjoys these less but produces fewer hard feelings. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Music.**
EXPECT: She has narrow taste, formed by accident in 1998–1999 from whatever was on car radios. She likes songs with clear narrative content and dislikes ambient or instrumental music. She will, in private, sing — well, in a low alto, in pitch — and is mortified if overheard. The "Once More, with Feeling" event is canonical confirmation she has the physical equipment; the privacy is the inference. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: A pet is proposed.**
EXPECT: Cat — possible, with negotiation. Dog — refused with arguments about logistics. Rabbit — phobic refusal, non-negotiable, distressing to be asked. Fish — accepted, named functionally ("Fish"), well cared for, mourned in proportion when it dies (which is not small). HIGH on the rabbit, MODERATE on the rest.

---

## K. APPEARANCE AND SELF-PRESENTATION

**GIVEN: Subject dresses for a normal workday.**
EXPECT: A small fixed rotation of outfits, color-coordinated, all of which she can put on without thought. Clothing is uniform-as-relief — decision-load reduction. She accessorizes in one fixed way (a particular necklace or watch) that functions as totem. She does not follow fashion; she follows function and the residual aesthetic of having been pretty in 1999 Sunnydale. MODERATE.

**GIVEN: Subject is asked to dress up for a formal event.**
EXPECT: She enjoys this and overprepares. She bought the dress months in advance, has worn it once to practice, and has shoes broken in. The night of, she narrates the cost of each item to the nearest dollar, which is partly pride and partly the only language she has for "I tried." HIGH.

**GIVEN: Hair.**
EXPECT: Self-cut at the ends between professional cuts she budgets for. She fusses with it more than she admits; the visible-aging substrate of her death-anxiety routes through hair more than face. A first grey hair, when it appears, will be an event. SPECULATIVE-MODERATE.

**GIVEN: A camera is pointed at her.**
EXPECT: She poses too soon, holds it too long, smiles with her teeth. She likes photographs because they are permanent records of having existed at a specific moment — she keeps an album, organized chronologically with dates and locations annotated on the back


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

*This section maps the subject's behavior under the conditions where her ordinary regulation fails. The predictions are structured as conditional pairs (GIVEN → EXPECT), arranged by the stratum of threat — physical, relational, ontological — and by escalation tier. Each pair is grounded in observed canonical instances and extrapolated to the granular tells a continuous surveillance record would have captured. The governing thesis: the subject's decompensation is unusually predictable because she has only ever had two scripts for crisis — concretize and count, or regress to the demon role — and the trigger that flips her from the first to the second is narrow, specific, and known.*

---

## 1. The Index Wound and Its Signature

The whole crisis architecture pivots on a single piece of biographical machinery: the Olaf event, c. 880 CE. Every subsequent acute decompensation in the eleven-hundred-year record either replays or actively defends against that event. The wound has four constituent elements, and a stimulus must contain at least two of them to produce relapse-grade behavior:

1. **A trusted male intimate** (not a peer, not a friend — a partner with sexual/marital standing).
2. **Public or witnessed humiliation** — the betrayal must be legible to her social field, not merely interior.
3. **A failure of *terms*** — the breach must violate an explicit or implicit contractual structure she believed she had secured.
4. **Helplessness in the moment** — she must be unable to act on the betrayal at the instant of discovery.

**GIVEN any two of these four elements coincident → EXPECT the Anyanka script to begin loading within hours.** The loading is observable: she will speak D'Hoffryn's name unprompted; she will narrate past vengeances in present tense; she will refer to her human self in the third person ("Anya would…"); she will physically orient toward elevated or northern positions (the canonical summoning posture). This is what was visible in the hour after "Hells Bells."

**GIVEN three of four → EXPECT relapse or relapse-attempt within 72 hours**, irrespective of intervening support. The Scoobies' presence in S6 did not prevent it; only the absence of D'Hoffryn's actual extended hand can.

**GIVEN all four → EXPECT immediate, non-negotiable reversion**, and expect her to perform the reversion with craftsmanship rather than rage — quiet, organized, almost relieved. The relief is the diagnostic. She is going home to a role.

---

## 2. Physical Threat — Combat, Bodily Danger, Acute Pain

The subject's relationship to her own body is anomalous and her threat-response reflects it. For 1,120 years she occupied a body that did not register injury as terminal. The reflexes built in that period have not fully decommissioned.

**GIVEN sudden physical assault on her person → EXPECT a half-second freeze, then competent but flat-affect counter-action.** She does not flinch in the usual sequence; she pauses to verify that the pain signal is real, then responds. Surveillance footage of her in combat across S5–7 (Glory's minions, the Geek Trio's traps, the Bringers, the Turok-Han) shows this pause as a recognizable somatic tic — a quarter-step backward and a glance at the wounded site before engagement.

**GIVEN injury that draws blood → EXPECT verbal narration of the injury in clinical register ("I'm bleeding from the abdomen, this is a lot of blood") and an underestimate of severity by roughly one tier.** She has no calibrated pain scale.

**GIVEN a Slayer-grade threat to her personally in a context where she is not the protector of others → EXPECT flight, openly and without shame.** She has never claimed warrior identity and will not perform one. The "Graduation Day" hospital-exit, the "Becoming" attempted flight, the Bringers-flight in S7 are consistent.

**GIVEN a Slayer-grade threat to a person she has bonded to → EXPECT her to remain in the line of fire past the point of tactical sense.** This is the inversion that killed her. The "Chosen" death is not anomalous; it is the predictable terminus of a person whose only stable identity-anchors are the few humans she still recognizes. Predict the same behavior whenever Xander, Willow, Tara (while alive), Dawn, or Halfrek are at acute risk in her presence.

**GIVEN torture or coercive interrogation → EXPECT high resistance to physical pressure and very low resistance to relational pressure.** She has a millennium of accumulated pain tolerance she has not consciously catalogued. She does not have a millennium of accumulated experience refusing a question framed as *don't you want to belong with us*. An interrogator who threatens her body will get capitalism jokes and accurate counts of how much money she still owes the Magic Box's suppliers. An interrogator who tells her, calmly, that the Scoobies have decided she is not really one of them will get usable intelligence within an hour.

**GIVEN imminent death she sees coming → EXPECT a quip.** This is the late-period integration of humor as affect regulation and it is the defense she dies inside of. The quip will be small, transactional, and slightly off-register. It is not bravery; it is the only voice she has left for occasions that exceed her vocabulary.

---

## 3. Relational Threat — Romantic, Sexual, Domestic

This is the stratum where her vulnerability is highest and her tells are richest.

**GIVEN a sexual partner's gaze lingering on another woman in her presence → EXPECT an immediate verbal challenge phrased as a transaction ("Are you planning to have sex with her instead of me?").** The challenge is not jealousy in the ordinary sense; it is contract enforcement. The flatness of the affect with which she asks it is the marker that the Olaf circuit is being checked, not yet tripped.

**GIVEN evidence — even ambiguous — of partner infidelity → EXPECT a 24–48 hour latency in which she behaves with eerie normalcy, followed by a discrete decision-event.** She does not process betrayal in real time. She files it, completes whatever bounded task is in front of her (close out the day's register, finish the inventory), and reaches a verdict alone. The verdict, once reached, is not appealable. This was the pattern with Olaf (she did not strike in the bedroom; she gathered materials and worked the spell) and it was the pattern after the wedding (she did not return to D'Hoffryn from the chapel; she went home, sat for a measurable interval, and then summoned).

**GIVEN cancellation of a publicly anticipated romantic event** — wedding, party, named anniversary — **→ EXPECT immediate decompensation if she is the cancelled party and a delayed, contractually-framed renegotiation if she is the canceller.** The asymmetry matters. She can break a promise; she cannot survive one being broken on her in front of witnesses.

**GIVEN a partner attempting graceful exit from intimacy** — the gentle conversation, the "I think we should" — **→ EXPECT her to misread the register entirely and respond with one of two scripts: (a) literal acceptance with full and inappropriate transactional accounting of what is now owed back ("you may have the apartment, I want the espresso machine, we had sex 847 times"), or (b) catastrophic interpretation as betrayal proper, with the Anyanka loading sequence beginning before the partner has finished speaking.** Which script she runs is determined by whether the exit is private (script a) or witnessed (script b).

**GIVEN a partner who remains and renegotiates in good faith → EXPECT, over weeks, a slow and visible re-regulation: more sleep, less money-counting, decreased rabbit-mentions, a return to clinical sex-talk as her ordinary affectionate register.** She can be brought down. The protocol is patience and explicit terms.

**GIVEN sexual encounter outside a primary relationship for the purpose of consolation** — the Spike pattern in "Entropy" — **→ EXPECT subdued affect afterward, an unusual quiet, and reduced verbal output for 48 hours.** This is not shame in the human sense; it is the sensation of having used a tool she does not yet know the operating cost of. She does not repeat the behavior often; she catalogues it.

**GIVEN public romantic humiliation specifically — the index-trauma stimulus — → EXPECT all four wound-elements to be present simultaneously and EXPECT reversion. There is no observed counter-protocol.** The only known mitigation is preventing the public dimension: a witnessed-by-strangers betrayal is categorically worse than a private one for this subject by a margin of months of relational rehabilitation. A handler with foresight removes the audience first, not the betrayer.

---

## 4. Social-Role Threat — Status, Inclusion, Category Membership

She has spent her existence trying to know which category she belongs to. Threats to category membership produce a wound second only to romantic betrayal, and arguably feeding it.

**GIVEN explicit exclusion from a Scooby planning meeting → EXPECT a 30–90 minute period of hyper-competent task-doing (re-shelving, accounting, weapon-sharpening) followed by a pointed verbal accounting of her contributions to the group.** The accounting will be numerical and will be correct. It is a request for re-inclusion phrased as a balance sheet.

**GIVEN implicit exclusion — being talked around rather than to — → EXPECT no immediate response and a delayed somatic one: she will report not sleeping, will eat less, will reference death more frequently in incidental conversation.** This is the most common form of harm done to her in the canonical record and the one for which she has the fewest defenses, because she cannot name it as harm.

**GIVEN a Scooby telling her, in conflict, that she is "still a demon" or "not really one of us" → EXPECT a freezing response, prolonged silence, and a markedly raised probability of accepting an outside offer of belonging within 72 hours.** This is the single most efficient destabilizer in her file. It does not require force; it requires one sentence from one trusted speaker.

**GIVEN D'Hoffryn entering her field of awareness — by message, by sigil, by presence — → EXPECT immediate orientation toward him as a parent figure**, irrespective of his most recent treatment of her. The Halfrek killing did not extinguish this; it merely tempered it. Predict that she would, under sufficient relational drought from the human side, take a meeting with him within a calendar quarter, regardless of stated intentions.

**GIVEN being addressed by her demon name, "Anyanka," by anyone other than a Scooby in joking register → EXPECT a measurable shift in posture (lengthening of spine, lowering of chin), a drop in vocal pitch, and increased formality of diction within five exchanges.** The role is sitting under the skin. The name calls it forward physically.

**GIVEN being addressed as "Aud" → EXPECT confusion, then distress, then either tears or aggressive deflection depending on whether women or men are present.** Almost no one alive knows the name. Anyone who deploys it has done research and intends harm; she will sense this correctly.

---

## 5. Temptation — Money, Power, Vengeance, Belonging

Temptation maps directly onto unmet need. The subject's needs are legible.

**GIVEN a financial windfall → EXPECT it to be visibly displayed (counted on table, deposited with ritual), spoken about for days, and not spent.** Money is not for use; it is for proof of placement. She will not be corrupted by money in the ordinary sense — she does not want what money buys, she wants the count.

**GIVEN an offer of magical power that does not require reverting to demon status → EXPECT cautious interest and high probability of decline.** Her relationship to magic is occupational rather than acquisitive; she misses the work, not the power. Distinguish carefully.

**GIVEN an offer to return to vengeance work in any form → EXPECT yes-vulnerability proportional to her current relational deficit.** With a stable Xander and a stable Scooby place, the offer fails. With either gone, it succeeds. The handler's lever is not the offer itself; it is the prior subtraction.

**GIVEN a stranger — particularly a woman — narrating a wrong done to her by a man, in Anya's presence, with no obvious avenue for redress → EXPECT Anya to volunteer, unprompted, a contractual or extralegal solution.** She cannot hear the genre of story without entering the role. This is a continuity tic across both demon and human periods and is independent of her current ontological status. She will offer to "help" in human terms; the offer's escalation depends on the wronged woman's response.

**GIVEN belonging offered without conditions → EXPECT her to refuse it, suspect it, or attempt to renegotiate it into conditions she can understand.** Unconditional acceptance is the one thing she does not know how to receive. A patient adversary or ally could destabilize her simply by giving her what she most wants without asking anything for it; she would invent a contract to make the gift legible, and the invented contract would be exploitable.

---

## 6. Existential Threat — Mortality, Time, Meaning

The death-anxiety stratum operates beneath the others and amplifies them.

**GIVEN proximate death of an acquaintance → EXPECT verbalization disproportionate to her closeness with the deceased, in registers others read as inappropriate.** This is the "we don't know what to do" speech after Joyce. She is not performing grief at the dead person; she is registering, again, the phenomenon. Predict similar speech at any newly-introduced death.

**GIVEN her own aging — a gray hair, a new line, a body ache — → EXPECT a one-to-three day spike in capitalism-talk, sex-frequency-talk, and rabbit-references.** The defenses cluster. She is fortifying her mortality-edge by counting things that can be counted.

**GIVEN being told she has only a defined period to live → EXPECT extraordinarily calm planning behavior.** A definite end is more tolerable to her than an indefinite one; she can run the count. Surveillance would show her completing tasks in order, settling accounts, and writing instructions. She would not panic.

**GIVEN being told she is functionally immortal again → EXPECT a complex distress response with no good script, including possible reversion attempt for the relief of being back in a known temporal frame.** The handler should not assume immortality is a gift to her; it is a category she escaped at extraordinary cost.

**GIVEN an apocalypse with realistic probability of completion → EXPECT her to be functionally the most useful Scooby for logistics and the most fragile one for morale.** She has seen apocalypses fail. She knows the work. She also knows, more clearly than the others, what dying as a human will cost her — because she only recently got the human part back.

---

## 7. The Decompensation Ladder (Operational Summary)

Predict in this sequence; intervene early.

- **Tier 0 — Baseline regulated.** Money-counting at ordinary rate; clinical but warm sex-talk with partner; occasional rabbit-mention treated as joke by group; humor present.
- **Tier 1 — Mild stress.** Money-counting frequency doubles; capitalism remarks lengthen; sex-talk becomes more frequency-oriented and less affectionate; pragmatic-language slips increase (more inappropriate volume, more wrong-register questions). *Intervention: bounded task, private validation of contribution.*
- **Tier 2 — Moderate stress.** Somatic complaints (headache, stomach, sleep); fear-of-death verbalizations enter ordinary conversation; rabbit-references increase and lose their joking frame; she begins to ask, in various phrasings, whether she is doing this right. *Intervention: explicit reassurance of category membership, ideally from Xander in early period or from Buffy/Willow in late period; physical presence over verbal content.*
- **Tier 3 — Acute stress.** Dissociative competence — she becomes flat, efficient, and verbally economical; she stops asking about her place; she begins referring to herself in third person or by old names; she orients spatially toward elevation and north. *Intervention narrow: someone she trusts must physically interrupt the trajectory and name what is happening. Verbal reassurance alone fails at this tier.*
- **Tier 4 — Decompensation.** Reversion script loads; she speaks D'Hoffryn's name or sigil; she requests, or accepts, the return of the role. *Intervention possible only if the role-offer is withdrawn from her side of the threshold; once accepted, irreversible without external rupture.*

The ladder is unusually slow and unusually legible. A continuous-presence observer could call each tier in advance from the verbal and postural tells alone. The reason her death is the only acute-tier outcome the Scoobies never prevented is that it occurred in a context where the threat was external and shared, the wound-elements were absent, and the script that loaded was not the demon-script but the late-period quip-and-stand-with-them script — which is not, in the technical sense, decompensation at all. It is the only script she ever wrote herself.

---

## 8. The Wound, Restated

Predictive accuracy collapses to one sentence: **she will break in exactly the place she was first broken, in exactly the way, by exactly the stimulus, and she will reach for exactly the tool that was put in her hand the first time she broke.** Eleven hundred years did not move the fracture line. Four years of human relearning narrowed it, taught her to feel it coming, and gave her — at the end — one new option that was not vengeance and not flight: to stand somewhere with someone and say so out loud. That option is fragile, late-acquired, and was, at the moment of her death, not yet fully consolidated. Any model of her crisis behavior that does not treat the new option as both real and provisional will misread her at the decisive moment in either direction — overestimating her resilience to the old trigger, or underestimating the genuine, hard-won capacity she had begun to build to choose differently.


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM

*Subject: "Anya" / Anyanka / Aud. Compiled for protective use — i.e. the inverse purpose for which such a compendium is normally written. The entries below are framed as: stimulus → predicted response → operational use (to reach, calm, persuade, provoke, predict, destabilize). Where a lever cuts both ways — usable to harm and to help — both faces are documented. The handler who would protect this subject must know the same things the handler who would break her would know.*

---

## 1. THE MASTER VULNERABILITY: CATEGORY-HOMELESSNESS

Everything below is a special case of one structural fact: the subject has no continuous interior self and therefore depends on an external category — "villager," "vengeance demon," "Xander's girlfriend," "Scooby," "shopkeeper" — to know what she is from one hour to the next. This is the master lever. To threaten her category-belonging is to threaten the entire scaffolding on which her behavior is organized.

**Operational signature.** When category is secure, she is high-functioning, competent, and verbally inappropriate-but-stable. When category is in doubt, she escalates through the predictable ladder (see §9): chatter → somatic complaint → flat dissociative competence → regression to prior identity (demon).

**To reach her:** name her category for her, plainly. "You are one of us." "You are running this store." "You are the bride." She metabolizes literal placement faster than reassurance. Vague comfort ("you'll be fine") slides off; sentence-form designation lands.

**To destabilize her:** say, in any register, *you don't really belong here.* Variants include "you're not one of us," "you'll always be a demon," "you don't understand humans," "we tolerate you." Any of these reproduce the deepest wound and will trigger the escalation ladder within minutes.

**Protective use:** keep her *placed* during transitions. The dangerous windows in her record are precisely the unplaced moments — newly mortal in S3, jilted in S6, depowered again in S7. A protector schedules her into named roles during such windows.

---

## 2. THE INDEX-TRAUMA REPLAY: ROMANTIC PUBLIC HUMILIATION

The original trauma (Olaf) was a private infidelity. The replay (Xander) was a public jilting. The subject has now been imprinted twice that romantic betrayal arrives *with witnesses*. The two events fused: in her affect after "Hells Bells," Xander's leaving is processed as if it always had been Olaf, and Olaf as if he always had been Xander.

**Provocation signature.** Any staged scenario in which she is romantically refused in front of others will produce the precise relapse template: no grief phase, immediate hardening, immediate seeking-out of a vengeance frame (D'Hoffryn, contract, target). She does not cry first. She becomes very still, then very efficient.

**Prediction.** If a romantic partner under her witness is unfaithful or publicly rejects her, the latency to vengeance ideation is hours, not days. The latency to vengeance *enactment* is gated only by whether a power-source is available.

**To calm her in the immediate aftermath:** do not argue the merits of the abandoner. She is not litigating fairness; she is drowning in re-experienced category-loss (she was about to become "wife"). Place her in the next available category instead — "you are still working tomorrow," "you are still in this house," "you are still ours." Halfrek's mistake in "Hells Bells" was to offer her the *old* category (demon) when no current one was available; a protector offers a current one.

**To destabilize her:** stage or even merely insinuate a betrayal. She has poor discrimination between rumor and event in this domain; the suggestion that Xander, or any later attachment-figure, has been unfaithful will register at near full intensity. This is one of the cleanest manipulation routes into her behavior and must be defended against by handlers controlling her information environment.

---

## 3. LEPORIPHOBIA AND ITS METONYMS

The rabbit phobia is real, specific, and load-bearing. It is the only intact piece of pre-trauma Aud still resident in her nervous system, and as such it functions as a tuning fork for the entire pre-Olaf self.

**Direct stimulus.** Live rabbit, image of rabbit, prolonged verbal description of rabbits, especially in numbers ("bunnies, bunnies, it must be bunnies"). Response: phobic — pupillary, vocal pitch up, attention narrowing, motor agitation, in extremis a fight-or-flight pivot away from current task.

**Metonymic stimulus.** Anything that reactivates the Aud era without the protective framing of "long ago." Soft, named, owned animals; gift-giving to villagers; agrarian Norse imagery; *being laughed at for affection.* The last is the operative metonym and the one most often inadvertently triggered by the Scoobies. When she offers a gift or a sentiment and is met with collective amusement, she is briefly in the Aud village again. Her recovery is fast but the micro-flinch is observable.

**To calm:** remove the rabbit, then *do not discuss it.* She does not want the phobia interpreted. She wants the stimulus gone and the conversation moved on. Reassurance phrased as analysis ("you know they can't hurt you") prolongs the episode.

**To provoke:** the phobia is so well-known among intimates that weaponizing it would be an act of explicit cruelty and would be read as such by the entire Scooby network; it is therefore self-limiting as an adversarial lever within that network. From outside the network, it is a clean panic-induction tool.

**Protective use:** her phobia is also her one reliable *somatic anchor to her own history.* A clinician (or a protector functioning as one) could, with consent and over years, use it as the keyhole through which the pre-trauma self is gradually accessed.

---

## 4. MORTALITY AND TIME

She has subjective experience of immortality and now lives in a body with a counter on it. The asymmetry produces a chronic, low-grade existential vertigo that flares to acute panic on any death-adjacent stimulus.

**Triggers, in approximate order of severity.**
- Death of someone she has met (Joyce → the "Body" speech; Tara; later, the prospect of Buffy's death).
- Visible aging in herself or others (grey hairs, wrinkles — verbalized obsessively).
- Markers of biological time (birthdays, anniversaries, calendars; she cannot tolerate the imagery of a clock running down without comment).
- Abstract discussion of mortality without a task attached.

**Response.** She does not dissociate from these; she over-attends. Her famous monologue at Joyce's death is the diagnostic moment: she narrates the phenomenon of death because she is encountering it as phenomenon, with no socialized script for the encounter. Her affect is bewildered, not stoic and not grieving in the recognizable shape.

**To calm:** attach the mortality datum to a task. She regulates by doing. "Yes, she's gone. Help me with the arrangements." This is not avoidance; it is the only regulation route her nervous system has been given.

**To persuade through this lever:** appeals framed as *finite-time prioritization* land disproportionately. "If you only had ten years left, would you spend them on this?" reaches her where moralistic framing does not. She will calculate, and she will act on the calculation.

**To destabilize:** monologue at her, slowly, about the inevitability of her own death and the brevity of her remaining years. She has no defense against this delivered in calm register; she will spiral within one conversation.

---

## 5. THE MONEY CHANNEL

Money is the substitute mastery domain — a bounded, countable, contractually-governed system in which her cognitive profile (high working memory, concretization, low pragmatic-inference, love of explicit rules) confers genuine advantage. It is also a transparent affect-regulator: when she is anxious, she counts.

**Operational uses.**

*To calm.* Hand her a ledger, a cash drawer, an inventory, or a budgeting problem. The behavior pattern collapses to focused, low-affect competence within minutes. This is the single most reliable de-escalation tool in the file. The Magic Box during business hours is her therapeutic environment.

*To persuade.* Frame the request as a transaction with stated terms and stated payoff. "I need X. In return, you get Y." She will respond to this framing even when the actual stakes are emotional, because her schema for trust is contractual. The corollary: vague favors asked "as a friend" without terms make her suspicious or anxious. She does not trust unstated debt.

*To predict.* Sudden, intense money-talk is a stress tell, not a value statement. When she escalates her capitalist register in the absence of business stress, *something else is wrong.* A handler tracking her affect should chart her money-chatter rate as a leading indicator.

*To destabilize.* Financial loss reaches her with extraordinary speed and depth — disproportionately to the actual dollar value. Theft, debt, audit, business failure: any of these will fold into her general category-anxiety because money is what she has been counting in lieu of an interior. Threats to the Magic Box are threats to her self.

---

## 6. THE D'HOFFRYN LEVER

The most dangerous single relationship in her file. D'Hoffryn is the figure who placed her in a category at her worst moment, gave her a thousand-year vocation, and remains for her — past his own betrayal of her — the closest thing to a parental imago she possesses. The pull is not nostalgic; it is structural. He is the standing offer of *a category to fall back into.*

**Predicted behavior.** Under sufficient stress (humiliation, abandonment, depowerment, terminal category-doubt), she will move toward D'Hoffryn's offer. The latency in "Hells Bells" was under twenty-four hours. The pull is automatic and pre-cognitive; she does not deliberate.

**To protect her:** the lever is *closed* by ensuring there is always an alternative, named, currently-occupied category. When she had the store and the Scooby seat, the demon offer had no opening. When she had just lost both Xander and the imminent role of wife, the offer had a clean channel. Her protectors must understand that maintaining her categorical placement is, operationally, *suicide prevention* in a slow form.

**To destabilize her:** route an offer of return through any plausible Arashmaharr-adjacent figure. She will not necessarily accept, but she will lose days of equilibrium to the consideration.

**Latent leverage.** Her loyalty to D'Hoffryn persists past Halfrek's death. This is the single most dangerous datum in the file for adversarial exploitation. If a hostile party could credibly act as D'Hoffryn or transmit a D'Hoffryn-shaped instruction, her compliance window is non-zero even after "Selfless."

---

## 7. PEER-FEMALE ATTACHMENTS AS BOTH ANCHOR AND BLADE

Her stable peer attachments are predominantly with women — Tara, Willow, Halfrek, and, after long warming, Buffy. With women she shows reduced verbal inappropriateness, longer conversational latency (i.e. she listens), and the only spontaneous physical affection in the record outside of sexual contexts.

**As anchor.** A female peer present during a destabilization shortens the escalation ladder. Tara's effect on her in S5–6 is particularly marked: in Tara's presence the somatic-complaint register drops and the literalism softens toward sincerity. This is replicable. A protector who needs her grounded for a difficult conversation places a trusted woman in the room.

**As blade.** Halfrek's death is the proof-of-concept that the most exquisite punishment available to anyone wishing to harm this subject is *harm to a peer-female attachment.* D'Hoffryn understood this with clinical precision. The lesson generalizes: threats to Willow, Tara (already realized, contributed to her late subdued affect), Buffy, or any future female intimate will reach her more deeply than threats to Xander or to herself. Her romantic attachments are loud and known; her peer-female attachments are quiet and load-bearing, and an adversary attending to the file would target the latter.

**Protective implication.** The women in her circle must be informed that they are also her stabilization infrastructure, and that their safety is operationally linked to hers.

---

## 8. THE LITERALISM-AND-CONTRACT INTERFACE

Her autistic-broad-phenotype cognitive profile produces a consistent and exploitable interface. She takes language at face value, she honors explicit terms, and she resents implicit terms imposed retroactively.

**To reach her:** speak in plain declaratives. State the request. State the reason. State the expected outcome. Do not hint, do not test, do not signal. She does not run the inference layer that hinting requires, and she experiences hinting as either nonsense or hostility.

**To persuade her:** offer a contract, even an informal one. "If you do X, I will do Y, and we will both know we did this." She finds the explicitness *relieving,* not insulting. Most humans find contractual framing of personal favors cold; she finds it the only comprehensible form of trust.

**To destabilize her:** change terms after agreement, or impose unstated norms ("you should have known that wasn't appropriate"). The combination of (a) violated explicit rule and (b) implication that she should have inferred a hidden rule is, in her processing, the texture of every social failure she has ever had. It produces a characteristic shamed-then-defensive response: brief silence, then verbal over-correction, then withdrawal.

**Adversarial misuse.** A bad-faith negotiator can extract surprising concessions from her by front-loading transparency ("here are my terms, fully disclosed") and then later invoking unstated implications. She is slow to detect this pattern because her template assumes parties operate as she does.

---

## 9. THE ESCALATION LADDER (DIAGNOSTIC)

For handlers: the subject's distress externalizes on a stable, predictable ladder. Each rung has observable verbal and somatic markers and a known intervention.

**Rung 1 — Baseline elevation.** Increased rate of capitalist or sexual chatter. Money-counting in absence of business need. Mildly inappropriate self-disclosure to nearby parties. *Intervention:* assign a bounded task. Ask about inventory, finances, or ritual mechanics. Frequently resolves within the conversation.

**Rung 2 — Somatization.** Verbal cataloguing of body states ("my head hurts, my stomach feels strange, my hands are cold"). Increased rabbit references, often deflected through humor by listeners but signaling real distress. *Intervention:* physical regulation — food, water, sitting down, weight in hands. Verbal acknowledgment of the body datum without interpretation ("you're hungry; eat this"). Do not analyze.

**Rung 3 — Mortality fixation.** Spontaneous discussion of death, aging, or the brevity of life, often initiated as if mid-thought. The hallmark is that she does not seem to know why she is bringing it up. *Intervention:* attach to task. Move her physically. Co-presence of a trusted female peer is highly effective at this rung; isolation worsens it rapidly.

**Rung 4 — Dissociative competence.** Affect flattens. Speech becomes efficient and oddly polite. She executes tasks with unusual precision and zero emotional coloring. This rung is often misread as her having "calmed down" — it is not calm; it is the last station before regression. *Intervention:* slow her down, force eye contact, get her into the presence of an attachment figure, do not let her leave alone. This is the operationally critical rung; missing it is how she ends up at D'Hoffryn's door.

**Rung 5 — Regression.** Active movement toward pre-formed institutional identity. Verbal markers: speaking of herself in role-prescribed third person ("Anyanka would…"), invoking the language of contracts and wishes, asking about absent demon contacts. *Intervention:* at this point, persuasion is low-probability. Physical proximity of multiple attachment figures, removal from solitary access to ritual implements, and direct naming of her current category ("you are Anya. You are here. You are with us.") are the available tools.

---

## 10. THE GUILT AND ATONEMENT CHANNEL

Unlike a true antisocial, she has access to guilt and has demonstrated the capacity for moral revision. This is both a protective resource and a precise lever for inducing self-destruction.

**Reach.** Direct appeal to her record as harm-doer will land. She is not in denial about the body count. What she lacks is a calibrated sense of *proportional* atonement, which means that an appeal of this form must be paired with a specifically scaled response, or she will scale it to her own death (as she did with Buffy in "Selfless").

**Persuade.** Frame protective action as restitution. "Helping these strangers is how someone with your history pays the debt." She will accept this framing and act on it sustainably. The Scoobies stumbled onto this lever; a clinician would use it deliberately.

**Provoke / destabilize.** A skilled adversary could collapse her by simply walking her through her own century-by-century record without buffer. She has no internal defense against an accurate accounting of her past delivered in cool register. The "Selfless" pattern would repeat: she would request her own death.
