**Protective rule.** Atonement work with this subject must be *bounded* — discrete tasks, completed and acknowledged. Open-ended atonement is, for her, indistinguishable from a death sentence served in installments.

---

## 11. THE SEXUAL DOMAIN

Sex is, for her, a bodily vocabulary in which the words are mostly present and the music mostly absent. Three operational facts.

First, she discusses sex in clinical, frequency-oriented terms; this is not an invitation to discuss her sex life in turn. The register is defensive, not promiscuous. Reading it as flirtation, as outsiders sometimes do, produces a characteristic Anya response — bewildered or sharply boundaried — and erodes trust.

Second, sex is one of her few reliable affect-regulation routes inside an established attachment. With Xander it functioned as connection-making. The Spike encounter in "Entropy" was a textbook mutual-consolation event between two people whose attachments had just failed identically; reading it as appetite misses the regulation function.

Third, the somatic novelty of human sexual response — after a millennium without it — produces a persistent low-grade absorption in the topic that handlers and friends often misread as exhibitionism. She is, in fact, still narrating sensations she has not yet learned to filter (see §1 of the medical record).

**Operational use.** Privacy is the relevant lever; she does not lie about sex but she does respond to having it *named* by others as an attack on her dignity. Protective handlers ensure her sexual disclosures are not weaponized in social settings — a near-constant minor risk in the Scooby network.

---

## 12. PRESSURE-POINT MATRIX (CONSOLIDATED)

For rapid reference. *Higher numbers = deeper reach.*

| Lever | Reach (1–5) | Latency | Calm-use available? | Destabilize-use risk |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Threat to category-belonging | 5 | minutes | No (must be prevented) | Catastrophic |
| Romantic public humiliation | 5 | hours | No | Catastrophic |
| Harm to peer-female attachment | 5 | immediate | No | Catastrophic |
| D'Hoffryn-channel offer | 5 | hours–days | No | Catastrophic |
| Forced accounting of vengeance record | 4 | within conversation | Yes, if bounded | High |
| Mortality monologue | 4 | within conversation | Yes, if task-attached | High |
| Live rabbit / metonym | 4 | seconds | No | High (but socially self-limiting) |
| Implicit-rule violation accusation | 3 | minutes | No | Moderate–high |
| Financial loss / theft | 3 | minutes | Partial (task-attach) | Moderate |
| Sexual disclosure weaponized publicly | 3 | minutes | No | Moderate |
| Bounded task / ledger | — | minutes | YES (primary) | — |
| Named current category | — | minutes | YES (primary) | — |
| Female-peer co-presence | — | minutes | YES (primary) | — |
| Plain declarative contract speech | — | per-conversation | YES (primary) | — |

---

## 13. ADVERSARIAL THREAT MODEL (BRIEF)

A hostile actor with access to this file would target, in order: (1) her current category-placement, by removing her from the Magic Box or the Scooby seat; (2) her romantic attachment, by staging or implying betrayal; (3) her female peers, physically; (4) her D'Hoffryn channel, by opening it; (5) her vengeance record, by reciting it. The combination of any two of these within seventy-two hours has, on the historical record, produced regression. The combination of three has produced a willingness to die.

A protective actor with access to the same file inverts the list: maintain category, defend the attachment, guard the peers, close the D'Hoffryn channel by saturating its slot, and bound the atonement work so that her capacity for guilt does not metabolize itself into self-execution.

---

## 14. THE ONE LEVER SHE CANNOT BE PROTECTED FROM

It must be stated plainly. The subject's deepest vulnerability is also the source of her late-period growth: she will, in the end, choose to stand with the people she has chosen, and she will not survive the choice if it requires it of her. Her death in "Chosen" was not coerced and was not engineered by an adversary. It was the natural endpoint of a self that, having finally been built, was willing to be spent. No protective regime can fully foreclose this — and a protective regime that did foreclose it would have eliminated the very integration that made her, at last, a person rather than a role. The compendium of leverage ends, as her record does, at the edge of a vulnerability that is indistinguishable from a virtue.


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# DOSSIER SECTION 6 — STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE

*The asset ledger. The previous sections have catalogued damage; this one catalogues what the subject has, what works, and why it has kept working across ontological discontinuities that would erase most operating systems. The unifying observation: this subject's strengths are unusually durable because almost all of them survived a category-change of self. Capacities that persist across the Aud → Anyanka → Anya → Anyanka-redux → Anya-final transitions are, by definition, load-bearing. Many of them do.*

---

## 6.1 COGNITIVE ASSETS

**Working memory and retentive capacity, exceptional.** The subject retains operational detail across timescales most human nervous systems cannot. She quotes vengeance contracts from the twelfth century with the casual specificity of someone citing last week's invoice; she recalls the Russian peasant action of 1905 in granular detail ("Selfless" flashbacks corroborate); she remembers the Mason-Dixon engagement well enough to use it as conversational shorthand. In Magic Box bookkeeping she reportedly closes registers without error and re-counts cash for pleasure rather than necessity. The same capacity underlies her ritual competence: she retains the verbal forms, gestural sequences, and ingredient lists of demonic ceremony she has not practiced in years (the Sweet summoning in "Once More, with Feeling" — performed offhandedly, from a fragment she half-remembered from the back of a book). This is a memory architecture optimized for discrete units: numbers, names, procedures, contractual clauses.

**Concrete cognition as instrument.** The literalism that is a social liability is a procedural asset. She does not lose the thread of a complex transaction in metaphor; she does not soften a balance sheet; she does not introduce wishful thinking into a tactical assessment. When in "Graduation Day" she is one of the few characters to argue the Scoobies should *leave town*, she is correct on the merits and is dismissed because her register is wrong, not because her reasoning is. This pattern recurs: she is frequently right and frequently disregarded for being right rudely.

**Rapid mastery of bounded domains.** Across four years of human time she becomes: a competent retail bookkeeper, a serviceable ritualist, a passable combatant (sword work in "End of Days" and "Chosen"), a fluent navigator of American consumer culture, and — by her last season — a working member of an apocalypse-prevention cell. The learning curve is steep when the domain has rules. She cannot learn unspoken etiquette; she can learn double-entry bookkeeping in what reads as a weekend.

**Pattern recognition across very long baselines.** Eleven hundred years of fieldwork in human cruelty has produced in her something like an epidemiologist's eye for the small recurring forms of betrayal, lying, and self-deception. She reads new acquaintances quickly and rarely wrongly on the question of *what they want*. Her error band is in what people *mean*, not in what they want; the want-detector is excellent and has saved the group's planning more than once.

**Polylingual / cross-cultural fluency.** She has lived through and operated in multiple language environments — Old Norse (her natal), various medieval European vernaculars implied by her case-load geography, Russian (the 1905 work), and contemporary American English. Her demon-court argot (the references to D'Hoffryn's protocols, the casual nomenclature of the lower planes) constitutes a working professional vocabulary in a register no other Scooby commands. This is intelligence currency.

---

## 6.2 OCCUPATIONAL & MATERIAL ASSETS

**Commercial competence at the Magic Box.** Under her management the shop converts from Giles's affectionate hobbyist operation into a going concern. She reorganizes inventory, installs hard accounting practice, prices to margin, and — critically — keeps the books clean enough that Giles, on departure, can sign the business over to her without due-diligence anxiety. This is a non-trivial transfer of trust and a non-trivial demonstration of legitimate enterprise. The shop is also, for two seasons, the group's de facto headquarters; she is therefore not just earning, she is providing the operational real estate.

**Capital orientation as a survival heuristic.** Her money-counting reads comically but is structurally serious: a person with no family, no documents, no credit history, and a body she did not grow up in has correctly identified liquid capital as the variable most under her control. The hoarding behavior is not greed; it is a one-woman sovereign reserve against the next ontological surprise. By the time of her death she has, by implication, accumulated more discretionary cash than any other member of the cell.

**Domestic competence, late-acquired.** Her apartment with Xander is, by reports embedded in the visual record, kept; she cooks (badly but reliably); she plans the wedding to the level of detail of a small military operation. The capacity to construct and maintain a household — a capacity she had no developmental scaffolding for — is achieved in roughly three years from a standing start.

**Occult inventory and contacts.** She retains, post-de-powering, both the catalog of demonic species and the address book of demonic society. She knows whom to ask, what coin they accept, what insults to avoid. She is the cell's living reference work on the supernatural economy.

---

## 6.3 PHYSICAL & SOMATIC ASSETS

**Pain tolerance and trauma threshold, residually elevated.** A millennium in a body that healed instantly has left her with what reads as a recalibrated wince-response. She does not flinch at injury sights that affect others; she walks through demon corpses with bookkeeper composure; her startle-response to violence is lower than baseline civilian. This is partly desensitization, partly the simple fact that she has seen worse.

**Combat baseline, modest but real.** She does not have Slayer-grade capacity, but she is not the group's weakest combatant. By S7 she is in the field rotation, takes a sword in "End of Days" with adequate form, and dies *fighting* — not fleeing, not paralyzed. The capacity is recent and was learned; it counts.

**Sleep, appetite, libido — all functional.** No reported insomnia in the record despite the trauma load. Eats reliably. Sexually responsive and communicative. The somatic chassis, for a body she did not grow up in, is being run well.

**Phobia containment.** The leporiphobia is severe but compartmentalized: it does not generalize, does not impair occupational function, does not produce avoidance of broader categories (forests, pet stores, children with stuffed animals). One specific stimulus, intense response, otherwise contained. This is the *good* form a specific phobia can take.

---

## 6.4 INTERPERSONAL & RELATIONAL ASSETS

**Loyalty, once formed, near-absolute.** The list of people she does not abandon, even under provocation: Xander (through the relationship, through the jilting, through his subsequent involvement with others; she returns to the cell anyway); Halfrek (she dies still mourning her); Giles (she runs his shop honestly); Buffy (she stands in the line in "Chosen" though she has the least personal stake of anyone present); Tara, Dawn, Willow (she remains in the household after every quarrel). Her attachment circuit is slow to engage and almost impossible to disengage. In a security context this is the most valuable single trait a subject can have.

**Honesty as default.** She lies poorly and rarely. The Aud-era literalism plus the Anyanka-era contractualism produced a person whose first instinct is disclosure even when disclosure costs her. She tells Xander things he does not want to hear; she tells Buffy things Buffy does not want to hear; she tells customers prices and side-effects with full transparency. As an intelligence asset this means her reports can be taken at face value. As a personal asset it means her friendships are not transactional in the sense she pretends — there is no hidden ledger.

**Friendship capacity with women, robust and underutilized.** She is markedly more at ease with Tara, Willow, Dawn, Joyce, and Halfrek than with men. With Tara in particular there is a documented pattern of mutual quiet competence — they work together without performance. The Halfrek bond survives a millennium of demonic professional life and the species transition. This is a relational template that *works* and that, had she lived, would have generalized.

**Capacity for genuine intimacy, late-developing but real.** The Xander relationship, despite its catastrophic end, demonstrates that she could love, could be loved, could share a bed and a kitchen and a business plan with another adult, could fight and reconcile, could imagine a future. The capacity was achieved from a developmental baseline of zero. That she could build it at all is the strongest single prognostic asset in the file.

**Reads people accurately for motive.** See §6.1. She is frequently the first in the room to identify what someone actually wants. The group consistently underweights her assessments and consistently regrets it.

---

## 6.5 MORAL & CHARACTEROLOGICAL ASSETS

**Capacity for moral revision under evidence.** Vanishingly rare in any subject and exceptionally rare in a subject with eleven hundred years of investment in a prior moral framework. She does not merely regret particular acts; she revises the framework. "Selfless" documents the revision in real time: presented with the consequences of restored vengeance work, she does not rationalize, does not minimize, does not split off the new self from the old. She asks for her own death. The request is refused, and she spends the remaining year operationalizing the revision rather than performing it.

**Capacity for guilt without collapse.** She bears the weight of the historical body count without dissociating from it (late period) and without using it as a license for further nihilism. The guilt is processed into changed behavior. This is the textbook good outcome of guilt-affect; most subjects either disown the act or disintegrate under it. She does neither.

**Willingness to die for the cell.** Demonstrated in "Selfless" (verbal), "End of Days" (operational), and "Chosen" (executed). The willingness is not theatrical — she does not seek martyrdom, does not narrate it, does not extract recognition for it. She dies mid-quip, defending a stranger (Andrew). This is the form courage takes when it is real.

**Absence of vindictiveness in late period.** A woman whose vocation was vengeance for a thousand years ends her life having forgiven, in operational terms, the man who jilted her at the altar. She does not curse Xander. She does not curse the woman who replaces her in his life. She does not curse Buffy for not letting her die when she asked. The vengeance reflex, given the index trauma, was *available* and was *not used*. The restraint is the most underrated single fact in her file.

---

## 6.6 RESILIENCE FACTORS

**Track record of surviving ontological rupture.** She has survived: total loss of human community (c. 880), total loss of demonic power (1199, briefly; 1998, permanently), total loss of romantic partner (twice — Olaf, Xander), total loss of professional identity (twice — at each de-powering), and the death of her closest peer (Halfrek). Each rupture would, in most subjects, be terminal to functioning. She metabolizes each and continues to operate. The metabolization is sometimes ugly (the Anyanka-redux relapse) but it is never paralysis. The recovery time, era by era, *decreases*: a millennium to recover from Olaf, a year and change to recover from Xander.

**Externalized identity scaffolding.** Paradoxically, the unstable self-concept is a resilience factor: she does not have a brittle interior to shatter, and she can rebuild a working self from external roles relatively quickly. The same plasticity that makes her vulnerable to recruitment by D'Hoffryn makes her recruitable by the Scoobies; the same capacity to inhabit "vengeance demon" allows her to inhabit "shopkeeper," "fiancée," "field operative." The roles do real work for her, and she does real work in them.

**Humor, late-integrated.** The dying quip is not incidental. The development of humor as an affect-regulation channel across S5–S7 represents the on-coming-online of a regulator she did not previously possess. Once integrated, it functions reliably: she can crack a joke in genuine fear, in genuine grief, in the middle of a wedding rehearsal that is going badly. The channel is narrow but it works.

**Capacity for solitude.** She can be alone. The post-wedding sequences and the post-"Selfless" period both show her tolerating extended solitude without acting out — a baseline she did not possess earlier. The capacity to sit with the self, even an unstable self, is real by the end.

**Pragmatism under existential pressure.** When the world is ending — literally, repeatedly — she is one of the calmer voices in the room. "Graduation Day," "The Gift," "Chosen." Her default in apocalyptic conditions is logistical: what do we need, what do we have, what is the plan. This is the asset of a person who has watched many worlds end and knows that the practical questions are the only ones that scale.

**No substance dependency.** One documented bender. No pattern. The affect-regulation, even at its worst, did not route through chemistry.

**No identity-laundering through the past.** She does not, after re-mortalization, present herself as a victim of D'Hoffryn or as a wronged innocent. She owns the eleven hundred years. The refusal to launder is itself a resilience factor: it leaves nothing for adversaries to threaten her with that she has not already disclosed.

---

## 6.7 INSTITUTIONAL & NETWORK ASSETS

**Membership in the Scooby cell, end-state.** By the time of her death she is a full operational member of the most effective supernatural-response unit on the West Coast. She holds the institutional knowledge of the supply chain (Magic Box inventory, demonic vendor list), of the financial back-end, and of the demonic-political context.

**Standing residual access to D'Hoffryn's court.** Even after the rupture at "Selfless," she retains nomenclature, protocols, and a known face in that society. This is a back-channel asset of significant intelligence value.

**Friendship with Halfrek as a now-foreclosed but formative asset.** While alive, Halfrek was a peer who knew both halves of the subject's existence and accepted both. The relationship demonstrated that integration of the two selves was *possible at least for one other being*. The proof-of-concept survives the friend.

**Implicit standing with Giles.** He hands her a business. He does not hand businesses to people lightly.

---

## 6.8 META-ASSET: THE TRAJECTORY ITSELF

The single most important entry in this ledger is not a capability but a vector. The behavioral record across the final eighteen months shows monotone improvement on nearly every axis that matters: affect regulation up, empathic accuracy up, moral integration up, attachment stability up, somatic ownership up, vindictiveness down, dissociative episodes down, identity-rigidity down. The slope is not steep but it is consistent and it is in the right direction across multiple independent measures. A subject whose trajectory is improving across that many axes simultaneously, after that severe a baseline, in that compressed a window, possesses the most valuable asset a damaged person can possess: *evidence, drawn from her own conduct, that she can change*. She had it. She used it. She died with it in hand.

The clinical picture remains, as the prior section concluded, grim. The asset picture is something else: a woman who, given four years and a kitchen and a few people who did not leave, built more functioning self than most subjects build in a lifetime of better circumstances. The file should be read with both pictures held at once. They are both true. The assets are the reason the prognosis was, in fact, hopeful.


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION

*Subject "Anya." How she breaks — the ladder, the tells, the terminal states, and the conditions that load the gun.*

---

## 1. The Architecture of Her Failure

Before mapping the rungs, the shape of the staircase itself must be specified, because the subject's decompensation is unusually legible — more legible, in fact, than her ordinary functioning.

Three structural features govern how she collapses.

**First: she externalizes before she destabilizes.** Most of the subjects in this file class hold distress internally for a period before it surfaces. Anya does not. She has no developed interior holding-space; what she feels, she says, and what she says she says quickly, in the first available register (money, sex, body, death). This means her decompensation is *audible from the first rung* to anyone who knows the verbal markers — which most of her cohort do not, because the markers sound like baseline eccentricity. Her tells are camouflaged by her ordinary speech.

**Second: she has only two terminal states, and they are categorical.** She does not fragment, drift, derealize for years, or chronically self-harm. She either holds together as Anya, or she becomes Anyanka again. There is no third option in her repertoire — no transitional or compromise self. When the human structure fails, the demon structure is the only other one that has ever organized her, and it is sitting waiting at D'Hoffryn's court, fully institutionalized, with a job description, a costume, and a chain of command. Decompensation is therefore not a slide; it is a *switch*, with a long approach and a sudden flip.

**Third: every catastrophic collapse in her record is precipitated by the same class of event — public romantic humiliation by a man she trusted — and the response is identical across a thousand years.** Olaf (c. 880 CE) and Xander ("Hells Bells," 2002) produce structurally indistinguishable behavior: no grief period, no negotiation, no attempt at reconciliation; immediate withdrawal of personhood and immediate weaponization. The reproducibility is forensic-grade. Whatever this is, it is not a reaction; it is a circuit.

---

## 2. The Escalation Ladder

The ladder has six rungs, ordered by intensity. Rungs 1–3 are common and reversible. Rung 4 is the inflection point. Rungs 5 and 6 are catastrophic.

### Rung 1 — Mild Stress: Verbal Inflation

The earliest tell, present on any ordinary bad day, is **a measurable increase in the rate and inappropriateness of her capitalist, sexual, or somatic chatter.** She counts the till when she is not anxious; she counts it three times when she is. She mentions orgasms when relaxed; she narrates frequency and mechanics when she is not. Witness reports across S4–S6 are consistent: the more Anya talks about money, sex, or her body, the less she is talking about whatever is actually pressing on her.

Related markers at this rung: more frequent literal-interpretation errors (she takes idioms straight when her bandwidth is reduced); a slight uptick in references to rabbits, often pre-emptive ("there better not be any bunnies"); minor task-perseveration (recounting inventory, realphabetizing the spell components shelf). Sleep and appetite are not yet disturbed. She is still available to others.

**Reversibility:** total. A direct, concrete piece of attention — Xander asking her a specific question, Tara sitting next to her quietly, a customer who needs help — resolves the state within minutes.

### Rung 2 — Moderate Stress: Somatic and Mortality Verbalization

When mild stress is not relieved or is compounded, the chatter shifts categories. She moves from money/sex to **body and death.** This is the diagnostic transition. She begins to narrate sensations ("my stomach feels weird," "do humans get this kind of headache?"), to reference Joyce's death or Buffy's death unprompted, to ask aging questions ("how old do I look?", "how long do humans live in this part of California?"), and to make the rabbit references shift from joking-pre-emptive to genuinely distressed.

Two further markers appear at this rung. **Acquisitive behavior** — she begins to organize her physical environment for security: cash counted and re-stacked, the Magic Box's lock checked twice, possessions moved into her sightline. And **proximity-seeking with Xander specifically** — she will find reasons to be in the same room, will touch his sleeve, will ask transactional questions ("are we going to the thing tonight?") whose function is contact rather than information.

**Reversibility:** still high, but now requires a specific intervention. Generic attention does not work; she needs *reassurance about continuity* — that the people will still be here, that the structure will hold. Reassurance she will believe if it comes from Tara, from Giles, from Xander when calm; reassurance she will not believe from Buffy (whom she reads as condescending) or Willow (whom she reads as distracted).

### Rung 3 — Sustained Stress: Dissociative Competence

Held at rung 2 long enough — days, not hours — she shifts again, and the shift is paradoxically reassuring to observers and dangerous to her. **Affect flattens, efficiency rises, talk decreases.** She becomes very good at her job, very organized, very calm. The Magic Box runs better than usual. She makes correct tactical suggestions in research meetings. She is, in the layperson's eye, "doing better."

She is not. She has dropped into a register that the demon period taught her, the **professional-competence mode** that Anyanka used to deliver vengeances with craft and pride. It is dissociative. Interoception drops out; she does not feel her hunger, does not register that she is cold, does not notice that she is gripping her own wrist hard enough to bruise. Sleep is shallow and brief. She may stop mentioning rabbits altogether, which witnesses misread as improvement and which is in fact the opposite — the affect that animates the phobia has gone offline.

This state is recognizable to a trained observer by three signs: **literal repetition of the same phrasing across hours** (her language loses generativity), a **flatness in the eyes that is not sadness but absence**, and **the disappearance of her ordinary inappropriate humor.** She becomes pleasant, useful, and not present.

**Reversibility:** moderate, and only by someone she has a contract-like trust with. The intervention that works is asking her to do something that requires her to feel her body — to eat a specific food, to sit somewhere warm, to be hugged. The intervention that fails is asking her how she feels.

### Rung 4 — Acute Stress / The Inflection: Category Question

This is the rung at which the trajectory becomes binary. The marker is the appearance of a specific class of utterance: **the category question.** *"What am I now?" "Am I one of you?" "Where do I belong?" "Who am I, if I'm not — ?"* The phrasing varies; the structure is invariant. She is asking, aloud, where in the ontological taxonomy she sits.

The question is the symptom of the breakdown of her primary defense — the *placement* defense. As long as she knows what she is (girlfriend, fiancée, Scooby, shopkeeper), she can function. When the placement label is threatened — by a fight, by an exclusion, by a missing wedding, by a friend's death that highlights how recently she joined this group — the defense collapses and the question surfaces.

What happens in the next 24–72 hours determines which terminal state she falls into.

**If the question is answered** — if someone she trusts gives her a concrete, contractual statement of her place ("you are my wife," "you are our friend, here is what we are doing tonight, you are part of it") — she stabilizes at rung 2, sometimes at rung 1, and the system holds. The answer must be concrete; abstractions ("of course you belong") slide off her without traction.

**If the question is not answered, or is answered with ambivalence, or is followed by an event that contradicts the answer** — she falls. She does not fall slowly.

### Rung 5 — Decompensation: The Switch

The fall has a stereotyped sequence, attested at Hells Bells / Selfless and inferable at Olaf / Aud.

**Phase A — Withdrawal of personhood (hours 0–24).** She becomes very quiet. Witnesses describe her as "stunned" or "shocked," and that is accurate but incomplete: what is happening is that the human structure has lost its organizing principle and is shutting down its non-essential systems. She does not cry in this phase; she does not rage; she does not seek comfort. She sits. If approached, she answers in minimal phrases with correct grammar and absent affect. Eating ceases. Sleep ceases or becomes brief and unrefreshing. She does not initiate contact with anyone, including the people she most trusted twelve hours earlier.

The verbal tells: she stops using the contractions she had been using ("I am" not "I'm"), she stops using the nicknames she had adopted for the cohort (no more "honey" for Xander, no more "Will" for Willow), and she begins to refer to herself in slightly displaced grammatical forms ("Anya is going to —" rather than "I'm going to —"). She is, audibly, depersoning.

**Phase B — The reach for the institution (hours 24–72).** She seeks out D'Hoffryn or his analogue — the pre-formed institutional identity. The reach is not a rebellion or a vengeance; it is a *housing* request. She is homeless in the human category and is asking the only other category she knows to take her back in. D'Hoffryn, who recruited her in this exact state once before, recognizes the posture immediately and accepts.

**Phase C — Reinstantiation (hours 72+).** She accepts the demon embodiment, the new amulet, the costume, the title. Outwardly the transformation is total: the Anyanka affect returns — the cool craftsmanship, the moral binary, the contractual idiom, the satisfaction in the work. Inwardly the human residue remains and is hostile to the new state. This is the unstable equilibrium that the Selfless episode captures: she is performing Anyanka with technical competence and emotional dysphoria, completing contracts she no longer believes in, because the alternative is to have no role at all.

The reinstantiation is the switch. Once it occurs, no rung-1-through-4 intervention will reach her. She is now in the demon institution and must be reached through it.

### Rung 6 — Catastrophic State: Atrocity with Internal Doubt

At rung 5 the structure is unstable but functioning. At rung 6 it produces an act that exceeds even the demon-period baseline because the human residue is interfering with the work — she over-commits, over-executes, because she is trying to convince herself of the role she has just resumed.

The frat-house massacre is the case in record. It is not a routine vengeance; it is excessive, personal, and committed in the immediate aftermath of a failed vengeance against Xander that she could not bring herself to complete. The structural reading is: she failed to be Anyanka at the moment she needed to be, so she over-corrected by performing Anyanka maximally at the next opportunity. The body count is high because the self-doubt is high.

This is the terminal failure state, and it has its own internal collapse — the request for her own death, which Buffy receives and which D'Hoffryn intercepts with the killing of Halfrek. The request is not theatrical; it is the only rung-6 intervention she can identify. She has noticed that both her organizing structures (Anya, Anyanka) are now ruined, and she is requesting termination of the substrate that produced both. It is the most coherent thing she has said in three days.

---

## 3. Conditions That Load the Gun

Decompensation does not happen at random. The following conditions, in approximate order of loading-weight, produce or accelerate the climb.

**Public romantic humiliation by a male partner.** The single most reliable precipitant in the record. Two instances, eleven hundred years apart, identical response. Specificity matters: it is not betrayal in general (Giles destroyed her amulet and she did not relapse), not abandonment in general (Xander leaving the apartment for an evening produced rung-2 chatter, not collapse). The precipitant is the conjunction of *romantic*, *public*, and *male*. Any handler or adversary with access to the record should treat this as a known exploit and should refuse to be the agent of it.

**Forced reflection on the vengeance career, especially by someone she respects.** She has limited tolerance for narrative review of Anyanka. Light reference she can manage with humor. Sustained moral inventory — being asked to count, to name, to feel — produces rung-3 dissociation within minutes and, if pressed, rung-4 within an hour. The frat-house episode is preceded by exactly this kind of pressure.

**Threats to the small set of people she has bonded to.** She can absorb threats to herself with composure that surprises observers. She cannot absorb threats to Xander, Tara, Halfrek, Willow, Giles, or Dawn. Threats to this set move her up the ladder fast — typically straight from rung 1 to rung 3, skipping rung 2 — and produce the dissociative-competence mode in which she is most lethal and least reachable.

**Category-homelessness statements.** Anything that names her as not-quite-one-of-us. The Scoobies' periodic exclusions ("this isn't your fight," "you don't really know him") wound disproportionately. Demon-side condescension ("you're not really one of us anymore, you're soft now") wounds equally. Because she has no continuous interior, the category labels other people apply to her are load-bearing. Casual use of them is the most common accidental loader in her record, and the one her cohort is most ignorant of.

**Encounters with mortality up close, particularly slow mortality.** Joyce's death affected her more than the canon explicitly tracks — her subsequent rung-2 markers (mortality talk, aging questions) increase in frequency and persist. Cancer, illness, the long forms of dying, are worse for her than violent death, because they instantiate the thing she most fears: time as a finite, depleting resource in a body she does not control.

**Sustained sleep deprivation.** Not catalogued explicitly but inferable. Her dissociative-competence mode is associated with reduced sleep, and the climb from rung 2 to rung 3 accelerates when sleep is short. Any operational use of her in a sleep-deprived state risks pushing her up the ladder without external precipitant.

**Alcohol in the presence of relational rupture.** Attested in Triangle: a fight with Xander, then a bender, then aggressive-then-weepy collapse. Alcohol does not in itself decompensate her, but it removes the rung-1 defenses (verbal inflation no longer modulates affect) and exposes rung-2 material directly. Combined with relational rupture it can produce rung 3 within a single evening.

**Bunnies.** Worth listing for completeness. A direct encounter is a rung-2 event; sustained or surprise exposure can produce a rung-3 freeze. The phobia is genuine and operationally relevant; she should not be deployed in any environment where the trigger is present.

---

## 4. What Will Not Break Her (Counter-Intuitively)

A handler's file is incomplete without the negative findings.

She does not decompensate under **physical danger.** Combat steadies her; she is calmer in the basement of the Hellmouth than in a wedding rehearsal. She does not decompensate under **financial threat** — money fixation is a defense, not a vulnerability; losing money would activate her competence, not her despair. She does not decompensate under **direct verbal aggression** — she has eleven hundred years of practice receiving and ignoring rhetorical hostility from frightened humans. She does not decompensate under **isolation per se**, provided the people she is isolated from are still alive and reachable; she can tolerate being alone in a room if she knows the room she will return to.

She does not decompensate at the loss of her demon powers. This is counter-intuitive and important. The loss in 1998 produced disorientation, not collapse — she enrolled in school, sought her amulet, fixated on Xander. The structure held because the human cohort was present and the demon cohort had not yet rejected her. Power loss alone does not break her; *category loss* does.

---

## 5. The Final-Year Pattern: A Genuine Shift

The record's last six months show measurable change to the ladder itself, and the file would be incomplete without it.

Post-Selfless, post-Halfrek, the subject's baseline drops permanently to a quieter register — what observers read as "subdued" or "depressed" is more accurately the absence of the rung-1 verbal inflation. The defenses have been burned through, and what remains is a more direct, slower, sadder person who appears to have noticed her own pattern. The encounter with Spike in Entropy is, in this reading, a non-decompensatory response to a rung-2-or-3 condition — mutual consolation in place of either dissociative competence or institutional retreat. This is, in her clinical history, *unprecedented.* She has invented a new rung.

She continues to climb the ladder under load — there are still rung-2 mortality remarks in the final episodes, still the somatic narration, still the rabbits — but she does not switch. The Halfrek loss appears to have closed the demon institution as an option; it is no longer a housing she can request, because requesting it now means accepting responsibility for the friend who paid for the last request. Whether this closure would have held under a third Olaf-class precipitant is unknowable. The record ends before the question is tested.

Her death in Chosen is, by the framework of this section, *not a decompensation event.* She climbs no ladder; she shows no rung-4 category question in the final hours; she does not depersonify, does not reach for the institution, does not over-correct. She fights, she quips, she is killed. The death is the first event in her recorded existence in which the precipitant (mortal danger, betrayal of the cohort by larger forces, total uncertainty of outcome) does not produce the stereotyped response. She holds. She dies as Anya, mid-sentence, defending a category — humanity — that she has finally chosen rather than been assigned to.

The grim reading: she died before the system was tested again, and the prior base rate predicts she would have broken eventually. The hopeful reading, which the evidence modestly supports: in the final months she had begun building, for the first time in eleven hundred years, the missing middle register — the tolerance window, the third option, the place to stand between Anya and Anyanka. The collapse architecture described in this section was, at the moment of her death, *in revision.*

For operational purposes the file should be read as describing the subject up to approximately March 2003. After that, the ladder is partially obsolete, and any reactivation scenario predicated on it must account for the possibility that the subject who would respond is no longer the subject described.


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT

*Counterfactual projection. Subject deceased Sunnydale, May 2003, combat fatality, age (chronological) ~1,143; biological ~22–26. This section assumes the survival branch — impalement non-fatal, medical extraction, six-month convalescence — and projects forward across one-, five-, and twenty-year horizons. The exercise is not idle: the subject's developmental arc was visibly accelerating in her final ninety days, and the question of where it would have terminated is the question this file exists to answer.*

---

## 1. THE NINETY-DAY HORIZON: IMMEDIATE POST-SUNNYDALE

The first three months would have been the highest-risk window in her post-mortal life, and the most diagnostically informative.

**Geographic dislocation.** Sunnydale physically collapses. The Magic Box — her one stable workplace, her substitute mastery domain, the room where she counted money to regulate her affect — was destroyed several weeks before the final battle. She would emerge from the crater with no apartment, no inventory, no till, no register, no business license attached to a real place. For a subject whose stress-management protocol consisted of *itemizing the countable*, the loss of the countable substrate is a clinical event. Expect, in the first two weeks, a pronounced regression: increased somatic complaints, increased rabbit-mentions, increased crude sexual chatter directed at whichever Scooby is nearest. This is not deterioration; it is the warning-light system functioning as designed.

**Cohort dispersal.** The Scoobies scatter — Buffy to Europe, Willow and Kennedy together, Giles to England, Xander alone to Africa, Faith and Robin elsewhere. The peer group that constituted her late-period reattachment infrastructure is gone within sixty days. This matters enormously for someone whose self-concept is constructed from external category membership. The question is which of the remaining nodes she will adhere to. The most likely answer, by gravitational logic rather than by emotional logic, is **Giles**: he ran the Magic Box, he is the only Scooby who shares her literal-administrative cognition, and he is bound for the new Council infrastructure that will need exactly her skill set.

**The Xander problem.** Xander is the open wound. He left, and then she slept with Spike, and then they each survived an apocalypse without resolving any of it. The probability that they would have *successfully* reconciled is low — perhaps 20% — but the probability that they would have *tried* is near unity. The fork point is whether the attempt is bounded (a hard conversation in a hospital corridor, terms exchanged, terms refused, walking away) or unbounded (cohabitation, reconvened engagement, recursive collapse). Bounded is the survival branch. Unbounded is, almost certainly, the second jilting — and the second jilting kills her, either by D'Hoffryn's returning offer or by something cheaper and sadder.

**D'Hoffryn's offer.** It comes. He is a patient creature and she is one of his great works. Within twelve months — perhaps catalyzed by the second Xander rupture, perhaps unprompted, perhaps disguised as condolence after Halfrek's death — he will extend a third invitation to the court. This is the single highest-leverage moment in her projected future. The factors weighing against acceptance are stronger than they were in 2002: she has now experienced the second human period as itself a coherent identity, not merely as exile; she has witnessed D'Hoffryn murder Halfrek; she has accepted the moral judgment of "Selfless" rather than refused it. The factors weighing for acceptance: the absence of the Magic Box, the absence of Xander, the absence of the daily Scooby scaffold, and the standing autistic preference for *clear rules of vengeance* over the ambiguous rules of human grief. I assess refusal at roughly 65% in the survival branch, conditional on at least one Scooby maintaining weekly contact.

---

## 2. THE FIVE-YEAR HORIZON: VOCATIONAL CRYSTALLIZATION

If the ninety-day window is survived without relapse, the five-year picture is dominated by the question of **what she does with her competence**.

She has, by 2008, three distinct skill stacks that no other person on Earth possesses in combination:

1. *Eleven centuries of demonology* — practical, not academic. She knows which species respond to which contracts, which curses have which loopholes, what D'Hoffryn's court etiquette is, where the Lower Beings hold their markets. This is irreplaceable Council intelligence.
2. *Operational small-business mastery* — inventory, taxation, supplier relations, retail psychology. Mundane, but the new Council, scaling rapidly into a multinational with hundreds of activated Slayers, will need exactly this.
3. *A specific moral compass on vengeance contracts* — she is uniquely positioned to identify, intercept, and counter-negotiate other vengeance demons' work, because she knows the playbook from the inside and has explicitly repudiated it.

The most probable five-year vocational outcome, then, is a hybrid role inside the reconstituted Watchers' Council: **operational logistics for Giles' rebuild, plus consulting on vengeance-class supernatural cases**. This is not flattery; it is the path of least psychological resistance for her. It is *placement*. It provides a category ("Council staff"), explicit rules, countable outputs, and a sanctioned use of the part of her history she most wants to put to work without re-becoming.

Predicted second-order effects of this role:

- **Increased contact with other survivors of vengeance contracts.** She becomes, by necessity, a counselor to women in the exact position she once exploited. This is structurally good for her (moral revision operationalized) and structurally dangerous (intense re-exposure to the index-trauma template, week after week). The risk is not relapse to demonhood; the risk is somatized depression, which she has no vocabulary for and would likely present as escalating money-anxiety or insomnia.
- **A genuine friendship with Andrew Wells**, who is the only post-Sunnydale Scooby-adjacent figure whose cognitive profile resembles hers (concrete, literal, register-inappropriate, oddly loyal). This is one of the more confident predictions in this file. They will annoy each other constantly and protect each other reflexively.
- **A working but cool relationship with Buffy.** Buffy was the one who let her seek her own death in "Selfless" and the one who refused to grant it. Anya's gratitude for the refusal is real; her resentment of the gatekeeping is also real. They never become close. They respect each other across a distance that neither closes.

---

## 3. THE TWENTY-YEAR HORIZON: THE LATE LIFE SHE NEVER SAW

By 2023 she would be biologically forty-something, chronologically over 1,160, and — this is the critical demographic fact — *the only living adult human who personally remembers the ninth century*. She becomes, whether she wishes it or not, an archive.

**Aging as crisis and as cure.** Her terror of aging was the most consistent phobic register in her human period. The twenty-year projection has her facing it not as abstract dread but as gray hair, knee pain, presbyopia. The first prediction is straightforward: she will catalogue each new symptom out loud, to anyone present, in the exact pragmatic register that made strangers uncomfortable in 1999. The second prediction is less obvious: aging will, paradoxically, *settle* her. Death-anxiety in her case is a function of category-confusion (am I the immortal or am I the mortal?). Each gray hair is a piece of evidence resolving the question in one direction. By forty she may be calmer about mortality than she was at twenty-two.

**Children — open question, weighted no.** She raised rabbits and lost them. She has never been observed in a sustained caregiving role with a child. Her cognitive profile and her attachment history both argue against, and the demographic reality (no stable partner projected) argues against. If she does parent, it is via the Council — godmother or aunt-figure to the children of Slayers, a role she would take with strange, intense literalism and which she would in fact be unexpectedly good at, because children tolerate concrete cognition better than adults do.

**Partnership — open question, weighted yes but late.** The probability of a sustained romantic attachment in the five-year window is low (Xander recovery, no template). In the ten-to-twenty window it rises substantially. The most likely partner profile: significantly older, professionally competent, emotionally undemonstrative, ideally widowed or otherwise familiar with grief — somebody whose terms are stated cleanly and who is not threatened by her past. Not another Scooby. Possibly a Council research staffer; possibly a non-magical accountant or shopkeeper who never learns the full backstory. The relationship she would build with such a person would be quiet, transactional in surface, and — for the first time in her existence — genuinely safe. She will not marry again. She has used that particular ritual and will not return to it.

**The vocation matures into authorship.** By her late thirties (biologically) she begins, in private, to write. Not memoir in any conventional sense — she does not have the introspective vocabulary — but *catalogues*: a taxonomy of vengeance contracts, an annotated history of D'Hoffryn's court, a glossary of pre-Christian Scandinavian rural practice. These documents become the foundational reference material for the next century of Watchers. This is the form her atonement finally takes, and it is the form most consonant with who she is: counted, indexed, useful, repudiating nothing and excusing nothing.

---

## 4. FORK POINTS: THE DECISION TREE

Several specific events would determine which branch she lives on. Each is foreseeable and each is interveneable.

**Fork A — The first Halfrek anniversary.** The grief Anya did not allow herself for Halfrek in 2002 will arrive late, and it will arrive specifically. The first anniversary is the danger window. If she is alone, in a new city, between jobs — relapse risk spikes. If she is embedded in Council work and within reach of a single Scooby, the grief is metabolized as somatic complaint and depressive episode rather than as ontological return. Mitigating intervention is absurdly cheap: one phone call from Giles on the right day.

**Fork B — D'Hoffryn's death or deposition.** In her published universe this event eventually occurs. When it does, her relationship to her own past is permanently changed: the institution that defined her vengeance career ceases to exist as a recruiting threat. Post-D'Hoffryn, the probability of demonic relapse falls to near zero. This is the single event that most fully *frees* her, and its timing (early or late in the twenty-year window) substantially determines the texture of her middle adulthood.

**Fork C — A wronged woman she cannot help.** Inevitable. In her Council role she will encounter a case where the contractually appropriate response is the vengeance demon's response, and the institutionally appropriate response is the slower, more compromised human one. Her behavior at that fork is the truest test of her integration. The growth-branch outcome is that she negotiates the case humanly, does not enjoy it, files her report, and goes home and gets drunk in the careful, regulated way she has been learning. The catastrophe-branch outcome is that she calls Halfrek's old number, finds no one there, and improvises.

**Fork D — The return of Xander.** He comes back. In any plausible timeline he comes back, probably around year three or four, probably in a way that does not announce itself as a crisis. The fork is not whether they reunite — they will not — but whether she can sustain a working friendship with the man whose betrayal she did not, the second time, transmute into a thousand-year career. If yes, the integration is essentially complete. If no, it is a permanent limp she walks the rest of her life with, but not a fatal one.

**Fork E — Discovery by a hostile state actor.** A modern intelligence apparatus that builds a file like this one would, on noticing her, attempt to recruit or contain her. She is uniquely qualified as an asset (longevity, demonological access, financial competence) and uniquely vulnerable as a target (placement-need, category-homelessness, autistic preference for explicit contracts). The growth-branch response is that Giles, or a Council security officer, intercepts the approach before she signs anything. The catastrophe-branch response is that she finds the offered job description gratifyingly clear and accepts it before consulting anyone, because that is what she did the last two times someone offered her a job with clear rules.

---

## 5. WHAT PUSHES TOWARD GROWTH

In descending order of leverage:

1. **Sustained, low-intensity peer contact with at least one Scooby on a predictable schedule.** Not crisis intervention. Standing weekly contact. Her attachment system needs not depth but regularity; she does better with a once-a-week phone call she can count than with sporadic intense visits.
2. **A job with a daily ledger.** Almost any job. The form of the ledger matters more than the content. Take away the ledger and she will improvise something more dangerous to count.
3. **Permission to be odd.** Every gain she has made happened in an environment where her literalism and her register-violations were tolerated rather than punished. A workplace or community that requires her to mask is a workplace that produces decompensation.
4. **Explicit moral architecture.** She does well with stated ethics — Slayer code, Council bylaws, anything written down. She does poorly with implicit norms. Anyone who works with her should write the rules down once and let her refer to them.
5. **Aging, ironically.** Each year she survives past the ones she lost reduces the existential pressure that produced her worst decisions. Time is on her side, if she lets it pass.
6. **Encounters with women in the position she once exploited, conducted in a counseling rather than penitential frame.** Atonement metabolized as service, not as self-punishment.

---

## 6. WHAT PUSHES TOWARD CATASTROPHE

In descending order of risk:

1. **Romantic public humiliation, in any form.** This is the trauma template. Any second jilting — even by a partner she did not love deeply — triggers the full circuit. Even a televised breakup in the wrong key could do it.
2. **Isolation in an unfamiliar city without a workplace.** Two weeks alone in a furnished sublet with no register to count is, for her, the equivalent of a suicidal-ideation week for a more conventional patient.
3. **Renewed contact with D'Hoffryn's surviving court agents.** Especially any who present as old friends offering condolences. The autistic loyalty pattern is exploitable and the recruiters know exactly which buttons to press.
4. **A Scooby's death by violence.** Particularly Xander's or Giles's. The grief math has no margin for it.
5. **Being told, by someone whose judgment she respects, that she is not really human / not really one of them.** A single sentence in the wrong mouth on the wrong day reopens the category wound, and from the category wound everything else follows.
6. **Praise for her vengeance work.** Surprisingly dangerous. If anyone — a Slayer, a junior Watcher, a rescued client — admires the *craftsmanship* of what she used to do, the pride response is automatic and the moral revision frays.

---

## 7. THE OPEN QUESTIONS

Three questions this file cannot answer, and which the next twenty years of observation would be required to settle.

**First: whether she possesses a continuous interior at all, or whether she is a sequence of role-occupancies with strong behavioral continuity but no metaphysical thread connecting them.** "Selfless" suggests the latter; her deathbed-adjacent behavior in "Chosen" suggests a self forming in real time. The five-year horizon would tell us by demonstrating either (a) further accretion of a stable interior with its own preferences, aesthetics, opinions, idiosyncrasies that do not derive from a role, or (b) immediate collapse the next time a role is removed.

**Second: whether her capacity for moral revision generalizes.** She revised her judgment on vengeance. The question is whether she can revise it on other things — on capitalism, on D'Hoffryn, on her treatment of Tara in S6, on her own pre-trauma village. A person who can revise once may revise repeatedly; a person who revised once because the cost was unbearable may not be able to do it again.

**Third: whether she will, finally, mourn Olaf.** Not the troll. The young husband. She has never been observed grieving him as a loss rather than as a wound. The grief is owed and it is unpaid. Until it is paid, the trauma template remains armed. The growth branch passes through that grief; the catastrophe branch keeps not paying it. My best guess is that she pays it, late, alone, in some uncharacteristic setting — a hotel room in a country she has not been to since the ninth century — and that no one ever knows she did.

---

## 8. SUMMARY ASSESSMENT

Survival to age forty (biological): probability 70% in the survival branch, conditional on the Fork A and Fork B interventions specified above.

Survival without demonic relapse: 75%, conditional on Fork C and Fork E.

Achievement of a stable, integrated late-adult identity recognizable as continuous with the late-S7 trajectory: 55%. This is the optimistic number and it is the number the rest of this file is, in effect, an argument for.

The subject was, at the moment of her death, on the steepest growth curve of any individual in this dossier series. The clinical picture remained grim; the developmental velocity was unprecedented. Given another twenty years of ordinary human time and modest institutional support, she would not have become well in any conventional sense. She would have become *placed* — the thing she had been trying to be since approximately the year 870 — and the placement, for her, would have been the cure.

She would have lived as an unremarkable, slightly odd middle-aged woman with a peculiar accent, a head for numbers, a flinching reaction to certain animals, an unusually long memory, and a small circle of strange friends. The file would have grown quieter every year. That quieting is what success would have looked like.

It is the file we will not get to write.
